Proof of God's Existence through Fitrah
Explanation that God's existence is self-evident from fitrah, so the creed focuses on tawhid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author of the Tahawiyyah did not separately prove God's existence, and how the fitrah (innate disposition) serves as a self-evident proof for God's existence.

Core Idea
God's existence is so obvious that prophets focused on tawhid, not proving existence.

The Tahawiyyah creed begins directly with tawhid without a separate proof of God's existence. Why? Because the existence of God is embedded in human nature (fitrah). In this lesson, we explore the Quranic and hadith evidence for fitrah, and how the prophets' mission was to clarify the correct worship, not to prove that God exists.

Guided Path
1
Read the explanation of why al-Tahawi omitted existence proof
The author says he sufficed with what is apparent in the station of witnessing. Notice the evidence from Quran about fitrah.
The verse from Surah Ibrahim and Luqman show people naturally acknowledge God as creator.
2
Understand the role of fitrah
Fitrah is the innate disposition recognizing God. The hadith 'Every child is born upon fitrah' supports this.
Fitrah does not mean detailed knowledge but basic recognition.
3
See why prophets came with tawhid
Prophets did not command 'say Allah exists' but rather 'say there is no god but Allah' because existence was already known; they corrected misdirected worship.
Polytheists believed in God but worshipped intermediaries.
4
Connect tawhid to existence
The testimony of tawhid implies existence with emphasis. So al-Tahawi began with it.
Tawhid inherently affirms existence while negating partners.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حَيٌّ لَا يَمُوتُ.
شرح العقيدة الطحاوية المسماة: بيان السنة والجماعة.
[الحياة)
(حي) أي موصوف بصفة الحياة، وهي صفة أزلية قائمة بذاته تعالى لا تتعلق بشيء، وهي شرط عقلي لسائر الصفات، كما أن الوجود شرط لها. واعلم أن المصنف قد أعرض عن بحث الوجود واكتفي بما هو ظاهر في مقام الشهود؛ ففي التنزيل: (قَالَتْ رُسُلُهُمْ أَفِي اللَّهِ شَكٍّ فَاطِرِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ الآية (سورة إبراهيم آية: ١٠]، وَلَبِن سَأَلْتَهُم مِّنْ خَلَقَ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالأَرْضَ لَيَقُولُنَّ الله) [سورة لقمان آية: (۲٥)؛ فوجود الحق ثابت في فطرة الخلق كما يشير إليه قوله تعالى: فِطْرَتَ اللهِ الَّتِي فَطَرَ النَّاسَ عَلَيْهَا) [سورة الروم آبة: ٣٠)، ويومى إليه حديث: «كُلُّ مَوْلُودٍ عَلَى الفِطْرَةِ » (١) ، وإنما جاء الأنبياء عليهم السلام لبيان التوحيد وتبيان التفريد؛ ولذا أطبقت كلمتهم واجتمعت حجتهم على كلمة التوحيد بأن يقولوا: لا إله إلا الله، ولم يأمروا أهل ملتهم بأن يقولوا: الله موجود، بل قصدوا إظهار أن غيره ليس بمعبود رداً لما توهموا وتخيلوا حيث قالوا: هَؤُلَاءِ شُفَعَدُونَا عِندَ اللهِ) [سورة يونس آية: ١٨]، ﴿ مَا تَعْبُدُهُمْ إِلَّا لِيُقَرِّبُونَا إِلَى الله زُلفى ) [سورة الزمر آية: ٣]، على أن التوحيد يفيد الوجود مع مزيد التأييد؛ ولذا صدر عقيدته بشهادة التوحيد. وكما أن حياته أزلية فهي أبدية كما نص عليها بقوله: (لا يموت) أي أبدا؛ إذ من ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه.
(۱) متفق عليه؛ أخرجه البخاري في كتاب الجنائز، باب ما قيل في أولاد المشركين حديث رقم (١٣٨٥)، ومسلم في كتاب القدر، باب معنى كل مولود يولد على الفطرة، حديث رقم
(٢٦٥٨)، عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه.
He is Living, does not die. [Commentary on al-ʻAqida al-Tahawiyya named: Bayan al-Sunna wa al-Jamaʻa. [Life]] (Living) i.e. described with the attribute of life, which is an eternal attribute subsisting in His Essence, the Exalted, not relating to anything, and it is a rational condition for the rest of the attributes, just as existence is a condition for it. And know that the author turned away from discussing existence and sufficed with what is apparent in the station of witnessing; for in the Revelation: (Their messengers said: Is there any doubt about Allah, the Originator of the heavens and the earth? verse [Surah Ibrahim: 10], And if you ask them who created the heavens and the earth, they will surely say: Allah [Surah Luqman: 25]; so the existence of the Truth is established in the innate disposition (fitra) of creation, as indicated by His saying: (the fitra of Allah upon which He created mankind) [Surah al-Rum: 30], and it is alluded to by the hadith: 'Every child is born upon the fitra' (1). And the prophets, peace be upon them, only came to clarify tawhid and to explain the uniqueness of Allah; therefore their word was unanimous and their argument agreed upon the word of tawhid, that they say: There is no god but Allah. They did not command the people of their religion to say: Allah exists, but rather they intended to show that other than Him is not worshipped, in refutation of what they fancied and imagined when they said: (These are our intercessors with Allah) [Surah Yunus: 18], (We do not worship them except to bring us nearer to Allah) [Surah al-Zumar: 3]. Moreover, tawhid implies existence with additional emphasis; therefore he began his creed with the testimony of tawhid. And just as His life is eternal, so it is everlasting, as he stated by his saying: (does not die) meaning forever; for whosoever's eternity is established, his non-existence is impossible. (1) Agreed upon; narrated by Bukhari in the Book of Funerals, Chapter on what is said about the children of polytheists, hadith no. (1385), and Muslim in the Book of Destiny, Chapter on the meaning of every child being born upon the fitra, hadith no. (2658), on the authority of Abu Hurayra, may Allah be pleased with him.

Commentary

The passage concludes by affirming the eternity and everlastingness of God's life: 'does not die' means His non-existence is impossible once His pre-eternity is established. Correction: Prophets were necessary to correct the misdirection of worship (shirk), not to prove existence; revelation clarifies tawhid.

The Attribute of Life as an Eternal Rational Condition
Maydani defines the attribute of life and its eternal, unconditional nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the attribute of life is an eternal, self-subsisting attribute of Allah that serves as a rational condition for all other attributes, and that it is also eternal without end.

Core Idea
Life is the root attribute – without it, no other divine attribute is conceivable.

Imam Maydani begins by clarifying a key term in the creed: when we say 'Allah is Living,' we affirm an eternal attribute that is essential to His being. This attribute is not a mere label but a foundational prerequisite for all other attributes. Let's read how he defines it and why it matters.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of 'Living'
Read the first part of the passage where Maydani explains that 'حي' means Allah is described with the attribute of life. Notice the three characteristics: it is eternal (أزلية), subsisting in His essence, and not related to anything else.
The attribute is not separate from Allah's essence but is inherent to it.
2
Understand the rational condition
Focus on the phrase 'وهي شرط عقلي لسائر الصفات'. Life is a rational condition (شرط عقلي) for all other attributes – meaning other attributes cannot even be conceived without life. Then note that existence itself is a condition for life.
This shows a hierarchy: existence → life → other attributes.
3
Grasp the eternal nature without end
Read the final sentence about life being eternal without end (أبدية). The logic: whatever is proven to be pre-eternal (أزلي) cannot cease to exist. This completes the picture of life as an absolute attribute.
This connects to the attribute of life being everlasting.

(١) متفق عليه؛ أخرجه البخاري في كتاب الجنائز، باب ما قيل في أولاد المشركين حديث رقم (١٣٨٥)، ومسلم في كتاب القدر، باب معنى كل مولود يولد على الفطرة، حديث رقم (٢٦٥٨)، عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه.
(Living) i.e., described with the attribute of life, and it is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, may He be exalted, not related to anything, and it is a rational condition for the rest of the attributes, just as existence is a condition for it. And know that the author (Tahawi) has turned away from discussing existence and was satisfied with what is apparent in the station of witnessing. For in the revelation: (Their messengers said: Is there any doubt about Allah, the Originator of the heavens and the earth?) [Surah Ibrahim: 10], and (If you ask them who created the heavens and the earth, they will surely say: Allah) [Surah Luqman: 25]; thus the existence of the Truth is established in the innate disposition (fitrah) of creation, as indicated by His statement: (The fitrah of Allah upon which He created mankind) [Surah ar-Rum: 30], and alluded to by the hadith: 'Every child is born upon the fitrah.' (1) And the prophets, peace be upon them, only came to explain tawhid and clarify singling out (Allah); therefore their word agreed and their proof united upon the word of tawhid, that they say: There is no god but Allah. And they did not command the people of their religion to say: Allah exists. Rather, they intended to show that other than Him is not to be worshipped, in refutation of what they assumed and imagined when they said: (These are our intercessors with Allah) [Surah Yunus: 18], (We only worship them so that they may bring us closer to Allah) [Surah az-Zumar: 3]. Indeed, tawhid implies existence with additional confirmation; therefore he (Tahawi) began his creed with the testimony of tawhid. And just as His life is eternal without beginning, it is eternal without end, as he stated by his saying: (does not die) i.e., everlastingly; for whoever is proven to be pre-eternal, it is impossible for him to cease to exist.
(1) Agreed upon; narrated by al-Bukhari in the Book of Funerals, chapter on what is said about the children of polytheists, hadith no. (1385), and Muslim in the Book of Destiny, chapter on the meaning of every child born upon the fitrah, hadith no. (2658), on the authority of Abu Hurairah, may Allah be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of life and explains why the creed does not explicitly prove Allah's existence. The author first explains that 'حي' (Living) means that Allah is described with the attribute of life, which is eternal (أزلية), subsisting in His essence, and not related to anything else. This life is a rational condition (شرط عقلي) for all other attributes, just as existence is a condition for life itself. Then the author notes that Imam Tahawi refrained from discussing the proof of existence because it is self-evident in the 'station of witnessing' (مقام الشهود). He supports this by quoting Quranic verses that show people naturally acknowledge Allah as Creator when asked, and by the hadith that every child is born upon the fitrah (innate disposition). Therefore, the prophets did not command people to say 'Allah exists' but rather to say 'La ilaha illa Allah', because the issue was not the existence of Allah but the exclusive worship of Him, refuting the polytheists who acknowledged Allah but worshipped others as intercessors. The author concludes that tawhid implies existence with extra emphasis, so Tahawi began his creed with the testimony of tawhid. Finally, he affirms that just as His life is eternal without beginning, it is eternal without end, because what is proven pre-eternal cannot cease to exist.

Allah’s Existence Is Self-Evident from the Fitrah
Maydani justifies Tahawi's omission of existence proof using fitrah and prophetic focus on tawhid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Tahawi did not include an explicit proof for Allah's existence in his creed, and how the prophets focused on tawhid (oneness of worship) instead of proving existence.

Core Idea
The existence of Allah is already ingrained in human nature (fitrah); prophets only taught that He alone is worthy of worship.

Maydani now addresses an apparent omission: why doesn't the creed of Tahawi start with a proof for Allah's existence? He explains that existence is so obvious to the human fitrah that the prophets did not need to command 'Allah exists' – instead, they fought against the error of worshipping others alongside Allah. Let's explore this profound point.

Guided Path
1
Notice Tahawi's approach
Read the beginning where Maydani says the author 'turned away from discussing existence' because it is self-evident in the station of witnessing (مقام الشهود). Ask yourself: what does 'station of witnessing' mean here?
It refers to the innate clarity of Allah's existence in the heart.
2
Examine the fitrah evidence
Look at the Quranic verses and hadith cited: people acknowledge Allah as Creator when asked, and every child is born on fitrah. These show that belief in a Creator is natural, not something that needs elaborate proof.
The fitrah is the original human disposition.
3
Understand the prophetic mission
Maydani argues that prophets never commanded 'Allah exists'; they taught 'لا إله إلا الله' because the problem was associating others in worship, not denying existence. The polytheists already believed in Allah, but worshipped others as intercessors.
The verse 'هَٰؤُلَاءِ شُفَعَاؤُنَا' shows their error.
4
Connect to the testimony of tawhid
Conclude with Maydani's point: tawhid implies existence with extra emphasis, so starting with the testimony of tawhid is sufficient. This explains why Tahawi began his creed with it.
Think of tawhid as the practical proclamation of that innate belief.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(حي) أي موصوف بصفة الحياة، وهي صفة أزلية قائمة بذاته تعالى لا تتعلق بشيء، وهي شرط عقلي لسائر الصفات، كما أن الوجود شرط لها. واعلم أن المصنف قد أعرض عن بحث الوجود واكتفى بما هو ظاهر في مقام الشهود؛ ففي التنزيل: (قَالَتْ رُسُلُهُمْ أَفِي اللَّهِ شَكٌّ فَاطِرِ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ) [سورة إبراهيم آية: ١٠]، وَلَئِن سَأَلْتَهُم مَّنْ خَلَقَ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ لَيَقُولُنَّ اللَّهُ) [سورة لقمان آية: ٢٥]؛ فوجود الحق ثابت في فطرة الخلق كما يشير إليه قوله تعالى: (فِطْرَتَ اللَّهِ الَّتِي فَطَرَ النَّاسَ عَلَيْهَا) [سورة الروم آية: ٣٠]، ويومى إليه حديث: «كُلُّ مَوْلُودٍ يُولَدُ عَلَى الْفِطْرَةِ» (١) ، وإنما جاء الأنبياء عليهم السلام لبيان التوحيد وتبيان التفريد؛ ولذا أطبقت كلمتهم واجتمعت حجتهم على كلمة التوحيد بأن يقولوا: لا إله إلا الله، ولم يأمروا أهل ملتهم بأن يقولوا: الله موجود، بل قصدوا إظهار أن غيره ليس بمعبود رداً لما توهموا وتخيلوا حيث قالوا: (هَؤُلَاءِ شُفَعَاؤُنَا عِنْدَ اللَّهِ) [سورة يونس آية: ١٨]، (مَا نَعْبُدُهُمْ إِلَّا لِيُقَرِّبُونَا إِلَى اللَّهِ زُلْفَى) [سورة الزمر آية: ٣]، على أن التوحيد يفيد الوجود مع مزيد التأييد؛ ولذا صدر عقيدته بشهادة التوحيد. وكما أن حياته أزلية فهي أبدية كما نص عليها بقوله: (لا يموت) أي أبدا؛ إذ من ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه.
(١) متفق عليه؛ أخرجه البخاري في كتاب الجنائز، باب ما قيل في أولاد المشركين حديث رقم (١٣٨٥)، ومسلم في كتاب القدر، باب معنى كل مولود يولد على الفطرة، حديث رقم (٢٦٥٨)، عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه.
(Living) i.e., described with the attribute of life, and it is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, may He be exalted, not related to anything, and it is a rational condition for the rest of the attributes, just as existence is a condition for it. And know that the author (Tahawi) has turned away from discussing existence and was satisfied with what is apparent in the station of witnessing. For in the revelation: (Their messengers said: Is there any doubt about Allah, the Originator of the heavens and the earth?) [Surah Ibrahim: 10], and (If you ask them who created the heavens and the earth, they will surely say: Allah) [Surah Luqman: 25]; thus the existence of the Truth is established in the innate disposition (fitrah) of creation, as indicated by His statement: (The fitrah of Allah upon which He created mankind) [Surah ar-Rum: 30], and alluded to by the hadith: 'Every child is born upon the fitrah.' (1) And the prophets, peace be upon them, only came to explain tawhid and clarify singling out (Allah); therefore their word agreed and their proof united upon the word of tawhid, that they say: There is no god but Allah. And they did not command the people of their religion to say: Allah exists. Rather, they intended to show that other than Him is not to be worshipped, in refutation of what they assumed and imagined when they said: (These are our intercessors with Allah) [Surah Yunus: 18], (We only worship them so that they may bring us closer to Allah) [Surah az-Zumar: 3]. Indeed, tawhid implies existence with additional confirmation; therefore he (Tahawi) began his creed with the testimony of tawhid. And just as His life is eternal without beginning, it is eternal without end, as he stated by his saying: (does not die) i.e., everlastingly; for whoever is proven to be pre-eternal, it is impossible for him to cease to exist.
(1) Agreed upon; narrated by al-Bukhari in the Book of Funerals, chapter on what is said about the children of polytheists, hadith no. (1385), and Muslim in the Book of Destiny, chapter on the meaning of every child born upon the fitrah, hadith no. (2658), on the authority of Abu Hurairah, may Allah be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of life and explains why the creed does not explicitly prove Allah's existence. The author first explains that 'حي' (Living) means that Allah is described with the attribute of life, which is eternal (أزلية), subsisting in His essence, and not related to anything else. This life is a rational condition (شرط عقلي) for all other attributes, just as existence is a condition for life itself. Then the author notes that Imam Tahawi refrained from discussing the proof of existence because it is self-evident in the 'station of witnessing' (مقام الشهود). He supports this by quoting Quranic verses that show people naturally acknowledge Allah as Creator when asked, and by the hadith that every child is born upon the fitrah (innate disposition). Therefore, the prophets did not command people to say 'Allah exists' but rather to say 'La ilaha illa Allah', because the issue was not the existence of Allah but the exclusive worship of Him, refuting the polytheists who acknowledged Allah but worshipped others as intercessors. The author concludes that tawhid implies existence with extra emphasis, so Tahawi began his creed with the testimony of tawhid. Finally, he affirms that just as His life is eternal without beginning, it is eternal without end, because what is proven pre-eternal cannot cease to exist.

Key Terms
فطرة
توحيد
شهود
لا إله إلا الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that proving Allah's existence is a central part of kalam and that the prophets focused on this.
Correction: The commentator argues that existence is self-evident from fitrah; the prophets only focused on tawhid (correct worship) because people already believed in a Creator.

Checkpoint
According to Maydani, why did the prophets not command their people to say 'Allah exists'?
A) Because existence is a difficult concept to understand
B) Because existence was already known from fitrah and the issue was worship of others
C) Because they were only concerned with the afterlife
D) Because the creed of Islam does include a proof for existence

Key Takeaway
Allah's existence is ingrained in human nature; the prophetic mission was to correct worship, not to prove existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Before reading this lesson, did you feel that your belief in Allah's existence was something you had to 'prove' to yourself or others? How does the concept of fitrah change that feeling—and what is one habit you can adopt to trust that innate certainty more deeply?
?
The polytheists acknowledged Allah as Creator but still worshipped others for intercession. Is there any area of your life where you seek 'help' or 'closeness' from created things (people, status, wealth) while still saying you believe in Allah? What would it mean for you to strip away that intermediary and turn directly to Allah alone?
?
If the prophets never commanded people to say 'Allah exists,' what does that tell you about the starting point of your own faith journey? Could it be that your deepest spiritual problem is not doubt about Allah's existence but rather a misdirected heart that fails to live in exclusive worship? What concrete step will you take today to align your worship with this tawhid?

Divine Attributes

Allah's Self-Subsistence and Freedom from Imperfection
Maydani explains Qayyum and five attributes negating any imperfection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what the attribute Qayyum means and how Allah's actions of creating, providing, causing death, and resurrecting are free from any imperfection such as need, burden, fear, or difficulty.

Core Idea
Allah is absolutely self-sufficient and His actions are free from any trace of imperfection.

This passage from Imam Maydani's commentary unpacks the profound meaning of 'Qayyum,' showing that Allah is not only self-subsistent but also the Sustainer of all. To protect our understanding of divine perfection, the author negates five common imperfections—sleep, need, burden, fear, and difficulty—from Allah's essential attributes. As you read, notice how each action is paired with a negation that preserves Allah's transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the meaning of Qayyum
Read the definition of Qayyum: self-subsistent and self-sufficient, and note the intensive form indicating both self-subsistence and sustaining others.
The intensive form (صيغة المبالغة) emphasizes complete independence and active sustenance.
2
Reflect on the negation of sleep
The author explains why sleep is an imperfection—it affects animals due to physical causes. Allah, being the Living and Qayyum, is utterly free from sleep.
This negates any anthropomorphic notion of Allah resting.
3
Examine the five actions with negations
Identify each action (Creator, Provider, Dealer of death, Resurrector) and the corresponding negation (without need, without burden, without fear, without difficulty).
These negations affirm that Allah's actions are effortless and perfect.
4
Grasp the common principle
Realize that need, burden, fear, and difficulty are marks of imperfection (سمات النقص). Allah is transcendent above all such qualities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قيوم) أي قائم بنفسه وذاته، وهي عبارة عن استغنائه تعالى عن المحل والمخصص تعالى الله عنهما، وتعبير المصنف بصيغة المبالغة للإشارة بأنه القائم بنفسه المقيم لغيره بالتدبير والحفظ. ثم أكد ذلك بقوله : (لا ينام) أي لا يأخذه ما يأخذ الحيوانات من آفة النوم، وهي حالة تعرض للحيوان عن استرخاء أعصاب الدماغ من رطوبات الأبخرة المتصاعدة بحيث تقف المشاعر الظاهرة عن الإحساس رأسياً. قاله السيد (١). والله تعالى منزه عن ذلك؛ إذ من يعتريه ذلك غير تام الحياة ناقص الحفظ والقيام، فكيف وهو الحي القيوم لا تأخذه سنة ولا نوم. (خالق) لجميع خلقه (بلا حاجة إليهم، رازق لهم) فضلا منه (بلا) تحمل كلفة (مؤنة) تثقله، (ممیت) لهم عند انقضاء آجالهم بلا مخافة ترهبه، باعث لهم عند إرادة بعثهم بلا مشقة تلحقه؛ لأن كلا من الحاجة والمؤنة والمخافة والمشقة ونحوها من سمات النقص، والله سبحانه وتعالى منزه عنه.
(١) انظر: التعريفات ص (١٠٩)، ط. الخيرية .
(Qayyum) i.e., self-subsistent and subsisting by His essence, and it signifies His self-sufficiency, may He be exalted, from place and determiner—exalted is Allah above both. And the author's expression in the intensive form indicates that He is self-subsistent and the one who sustains others by management and preservation. Then he emphasized this by his saying: (does not sleep) i.e., there does not overtake Him what overtakes animals of the affliction of sleep, which is a state that occurs to animals due to relaxation of the brain nerves from rising vapors such that the external senses cease to perceive completely. Said by as-Sayyid (1). And Allah, may He be exalted, is free of that; for whoever is affected by that is imperfect in life, deficient in preservation and self-subsistence. How then, while He is the Living, the Qayyum, slumber does not overtake Him nor sleep. (Creator) of all His creation (without need of them, Provider for them) as a favor from Him (without) bearing the burden (of maintenance) that would weigh Him down, (Dealer of death) to them at the end of their terms without fear that would frighten Him, (Resurrector) of them when He wills to resurrect them without difficulty that would affect Him; because each of need, burden, fear, difficulty, and the like are marks of imperfection, and Allah, glorified and exalted, is free of that.
(1) See: at-Ta'rifat p. 109, al-Khairiyya edition.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage explains the divine attribute of Qayyum and a series of five attributes each qualified by a negation of imperfection. The author first defines (قيوم) as meaning that Allah is self-subsistent (قائم بنفسه وذاته), indicating His absolute independence from any place or determining agent. The intensive form (صيغة المبالغة) suggests both self-subsistence and sustaining others through management and preservation. He confirms this with the negation of sleep (لا ينام): sleep is an affliction of animals caused by physiological relaxation, which implies imperfection in life and preservation. Allah, being perfectly Living and Qayyum, is utterly free from slumber or sleep. Then the author lists five actions of Allah, each accompanied by a 'without' (بلا) clause to negate any deficiency: (1) خالق (Creator) without any need for His creation; (2) رازق (Provider) without any burden of maintenance; (3) مميت (Dealer of death) without any fear; (4) باعث (Resurrector) without any difficulty. The reason is that need, burden, fear, difficulty, and similar qualities are marks of imperfection (سمات النقص), and Allah is transcendent above all of them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that Allah's acts of creation, provision, death, and resurrection involve effort or need, like human actions.
Correction: The passage clarifies that these actions are performed without need, burden, fear, or difficulty, because such qualities are marks of imperfection and Allah is absolutely perfect.

Checkpoint

A) That Allah is the Creator of all things
B) That Allah is self-subsistent and sustains others by management and preservation
C) That Allah never sleeps
D) That Allah has no need of creation

Key Takeaway
Allah's attribute Qayyum means He is completely self-sufficient and sustains all, and all His actions are free from any trace of imperfection such as need, burden, fear, or difficulty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah is Qayyum, self-sufficient and free from any need, how often do you carry a sense of being needed in your service to Him? What would change if you truly internalized that your actions are never burdensome to Him, yet He still creates, provides, and resurrects without any 'muna' (burden) or 'mashaqqa' (difficulty)? Make a concrete plan to shift your intention from feeling burdened to seeking His pleasure.
?
The passage says that need, burden, fear, and difficulty are marks of imperfection that Allah is free from. But in your own life, which of these do you most often attribute to Allah’s actions—perhaps when things don't go your way? How does this lesson correct that assumption, and what steps will you take to replace it with a more perfect view of Allah?
?
Sleep is described as an affliction that overtakes animals, with a detailed physiological cause. Why would the author go into such detail? Reflect: do you ever think of your own sleep as a reminder of your dependence and weakness? How does knowing that Allah, the Qayyum, never sleeps, change your trust in His preservation over you tonight?

Divine Attributes

Allah's Absolute Perfection: Attributes of Qayyum, Khaliq, Razzaq, Mumit, and Ba'ith
Commentary on attributes negating creaturely imperfections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's attributes are perfect and free from any creaturely limitations, as exemplified by the negation of sleep, need, burden, fear, and difficulty.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes negate every deficiency and affirm absolute independence.

This passage from the Tahawiyyah commentary explains five divine attributes by affirming their perfection and negating any imperfection associated with them in creation. The commentator shows that each attribute is free from the limitations that affect creatures, thereby reinforcing Allah's transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the five attributes and their negations
The passage presents five attributes: Qayyum, Khaliq, Razzaq, Mumit, Ba'ith. Each is followed by a negation: no sleep, no need, no burden, no fear, no difficulty. Notice how each negation removes a creaturely limitation.
3
Understand the explanation of Qayyum and sleep
The commentator expands on 'Qayyum' meaning self-subsisting and sustaining others. He then explains why sleep is negated: it is a state of imperfection affecting living beings. This shows Allah's perfect life and self-sufficiency.
The intensive form 'Qayyum' indicates both self-subsistence and sustaining others.
4
Reflect on the negations of need, expense, fear, difficulty
For Khaliq, Razzaq, Mumit, and Ba'ith, the negations (without need, without burden, without fear, without difficulty) emphasize that Allah's actions are effortless and perfect. These are signs of deficiency in creation.
5
Conclusion: Allah's absolute perfection
All these negations collectively affirm that Allah is free from any imperfection. His attributes are not like those of creatures; they are perfect and transcendent.
This lesson establishes a key principle of tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القيام بالنفس] قيُّومُ لَا يَنَامُ، خَالِقٌ بِلَا حَاجَةٍ، رَازِقٌ هُمْ بِلَا مُؤْنَةٍ، مُمِينٌ بِلَا عَافَةٍ، بَاعِثُ بِلَا مَشَقَّةٍ. (قيوم) أي قائم بنفسه وذاته ، وهي عبارة عن استغنائه تعالى عن المحل والمخصص تعالى الله عنهما، وتعبير المصنف بصيغة المبالغة للإشارة بأنه القائم بنفسه المقيم لغيره بالتدبير والحفظ. ثم أكد ذلك بقوله : (لا ينام أي لا يأخذه ما يأخذ الحيوانات من آفة النوم، وهي حالة تعرض للحيوان عن استرخاء أعصاب الدماغ من رطوبات الأبخرة المتصاعدة بحيث تقف المشاعر الظاهرة عن الإحساس رأسياً. قاله السيد (١). والله تعالى منزه عن ذلك؛ إذ من يعتريه ذلك غير تام الحياة ناقص الحفظ والقيام، فكيف وهو الحي القيوم لا تأخذه سنة ولا نوم. (خالق) لجميع خلقه (بلا حاجة إليهم، رازق لهم) فضلا منه (بلا) تحمل كلفة (مؤنة) تثقله، (ممیت) لهم عند انقضاء آجالهم بلا مخافة ترهبه، باعث لهم عند إرادة بعثهم بلا مشقة تلحقه؛ لأن كلا من الحاجة والمؤنة والمخافة والمشقة ونحوها من سمات النقص، والله سبحانه وتعالى منزه عنه.
Al-Qayyum (the Self-Subsisting) does not sleep, Creator without need, Provider to them without burden, Giver of death without fear, Raised [them] without difficulty. (Qayyum) meaning He is self-subsisting and self-existing, which is an expression of His highness being free of need for a location and a specifier — exalted is Allah above them both. And the author's expression in the intensive form indicates that He is the Self-Subsisting who sustains others through management and preservation. Then he emphasizes that by His saying: (does not sleep) meaning He is not overtaken by what overtakes animals from the affliction of sleep, which is a state that occurs to an animal from relaxation of the brain nerves due to rising moist vapors such that the external senses cease sensation completely — as stated by Sayyid. And Allah is transcendent above that; for whoever is affected by that is imperfect in life and deficient in preservation and self-subsistence, so how [could that be] when He is the Living, the Self-Subsisting whom neither slumber nor sleep overtakes. (Creator) of all His creation (without need of them, Provider to them) as a favor from Him (without) bearing the burden of (expense) that weighs Him down, (Giver of death) to them at the end of their terms without fear that terrifies Him, (Raise) them when He wills their resurrection without difficulty that affects Him; because each of need, expense, fear, difficulty and the like are marks of deficiency, and Allah — glorified and exalted — is transcendent above that.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the attributes of Allah mentioned in the Tahawiyyah text: Al-Qayyum, Al-Khaliq, Ar-Razzaq, Al-Mumit, and Al-Ba'ith. The commentator first explains 'Qayyum' as meaning self-subsisting and self-existing, emphasizing that Allah is free from need for a location or a specifier. The intensive form of the word indicates that He not only subsists Himself but also sustains others through His management and preservation. Then he explains the negation of sleep: sleep is a weakness that affects living beings due to bodily functions, but Allah is free from such imperfection; He is the Living, Self-Subsisting who never slumbers. Next, He is the Creator of all without any need of them, the Provider without burden, the Giver of death without fear, and the Resurrector without difficulty. All these negated elements — need, expense, fear, difficulty — are signs of deficiency, and Allah is utterly transcendent above them. The commentary thus affirms Allah's absolute perfection and independence.

Key Terms

الخالق
الرازق
المميت
الباعث
النوم
المشقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that Allah's attributes imply similarity to creation, e.g., that His being 'Qayyum' means He needs a place, or that His 'sleep' negation suggests He could sleep like us.
Correction: The commentary clarifies that these attributes are perfect and free from any creaturely imperfections. Allah is self-subsisting without a location, and His negation of sleep is because sleep is a deficiency, not because He could sleep but chooses not to.

Checkpoint
What does the commentary say about Allah's attribute 'Qayyum'?
A) It means He is dependent on creation.
B) It means He is self-subsisting and sustains others.
C) It means He sleeps to rest.
D) It means He has a body.

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes are perfect and free from any deficiency; His independence, power, and mercy are absolute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you worry about your daily provision, do you truly believe that Allah is ar-Razzaq who provides without any burden? How would your anxiety change if you internalized this attribute?
?
If Allah is al-Qayyum, self-subsisting and sustaining all, why do you still act as if your existence or success depends on your own efforts or others? What step can you take today to rely more on His sufficiency?
?
The passage teaches that Allah gives death without fear. Are you afraid of death because you doubt His mercy, or because you cling to this world? How can you prepare your heart to meet the One who causes death without fear?

Allah's Eternal Attributes and Names Before Creation
Commentary affirming the eternity of Allah's attributes and names.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's attributes and names are eternal and not dependent on creation, and why He is rightly called 'Creator' and 'Originator' even before any creation exists.

Core Idea
Allah's names are as eternal as His attributes, not acquired through creation.

This passage from the Sharh al-Tahawiyyah addresses a common misconception: that Allah's names like 'Creator' only apply after He creates. The commentary explains that these names are eternal because they are based on His eternal attributes. As you read, notice how the author uses logic and analogy to affirm Allah's perfection independent of creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage includes both the core text and its commentary in parentheses.
2
Identify the main claim about attributes
The passage starts by stating that Allah has always been eternal with His attributes and did not increase by creation. Find this claim and understand its meaning.
The word 'Qadim' (eternal) is key.
3
Follow the argument for names
The passage then argues that Allah's names like 'Creator' and 'Originator' are not acquired upon creation. Notice the analogy with 'Giver of life' and the underlying reason given.
The reason: Allah's power, everything's need, and ease.
4
Reflect on the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding that Allah only becomes 'Creator' when He creates. The passage directly refutes this, showing that names are based on eternal attributes.
This safeguards divine transcendence.

الأسماء والصفات] مَا زَالَ بِصِفَاتِهِ قَدِيبًا قَبْلَ خَلْقِهِ، لَمْ يَزْدَدْ بِكَوْنِهِمْ شَيْئًا لَمْ يَكُنْ قَبْلَهُمْ مِنْ صِفَاتِهِ، وَكَمَا كَانَ بِصِفَاتِهِ أَزَلِيًّا كَذَلِكَ لَا يَزَالُ عَلَيْهَا أَبَدِيًا. لَيْسَ مُنْذُ خَلَقَ الخَلْقَ اسْتَفَادَ اسْمَ الخَالِقِ، وَلَا بِإِحْدَائِهِ البَرِيَّةَ اسْتَفَادَ اسْمَ البَارِي، لَهُ مَعْنَى الرُّبُوبِيَّةِ وَلَا مَرْبُوبَ وَمَعْنَى الخَالِقِيَّةِ وَلَا تَخْلُوقَ، وَكَما أَنَّهُ يُحْيِي المَوْتَى بَعْدَمَا أَحْيَاهُمْ اسْتَحَقَّ هَذَا الاسْمَ قَبْلَ إِحْيَاتِهِمْ كَذَلِكَ اسْتَحَقَّ اسْمَ الْخَالِقِ قَبْلَ إِنْشَائِهِمْ؛ ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّهُ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ إِلَيْهِ فَقِيرٌ وَكُلُّ أَمْرٍ عَلَيْهِ يَسِيرٌ. (ما زال سبحانه وتعالى (بصفانه ) أي معها ( قديما) من قبل خلقه) الخلق (لم يزدد بكونهم أي بسبب وجودهم شيئًا لم يكن قبلهم) أي قبل وجودهم (من صفاته) متعلق بمحذوف صفة لشيء؛ أي: لم يزدد بوجودهم شيئًا من صفاته لم يكن قبل وجودهم؛ إذ لو استفاد صفة لم يكن موصوفًا بها في الأزل لكان إذ ذاك ناقضا تعالى الله عن ذلك، ( وكما كان سبحانه وتعالى (بصفاته) قديا أزليا كذلك لا يزال عليها أبديًا ) سرمديا ، ليس منذ خلق الخلق) وأوجدهم (استفاد اسم الخالق ولا بإحداثه البرية) أي الخلق (استفاد اسم البارئ)؛ بل هو سبحانه موصوف وثابت له معنى الربوبية ولا إذ ذاك (مربوب) موجود (و) له معنى الخالقية ولا إذ ذاك (مخلوق) موجود، (وكما أنه سبحانه وتعالى يوصف بأنه (محيي الموتى بعدما أحياهم) أي بعد إحيائهم وقد استحق هذا الاسم) الآن والحال أنه قبل إحيائهم كذلك استحق اسم الخالق قبل خلقهم و إنشائهم) و ذلك بأنه) أي بسبب أنه على كل شيء قدير وكل شيء إليه فقير وكل أمر عليه يسير).
He has always been eternal with His attributes before His creation; He did not increase by their existence something of His attributes that was not before them, and just as He was eternal with His attributes, so also He will always remain upon them forever. It is not that since He created creation He acquired the name 'Creator', nor by originating creatures did He acquire the name 'Originator'. He has the meaning of Lordship without a lorded, and the meaning of Creatorship without a created. And just as He gives life to the dead after having given them life, He deserved this name before giving them life, likewise He deserved the name 'Creator' before creating them; that is because He is powerful over everything, everything is needy towards Him, and every matter is easy for Him. (He, glorified and exalted, has always (with His attributes) as eternal (before His creation) of creatures. (He did not increase by their existence, i.e., because of their existence, from His attributes) an attribute that was not before them, i.e., before their existence. (Just as He, glorified and exalted, was with His attributes eternally primordial, so also He will never cease upon them eternally) perpetual. It is not since He created the creation and brought them into existence (that He acquired the name 'Creator', nor by originating the creatures i.e., the creation (did He acquire the name 'Originator'); rather, He, glorified, is described and established with the meaning of Lordship while there is not then a 'lorded' existing, and with the meaning of Creatorship while there is not then a 'created' existing. (And just as He, glorified and exalted, is described as 'Giver of life to the dead after having given them life' i.e., after giving them life, and He deserved this name) now, while He has before giving them life, likewise He deserved the name 'Creator' before creating them and originating them. (And that is because) i.e., because He is powerful over everything, and everything is in need of Him, and every matter is easy for Him.)
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Tahawiyyah text regarding Allah's eternal attributes and names. It explains that Allah has always been eternal with His attributes, and He did not acquire any new attribute upon creating the creation. The author then emphasizes that Allah is called 'Creator' even before creation existed, just as He is called 'Giver of life' even before actually giving life. The reason given is that Allah is powerful over everything, everything is needy of Him, and everything is easy for Him. The commentary expands by clarifying that Allah has the meaning of Lordship and Creatorship intrinsically, irrespective of the existence of any created thing. It dismisses any notion that Allah's names or attributes are contingent upon creation. This safeguards the doctrine of the eternality of Allah's attributes and names.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Allah is called 'Creator' only after He creates, as if the name is acquired at the moment of creation.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Allah has always been worthy of the name 'Creator' because His attribute of power is eternal, regardless of whether creation exists.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Allah deserve the name 'Creator' before creating?
A) Because He created in the past.
B) Because He is powerful over everything and everything is in need of Him.
C) Because He will create in the future.
D) Because He only deserves names after the act.

Key Takeaway
Allah's names and attributes are eternal, rooted in His power and independence from creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's names are eternal and He is called 'Creator' even before you existed, does that mean your existence is necessary for His attribute of creativity? How does this shape your view of your own significance and purpose in life? What would change if you truly believed you were created purely because Allah is the Creator, not because He needed you?
?
The passage says Allah has 'the meaning of Lordship without a lorded.' This means that His lordship is real even when there is no one to lord over. What does this tell you about your need for Him? Are you living each day as a 'lorded' being, completely dependent, or do you act as if you can manage without Him? Take a moment to name one area where you have been trying to be independent of His lordship, and commit to surrendering it today.
?
Allah is powerful over everything, everything is in need of Him, and every matter is easy for Him. Do you feel the weight of your own bankruptcy before Him? When you face a difficult situation, do you rush to your own plans first or do you turn to the One for whom every matter is easy? If you are honest, what is the one worry you have not handed over to Him because you think it is too hard for even Allah to solve? How will you change that right now?

The Eternity of Allah's Attributes and Names
Imam Maydani elaborates on the eternity of Allah's attributes using the example of creation and revival.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's attributes and names are eternal and not contingent upon creation, based on the explanation of Imam al-Tahawi's creed by Imam Maydani.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are eternal—He never acquires new ones upon creating.

This passage from Imam al-Tahawi's creed, explained by Imam Maydani, affirms that Allah's attributes are inherent and not acquired through creation. It corrects the misconception that Allah became the Creator only after creating. Let's read the original Arabic and its explanation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic matn
First, read the first paragraph of the Arabic passage (the original creed statement) without distraction. Notice how it asserts the eternity of Allah's attributes.
This is the foundational text by Imam al-Tahawi.
2
Read the commentary
Next, read the second paragraph, which is Imam Maydani's expanded explanation. See how he unpacks each phrase.
The commentary uses logical reasoning to defend the creed.
3
Identify the key argument
Notice the core argument: if Allah acquired an attribute at creation, He would have been deficient before. Also, the example of reviving the dead shows that names are deserved before the act.
This demonstrates that power and lordship are eternal.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this matters: if attributes were acquired, Allah would change—but He is perfect and eternal. This doctrine safeguards tawheed.
This lesson reinforces the transcendence of Allah.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأسماء والصفات

مَا زَالَ بِصِفَاتِهِ قَدِيبًا قَبْلَ خَلْقِهِ، لَمْ يَزْدَدْ بِكَوْنِهِمْ شَيْئًا لَمْ يَكُنْ قَبْلَهُمْ مِنْ صِفَاتِهِ، وَكَمَا كَانَ بِصِفَاتِهِ أَزَلِيًّا كَذَلِكَ لَا يَزَالُ عَلَيْهَا أَبَدِيًا.

لَيْسَ مُنْذُ خَلَقَ الخَلْقَ اسْتَفَادَ اسْمَ الخَالِقِ، وَلَا بِإِحْدَائِهِ البَرِيَّةَ اسْتَفَادَ اسْمَ البَارِي، لَهُ مَعْنَى الرُّبُوبِيَّةِ وَلَا مَرْبُوبَ وَمَعْنَى الخَالِقِيَّةِ وَلَا مَخْلُوقَ، وَكَما أَنَّهُ يُحْيِي المَوْتَى بَعْدَمَا أَحْيَاهُمْ اسْتَحَقَّ هَذَا الاسْمَ قَبْلَ إِحْيَاتِهِمْ كَذَلِكَ اسْتَحَقَّ اسْمَ الْخَالِقِ قَبْلَ إِنْشَائِهِمْ؛ ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّهُ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ إِلَيْهِ فَقِيرٌ وَكُلُّ أَمْرٍ عَلَيْهِ يَسِيرٌ.

(ما زال سبحانه وتعالى (بصفاته) أي معها (قديما) من قبل خلقه) الخلق (لم يزدد بكونهم أي بسبب وجودهم شيئًا لم يكن قبلهم) أي قبل وجودهم (من صفاته) متعلق بمحذوف صفة لشيء؛ أي: لم يزدد بوجودهم شيئًا من صفاته لم يكن قبل وجودهم؛ إذ لو استفاد صفة لم يكن موصوفًا بها في الأزل لكان إذ ذاك ناقصًا تعالى الله عن ذلك، (وكما كان سبحانه وتعالى (بصفاته) قديما أزليا كذلك لا يزال عليها أبديًا) سرمديا، ليس منذ خلق الخلق) وأوجدهم (استفاد اسم الخالق ولا بإحداثه البرية) أي الخلق (استفاد اسم البارئ)؛ بل هو سبحانه موصوف وثابت له معنى الربوبية ولا إذ ذاك (مربوب) موجود (و) له معنى الخالقية ولا إذ ذاك (مخلوق) موجود، (وكما أنه سبحانه وتعالى يوصف بأنه (محيي الموتى بعدما أحياهم) أي بعد إحيائهم وقد استحق هذا الاسم) الآن والحال أنه قبل إحيائهم كذلك استحق اسم الخالق قبل خلقهم وإنشائهم) (وذلك بأنه) أي بسبب أنه على كل شيء قدير وكل شيء إليه فقير وكل أمر عليه يسير).
The Names and Attributes. He continues to be with His attributes eternal before His creation. He did not increase by their existence anything that was not before them from His attributes. And just as He was with His attributes eternally beginningless, so also He continues upon them eternally endless. It is not that since He created the creation He acquired the name al-Khaliq (the Creator), nor by His bringing into existence the creatures He acquired the name al-Bari (the Maker). He possesses the meaning of Lordship when there is no lorded-over, and the meaning of Creatorship when there is no created thing. And just as He revives the dead after they have died—He deserves this name before their revival—so also He deserved the name al-Khaliq before their origination. That is because He is over all things powerful, and everything is to Him dependent, and every matter for Him is easy. (He, exalted and high, continues (with His attributes) i.e. along with them (eternal) before His creation) the creation (did not increase by their existence i.e. because of their existence anything that was not before them) i.e. before their existence (from His attributes) attached to an omitted noun as a description of 'something'; i.e. He did not increase by their existence any of His attributes that was not before their existence; for if He had acquired an attribute that He was not described with in pre-eternity, He would then have been deficient—exalted is Allah above that. (And just as He, exalted and high, (with His attributes) was eternal, beginningless, so also He continues upon them endlessly) perpetual. It is not since He created the creation) and brought them into existence (He acquired the name al-Khaliq, nor by His bringing into existence the creatures) i.e. the creation (did He acquire the name al-Bari); rather He, exalted, is described and established with the meaning of Lordship when there is no (lorded-over) existing, and (He has) the meaning of Creatorship when there is no (created thing) existing. (And just as He, exalted and high, is described as (Reviver of the dead after they have died) i.e. after their revival, and He deserved this name) now and the case is that before their revival, likewise He deserved the name al-Khaliq before their creation and origination) (and that is because) i.e. because He is over all things powerful and everything is to Him dependent and every matter for Him is easy.)
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a statement of Imam al-Tahawi regarding the divine attributes and names. It begins by quoting the original text: 'He continues with His attributes eternal before His creation, He did not increase by their existence anything that was not before them from His attributes...' and then explains it phrase by phrase. The core doctrine affirmed here is that Allah's attributes are not acquired through creation; they are eternal and inherent. The argument is that if He had acquired a new attribute at creation, He would have been deficient before—which is impossible for Allah. Furthermore, the names like al-Khaliq (the Creator) and al-Bari (the Maker) were always deserved, even before anything was created, because He had the power and lordship eternally. The example of reviving the dead is used: Allah deserved the name 'Reviver' before actually reviving anyone, because He had the power. The same logic applies to creation. The passage concludes that this is because He is all-powerful, everything depends on Him, and all matters are easy for Him. This commentary thus reinforces the Ash'ari/Maturidi doctrine that Allah's attributes are eternal and not contingent on creation.

The Maturidi View on Takwin
Imam Maydani presents the Maturidi proof for the eternity of takwin and its implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi argument for the eternity of the attribute of takwin and its implications, including its distinction from power and created things.

Core Idea
Takwin is an eternal attribute distinct from power and the things made.

This lesson examines the Maturidi position on the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). Imam Maydani presents their proof that Allah must possess an eternal attribute of making, otherwise His being the Maker would be like a knower without knowledge. We will unpack this argument and its consequences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without worrying about details. Then read the translation to get the main claim and proof.
2
Identify the core proof
Find the Maturidi proof: Allah is the Maker of things by consensus; if He were a Maker without an attribute of making (takwin), that would be impossible, like a knower without knowledge. Hence takwin must exist.
The analogy of 'knower without knowledge' is key.
3
Understand why takwin is eternal
The passage argues that takwin must be beginningless because accidents cannot subsist in Allah's essence. This prevents takwin from being a temporal attribute.
This distinguishes the Maturidi view from the Ash'ari position, where attributes of action are temporal.
4
Reflect on the Maturidi conclusions
The Maturidis affirm four points: takwin is beginningless, distinct from power, other than the thing made, and its beginninglessness does not imply the eternity of created things.
This safeguards against accusations of believing in the eternity of the world.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنه قد اشتهر الخلاف في صفات الفعل (۱) من الخلق والرزق والإحياء والإماتة ونحو ذلك المعبر عنها بالتكوين؛ فذهب الماتريدية (٢) إلى أنها صفات قديمة بدليل أن البارئ تعالى مكون الأشياء ومنشئها إجماعا، وكونه تعالى مكون الأشياء بدون صفة التكوين - التي المكونات آثار تحصل عن تعلقها بها ـ محال ضرورة استحالة وجود الأثر بدون الصفة التي يحصل بها الأثر؛ كالعالم بلا علم ولابد أن تكون صفة التكوين أزلية؛ لامتناع قيام الحوادث بذاته تعالى. قال في شرح المقاصد: أسند القول بالتكوين إلى الشيخ أبي منصور الماتريدي وأتباعه، وهم ينسبونه إلى قدمائهم الذين كانوا قبل الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري؛ حتى قالوا: إن قول أبي حنيفة والطحاوي له معنى الربوبية ولا مربوب والخالقية ولا مخلوق إشارة إلى هذا، ثم أطبقوا على إثبات أزلية التكوين ومغايرته للقدرة وكونه غير المكون وأن أزليته لا تستلزم أزلية المكونات (۳) انتهى.
Know that the dispute has become famous regarding the attributes of action (1)—such as creation, provision, giving life, causing death, and the like, which are expressed by the term 'takwin' (bringing into existence). The Maturidis (2) held that they are eternal attributes, based on the proof that the Creator, exalted, is the Maker of things and their Originator, by consensus. And His being the Maker of things without the attribute of takwin—of which the made things are effects that come about through its attachment to them—is impossible, due to the impossibility of the existence of the effect without the attribute through which the effect is obtained; like a knower without knowledge. And it is necessary that the attribute of takwin be beginningless, due to the impossibility of accidents subsisting in His essence, exalted. It is said in Sharh al-Maqasid: The statement on takwin is attributed to Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and his followers, and they trace it back to their early scholars who were before Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. They even said that the statement of Abu Hanifa and al-Tahawi—'He has the meaning of Lordship when there is no lorded-over, and the meaning of Creatorship when there is no created thing'—is an indication of this. Then they agreed upon affirming the beginninglessness of takwin, its distinction from power, its being other than the thing made, and that its beginninglessness does not necessitate the beginninglessness of made things. (3) End.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage presents the Maturidi position on the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). It begins by noting the famous dispute concerning the attributes of action, which include creation, provision, life, death, etc., all encompassed by the concept of takwin. The Maturidis assert that these attributes are eternal. Their proof is that Allah is unanimously considered the Maker of things; if He were a Maker without an attribute of making (takwin), it would be like saying a knower knows without knowledge, which is impossible. Therefore, there must be an eternal attribute of takwin. Furthermore, since accidents cannot subsist in Allah's essence, this attribute must be beginningless. The passage then quotes from Sharh al-Maqasid, which reports that the doctrine of takwin is attributed to Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and his early followers, even before al-Ash'ari. They interpret the statement of Abu Hanifa and al-Tahawi about Allah having the meaning of Lordship without a lorded-over as supporting their view. The Maturidis affirm four points: that takwin is beginningless, distinct from power, other than the thing made, and that its beginninglessness does not entail the beginninglessness of created things. This distinguishes them from those who might argue that such an attribute implies the eternity of the world.

Key Terms
تكوين
صفات الفعل
ماتريدية
قدرة
المكون
أزلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Maturidi view of eternal takwin means the world is eternal or that takwin is a created attribute.
Correction: The Maturidis explicitly affirm that takwin's beginninglessness does not necessitate the eternity of created things. Takwin is an eternal attribute, but its effects (the things made) are temporal.

Checkpoint
What is the Maturidi proof for the eternity of the attribute of takwin?
A) Allah is the Maker of things, and making requires an attribute of making; else it would be like a knower without knowledge.
B) The Qur'an states that Allah's attributes are eternal.
C) The early scholars unanimously agreed on its eternity.
D) Attributes of action cannot be temporal because they are essential.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidis affirm an eternal attribute of takwin, distinct from power and from the things made, without implying the eternity of creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah’s attribute of takwin is eternal, meaning He is always the Creator even when nothing is created, does your awareness of Him as your personal Creator every single moment remain constant, or do you only remember Him when you need something? How can you train yourself to live with the consciousness that His act of bringing you into existence is ongoing and not a one-time event?
?
The Maturidis argue that it is impossible for Allah to be the Maker without an attribute of making—just as a knower cannot know without knowledge. Does your faith have a real attribute behind it? Do you merely claim to be a believer, or is there an active, living attribute of Iman that produces effects in your daily choices and character? What would change if you took this analogy seriously?
?
The passage emphasizes that the eternity of takwin does not force the world to be eternal. Are there areas in your life where you assume that because Allah is eternal and His decrees are timeless, your own efforts or changes are pointless? How can you embrace the truth that His eternal attribute of bringing into existence does not negate your responsibility to act, but rather empowers it?

Essential vs Active Divine Attributes
The editor divides divine attributes into essential and active categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between essential and active attributes and how active attributes are merely relational, preserving divine immutability.

Core Idea
Essential attributes have no opposites; active attributes are relational.

This footnote from a classical commentary on al-Tahawiyyah provides a clear criterion for distinguishing two categories of divine attributes. Before we explore specific names of Allah, we must first grasp this foundational classification. The passage not only defines each category but also explains how attributes of action are rooted in the single attribute of power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
First, read the Arabic text and the English translation carefully. Note the author's concise style.
2
Identify the two categories
Find the definitions of 'attributes of essence' and 'attributes of action'. Notice the key difference: essence attributes have no opposites, action attributes do.
Also note that action attributes are described as 'relations of power'.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why action attributes are considered relations of power and not separate attributes. How does this preserve the belief that Allah does not change?
This connects to the broader theological principle of divine immutability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱) تنقسم الصفات إلى قسمين: الأولى: صفات ذات، وهي كل صفة يوصف الله تعالى بها ولا يوصف بضدها، والثانية: ما يوصف الله به ويضده كالرضا والرحمة والسخط والغضب، ونحو ذلك من تعلقات صفة القدرة؛ فالقدرة إذا تعلقت بالحياة سمي إحياء وإذا تعلقت بالشيء المرزوق به سمي رزقا ... وهذه التعلقات هي المسماة بصفات الأفعال نحو الخالق البارئ المحيي المميت الرازق... إلخ.
(1) The attributes are divided into two divisions: First: attributes of essence (sifāt dhāt), which are every attribute by which Allah, exalted, is described and is not described by its opposite. Second: what Allah is described by and its opposite, such as pleasure (riḍā), mercy (raḥma), anger (sakhaṭ), wrath (ghaḍab), and the like among the relations of the attribute of power (qudra). For power, when it relates to life, it is called giving life (iḥyā'); when it relates to the thing that is provided, it is called provision (rizq)... and these relations are what are called the attributes of action (ṣifāt al-afʿāl), such as al-Khāliq, al-Bāri', al-Muḥyī, al-Mumīt, al-Rāziq... etc.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This footnote defines a key classification in Islamic theology: attributes of essence (sifāt dhāt) and attributes of action (sifāt afʿāl). Attributes of essence are those like knowledge, power, will—they have no opposites. Attributes of action are relational; they are described by both the attribute and its opposite (e.g., pleasure vs. anger). They are actually relations of the attribute of power (qudra) to specific objects. For example, when power relates to giving life, the resulting description is 'Giver of life' (Muḥyī); when it relates to providing, it is 'Provider' (Rāziq). These relational descriptions are called attributes of action, and they correspond to names like al-Khāliq (The Creator), al-Bāri' (The Maker), etc. This distinction helps clarify that attributes of action do not imply change in the divine essence, only different relationships with creation.

Key Terms
صفات الذات
صفات الأفعال
القدرة
تعلقات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that attributes of action imply change in Allah's essence.
Correction: The passage explains that these are merely relations of power to objects; the essence remains unchanged.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what distinguishes an attribute of essence from an attribute of action?
A) Attributes of essence have no opposite; attributes of action have opposites.
B) Attributes of essence are eternal; attributes of action are temporal.
C) Attributes of essence are known only through revelation; attributes of action are known through reason.
D) Attributes of essence describe God's relationship with creation; attributes of action describe His eternal nature.

Key Takeaway
Essential attributes are inherent and have no opposites, while active attributes are relational descriptions of Allah's power in creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that Allah's attributes of action like anger and mercy are real but not like human anger or mercy. Does your fear of Allah's anger feel more real knowing it is a direct relation of His power? How will you let this shape your daily choices this week?
?
If essential attributes like knowledge and power have no opposites, how does that strengthen your trust in Allah's complete control over your life? Write one specific area where you will rely more on His power and less on your own.

The Dispute Over the Attributes of Actions: Ash'ari vs. Hanafi
Maydani presents the Ash'ari and Hanafi views on the attributes of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the dispute over whether the attributes of actions (ṣifāt al-afʿāl) are created or eternal, and the key arguments from both Ash'ari and Hanafi perspectives.

Core Idea
The attributes of actions are either attachments of power (Ash'ari) or eternal attributes (Hanafi).

This passage from Maydani delves into a central theological disagreement: are God's attributes of action—like creating and providing—eternal or created? The Ash'arites argue they are temporal attachments of power, while the later Hanafites consider them eternal attributes. We will examine both positions and their scriptural evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage introducing the dispute
Read the Arabic passage from the beginning up to the Hanafite argument. This part presents the Ash'ari position and the Hanafite claim.
Notice that the Ash'ari position is stated first: attributes of actions are created because they are attachments of power.
2
Identify the Ash'ari position and its rationale
The Ash'arites say these attributes are created (ḥāditha) because they are attachments (taʿalluqāt) of power, and all attachments are created. Understand why this makes them temporal.
Attachments are relational aspects that arise with the existence of the created thing.
3
Understand the Hanafi claim and their evidence
The later Hanafites from Abu Mansur claimed these attributes are eternal (qadīma) and additional to the essential attributes. They base this on Abu Hanifa's statement: 'He was Creator before He created, and Provider before He provided.'
The Hanafites interpret this as indicating an eternal attribute of origination (takwīn).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذهب الأشاعرة إلى أنها حادثة؛ لأنها عبارة عن تعلقات القدرة والتعلقات كلها حادثة، وفي المسايرة للمحقق الكمال بن الهمام: اختلفت مشايخ الحنفية والأشاعرة في صفات الأفعال، والمراد صفات تدل على تأثير لها أسماء غير اسم القدرة باعتبار أسماء آثارها، والكل يجمعها اسم التكوين؛ فإن كان ذلك الأثر مخلوقا فالاسم الخالق والصفة الخلق، أو الأثر رزقا فالاسم الرازق والصفة الترزيق، أو حياة فهو المحيي أو موتا فهو المميت؛ فادعى متأخر و الحنفية من عهد أبي منصور أنها صفات قديمة زائدة على الصفات المتقدمة، وليس في كلام أبي حنيفة والمتقدمين تصريح بذلك سوى ما أخذوه من قوله: "كان تعالى خالقا قبل أن يخلق ورازقاً قبل أن يرزق"، وذكروا له أوجها من الاستدلال. والأشاعرة يقولون: ليست صفة التكوين على فصولها سوى صفة القدرة باعتبار تعلقها بمتعلق خاص فالتخليق القدرة باعتبار تعلقها بالمخلوق والترزيق تعلقها بإيصال الرزق، وما ذكروه ـ يعني متأخري الحنفية ـ في معناه لا ينفي هذا ولا يوجب كونها صفات أخرى لا ترجع إلى القدرة المتعلقة بما ذكر، ولا يلزم في دليل لهم ذلك، وأما نسبتهم ذلك للمتقدمين ففيه نظر؛ بل في كلام أبي حنيفة ما يفيد أن ذلك على ما فهم الأشاعرة من هذه الصفات على ما نقله عنه الطحاوي، وساق العبارة المتقدمة في المتن بحروفها. ثم قال: فقوله: "ذلك بأنه على كل شيء قدير " تعليل وبيان لاستحقاق اسم الخالق قبل المخلوق؛ فأفاد أن معنى الخالق [ قبل الخلق واستحقاقه اسمه بسبب قيام قدرته تعالى عليه ؛ قاسم الخالق ] والحال لا مخلوق في الأزل لمن له قدرة الخلق في الأزل، وهذا ما يقوله الأشاعرة، والله الموفق. انتهى. وفي المطالب: وأما صفة التكوين فمذهب أهل الحق رجوعها لتعلقات القدرة والإرادة اهـ.
And the Ash'arites held that they are created, because they are expressions of the attachments of power, and all attachments are created. And in al-Musāyarah by the investigator Kamāl ibn al-Humām: The Hanafite and Ash'arite shaykhs differed concerning the attributes of actions. What is meant are attributes that indicate effect; they have names other than the attribute of power considering the names of their effects. All of them are gathered by the name 'origination' (al-takwīn). For if that effect is created, the name is the Creator (al-khāliq) and the attribute is creation (al-khalq); or if the effect is provision, the name is the Provider (al-rāziq) and the attribute is providence (al-tarzīq); or if life, then He is the Giver of life (al-muhyī); or if death, then He is the Giver of death (al-mumīt). The later Hanafites from the era of Abū Mansūr claimed that they are eternal attributes additional to the preceding attributes. There is nothing explicit in the words of Abū Ḥanīfah and the early authorities except what they derived from his saying: 'He, exalted, was Creator before He created, and Provider before He provided.' And they mentioned for it aspects of reasoning. The Ash'arites say: The attribute of origination in its subdivisions is nothing but the attribute of power, considering its attachment to a particular object. So bringing into creation is power considering its attachment to the created thing, and providing is its attachment to delivering provision. And what they (i.e., the later Hanafites) mentioned in its meaning does not negate this, nor does it necessitate that they are other attributes not reducible to power attached to what was mentioned. Nor does it follow from any proof of theirs. As for their attributing that to the early authorities, it is subject to consideration. Rather, in the words of Abū Ḥanīfah there is something that indicates that this is as the Ash'arites understood these attributes, as is transmitted from him by al-Ṭaḥāwī, and he cited the aforementioned phrasing from the text in its exact letters. Then he said: So his saying: 'That is because He is over all things powerful' is a cause and explanation for the entitlement to the name 'Creator' before the creature. So it indicates that the meaning of 'Creator' [before creation and his entitlement to his name due to the establishment of His power over it; the Creator] in the state of no creature in pre-eternity belongs to one who has the power of creation in pre-eternity. And this is what the Ash'arites say. And Allah is the Grantor of success. End. And in al-Maṭālib: As for the attribute of origination, the doctrine of the people of truth is that it reduces to the attachments of power and will. End.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument about the nature of the attributes of actions (ṣifāt al-afʿāl), specifically the attribute of origination (al-takwīn). The author begins by stating the Ash'arite position: these attributes are created (ḥāditha) because they consist of the attachments (taʿalluqāt) of power (al-qudra), and all attachments are created. This means that when Allah creates, the specific attachment of His power to that creation is a temporal event, not an eternal state. He then references al-Musāyarah by Kamāl ibn al-Humām, which records the dispute. The Hanafites (Māturīdites) argue that these attributes are eternal (qadīma) additional to the essential attributes, based on Abū Ḥanīfah's statement that Allah was Creator before creating and Provider before providing. The Ash'arites respond that the attribute of origination is nothing other than the attribute of power in relation to its objects; e.g., 'creating' is power related to the created thing, and 'providing' is power related to delivering provision. They deny that the later Hanafites' interpretation proves additional eternal attributes. Moreover, they challenge the Hanafites' attribution of this view to the early authorities, especially Abū Ḥanīfah, claiming that Abū Ḥanīfah's words actually support the Ash'arite interpretation, as transmitted by al-Ṭaḥāwī. The passage then quotes al-Ṭaḥāwī's creedal statement: 'That is because He is over all things powerful.' The commentary explains that this verse (or saying) serves as a rationale for Allah's entitlement to the name 'Creator' before the existence of creation—because He has the power to create from eternity. This aligns directly with the Ash'arite view that the attribute of power suffices for the name, without needing an eternal attribute of creation. The passage concludes that this is the position of the Ash'arites and endorses it, adding that in al-Maṭālib, the doctrine of the people of truth (Ahl al-Ḥaqq) is that the attribute of origination reduces to attachments of power and will.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Ash'arites deny any real meaning to names like 'Creator' before creation.
Correction: The Ash'arites affirm the name based on eternal power, not on an eternal attribute of creation.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'arites as presented in this passage, what are the attributes of actions such as creating and providing?
A) Eternal attributes additional to power
B) Merely the attachments of power to particular objects
C) Identical with the essence of Allah
D) Created actions that inhere in Allah

Key Takeaway
The core dispute is whether the attributes of action are temporal attachments of power (Ash'ari) or eternal attributes (Hanafi).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You call Allah 'al-Khāliq' (The Creator) every day. But do you live as though His creating attribute is eternal—meaning He is actively creating in your life right now, even when you see no change? What would change if you truly believed that His power to create is eternally present, not just something that happens once?
?
The Hanafis say God was 'Provider before He provided'. When you struggle with provision, do you doubt that He is already the Provider before the provision arrives? How can you strengthen your trust in His eternal attribute of providing, rather than waiting for the outcome to believe?
?
If the Ash'aris are right that the attributes of action are merely relations of God's power, does that make God feel more unified and immediate to you, or more distant? Be honest: which view helps you feel closer to Allah in your prayers—knowing that His creating is just an aspect of His power, or knowing that it is a separate eternal attribute? What does your preference reveal about your heart?

Tahawi's Creed as Evidence for the Ash'ari View
Maydani quotes Tahawi's creed to defend the Ash'ari position on the attributes of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see how Tahawi's creedal statement is used by Ash'arites to argue that God is called Creator before creation because of His eternal power, not an eternal attribute of creation.

Core Idea
God's name 'Creator' is based on eternal power, not an eternal attribute of creating.

After presenting the dispute, Maydani quotes Tahawi's creed to support the Ash'ari interpretation. Tahawi's words—'That is because He is over all things powerful'—serve as a rationale. We will analyze this evidence and see why it aligns with the Ash'ari position.

Guided Path
1
Read the quoted text from Tahawi
Read the section beginning with 'ثم قال: فقوله: "ذلك بأنه على كل شيء قدير "' to the end. This is the evidence from Tahawi.
The passage is a direct quote from Tahawi's creed, which Maydani uses to support the Ash'ari view.
2
Understand how it explains the entitlement to the name 'Creator'
The phrase 'That is because He is over all things powerful' is presented as a rationale (ta'līl) for why God deserves the name 'Creator' even before creation. It shows that the meaning of 'Creator' is based on power, not on an eternal attribute of creation.
The power to create exists eternally, which entitles God to the name 'Creator' even when no creature exists.
3
Connect to the Ash'ari claim that power suffices
This evidence demonstrates that the Ash'ari position—that the attribute of origination reduces to power—is consistent with Tahawi's creed. The passage concludes that this is what the Ash'arites say.
Thus Tahawi's text is used to authenticate the Ash'ari interpretation.

Allah's Eternal Name al-Khaliq
The author explains that Allah deserves the name al-Khaliq before creation due to His eternal power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Allah is called al-Khaliq even before any creation exists, based on His eternal power.

Core Idea
Allah's names are based on eternal attributes, not temporal acts.

This lesson tackles a subtle but crucial point in Islamic theology: does Allah only become 'Creator' when He creates? The Tahawiyyah affirms that Allah's name al-Khaliq is deserved before creation, and the commentary explains why. We'll see how the eternal power (qudra) of Allah justifies this name from pre-eternity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. Notice the key terms like 'قدرة' (power) and 'أزل' (pre-eternity). The structure begins with a citation from Tahawiyyah.
The passage uses a Quranic verse 'ذلك بأنه على كل شيء قدير' as support.
2
Understand the core argument
The passage argues that Allah deserves the name al-Khaliq before creating because His power to create is eternal. This power is a real attribute, even when no creature exists.
Contrast with the view that attributes only exist when they have objects.
3
Explore the analogy
The author compares it to Allah's name as 'One who gives life to the dead' - He deserves that name even before resurrecting anyone, because His power to do so is eternal.
4
Consider the misconception
Many think that names like 'Creator' only apply after the act. This lesson corrects that by establishing that Allah's names reflect His eternal attributes.
This is the position of Ahl al-Sunnah (Ash'aris).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال: فقوله: "ذلك بأنه على كل شيء قدير" تعليل وبيان لاستحقاق اسم الخالق قبل المخلوق؛ فأفاد أن معنى الخالق قبل الخلق واستحقاقه اسمه بسبب قيام قدرته تعالى عليه، والحال لا مخلوق في الأزل لمن له قدرة الخلق في الأزل، وهذا ما يقوله الأشاعرة. انتهى. وفي المطالب: وأما صفة التكوين فمذهب أهل الحق رجوعها لتعلقات القدرة والإرادة. استفاد اسم الخالق ولا بإحداثه البرية استفاد اسم البارئ، له معنى الربوبية ولا مربوب ومعنى الخالقية ولا مخلوق، وكما أنه يحيي الموتى استحق هذا الاسم قبل إحيائهم؛ كذلك استحق اسم الخالق قبل إنشائهم؛ ذلك بأنه على كل شيء قدير. كذا نقله في المسايرة.
Then he said: His saying: 'That is because He is over all things powerful' is a clarification and explanation of deserving the name al-Khaliq before the created; so it indicated that the meaning of al-Khaliq is before creation and his deserving His name due to the establishment of His power over it, and the state is that there is no created in pre-eternity for the one who has the power of creation in pre-eternity, and this is what the Ash'aris say. It ended. And in al-Matalib: As for the attribute of takwin, the school of Ahl al-Haqq is that it refers back to the attachments of power and will. He derived the name al-Khaliq and not by creating creation derived the name al-Bari'; He has the meaning of Lordship without a lorded, and the meaning of Creator-ness without a created, and just as He gives life to the dead He deserved this name before giving them life; likewise He deserved the name al-Khaliq before creating them; that is because He is over all things powerful. Thus it was transmitted in al-Musayara.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a continuous argument explaining why Allah is called al-Khaliq before any creation exists. It begins with the line from Tahawiyyah quoting the Quranic verse 'that is because He is over all things powerful' as a justification. The author explains that this verse indicates that the name al-Khaliq is deserved before the existence of created beings because Allah's power is eternal and precedes creation. The state (al-hal) is that in pre-eternity there is no creation, but He has the power to create. This is the position of the Ash'aris. Then it quotes from al-Matalib that the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence) according to Ahl al-Haqq is reducible to the attachments of power and will. Then it continues: He derived the name al-Khaliq (Creator) not by creating; similarly He derived the name al-Bari' (Maker) without making; He has the meaning of Lordship without a lorded, and the meaning of Creator-ness without a created. The analogy is given: just as He is called 'He gives life to the dead' before actually giving life, so too He is called Creator before creating. All this is because He is powerful over everything. This shows that Allah's names are based on His eternal attributes, not on temporal actions.

Correction: The passage clarifies that Allah deserves the name al-Khaliq before creation because His power to create is eternal and unchanging.

Checkpoint
