The Vision of Allah and the Principle of Tafwid
The author explains the correct approach to the vision of Allah in paradise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the correct belief about seeing Allah in paradise requires abandoning interpretation and submitting to the text.

Core Idea
The only valid interpretation of divine attributes is to abandon interpretation.

This passage from Imam al-Tahawi's creed addresses a delicate matter: the vision of Allah in the afterlife. While affirming this belief, the author warns against two wrong approaches: imagining it or interpreting it metaphorically. Instead, the correct path is what the righteous predecessors followed—submission without asking 'how' or 'why.'

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once, then the literal translation. Notice the key terms: ru'ya, ta'wil, tafwid, taslim.
Pay attention to the phrase 'ترك التأويل' (abandoning interpretation).
2
Identify the two incorrect approaches
The passage says faith is not valid for those who consider it 'by imagination' (wahm) or interpret it 'by understanding' (fahm). These are the two extremes to avoid.
These represent human attempts to conceptualize Allah.
3
Understand the principle of tafwid
The correct interpretation of the vision—and all divine attributes—is to abandon interpretation and adhere to submission. This is the essence of tafwid.
This is the way of all messengers and the righteous predecessors.
4
Reflect on the consequences
The commentary warns that those who rely on imagination or intellect slip from perfect faith into misguidance. Tafwid preserves faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَصِحُ الإِيمَانُ بِالرُّؤْيَةِ لِأَهْلِ دَارِ السَّلَامِ مَنِ اعْتَبَرَهَا مِنْهُمْ بِوَهُم أَوْ تَأَوَّهَا بِفَهُم إِذَا كَانَ تَأْوِيلُ الرُّؤْيَةِ وَتَأْوِيلُ كُلِّ مَعْنَى يُضَافُ إِلَى الرُّبُوبِيَّةِ تَرْكَ التَّأْوِيلِ وَلُزُومَ التَّسْلِيم وَعَلَيْهِ دِينُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ وَشَرَائِعُ النَّبِيِّينَ. ولذا قال: (ولا يصح الإيمان بالرؤية لأهل الجنة دار السلام لمن اعتبرها منهم) أي المؤمنين بالرؤية (بوهم) ،توهمه أو تأولها بفهم) فهمه فينعكس عليه الموضوع إلى الرجوع من تحري كمال الإيمان إلى مزلة الضلالة والطغيان (إذا كان تأويل الرؤية) بل وتأويل كل معنى لا يدرك مما يضاف إلى حضرة (الربوبية) والذات العلية (ترك التأويل ولزوم) الاستسلام) و(التسليم، وعليه) أي على ذلك المذكور (دين المرسلين وشرائع النبيين) وهو مذهب السلف الصالحين صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم أجمعين .
And faith in the vision (of Allah) for the people of the abode of peace is not valid for the one among them who considers it by imagination or interprets it by understanding, when the interpretation of the vision and the interpretation of every meaning attributed to Lordship is to abandon interpretation and adhere to submission. And upon this is the religion of the messengers and the laws of the prophets. Therefore he said: 'Faith in the vision for the people of paradise, the abode of peace, is not valid for the one among them who considers it by imagination or interprets it by understanding.' That is, those who believe in the vision by their imagination or interpret it by their understanding – the matter is reversed for them, turning from seeking perfect faith to the slippery slope of misguidance and transgression. When the interpretation of the vision, and even the interpretation of every meaning that is not grasped from what is attributed to the presence of Lordship and the High Essence, is to abandon interpretation and adhere to surrender and submission. And upon this is the religion of the messengers and the laws of the prophets, and it is the way of the righteous predecessors, may the prayers and peace of Allah be upon them all.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal rule regarding the vision of Allah (ru'ya) in paradise. The matn states that faith in the vision is not valid for the one who considers it by imagination (wahm) or interprets it by understanding (fahm). The correct approach is that the interpretation (ta'wīl) of the vision and every attribute of Lordship is to abandon interpretation and adhere to submission (taslīm) and surrender (istislām). The commentary explains that those who rely on imagination or intellectual interpretation invert the situation, turning from seeking perfect faith into misguidance. The commentator emphasizes that this method – abandoning interpretation and adhering to submission – is the religion of all messengers and the way of the righteous predecessors (salaf).

Key Terms
رؤية
تأويل
تفويض
تسليم
السلف الصالحين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the vision of Allah can be understood metaphorically through human intellect.
Correction: The text asserts that the only valid approach is tafwid (delegation) without interpretation or imagination.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the correct interpretation of the vision of Allah and all attributes attributed to Lordship?
A) To interpret them metaphorically using reason.
B) To imagine them in a manner befitting Allah.
C) To abandon interpretation and adhere to submission.
D) To deny them entirely.

Key Takeaway
The correct belief about the vision of Allah is to affirm it without imagining or interpreting, and to submit completely to the divine text.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The passage warns that relying on your own understanding turns you from perfect faith to misguidance. In what area of your aqeedah have you been trusting your reason more than the revelation? Will you commit today to abandon that interpretation and say, 'I believe as the messengers believed, without knowing how'?

Anthropomorphic Expressions in Scripture: The Tafwid Approach
Enumeration of scriptural texts requiring tafwid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the classical Sunni scholars approach Quranic verses and hadith that seem to describe Allah in human-like terms, by applying the method of tafwid (delegation of meaning to Allah).

Core Idea
Scriptural anthropomorphic expressions are not to be interpreted literally; we submit and leave meaning to Allah.

This lesson presents a collection of Quranic verses and prophetic hadith that use words like 'hand,' 'face,' and 'finger' in reference to Allah. These are examples of mutashābih (ambiguous) texts that require a special approach. The author lists them to show the practical application of tafwīḍ, a key principle in Sunni theology for handling such expressions without falling into anthropomorphism or negation.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once slowly, then read the English translation. Notice the specific words highlighted: yad, wajh, nafs, iṣbaʿ, qadam.
The text is cut off due to page break; we only have the beginning of a hadith.
2
Identify the common feature of all cited texts
Ask yourself: What do all these verses and hadith have in common? They all use terms that, if taken literally, would imply Allah has physical body parts. The author lists them as examples of mutashābihāt.
3
Understand the method of tafwid
Based on the commentary, these texts are not to be interpreted metaphorically or literally by human reasoning. Instead, the correct approach is tafwid: we affirm the words as revealed, but delegate the true meaning and modality to Allah alone.
This connects to the previous lesson's explanation of tafwid.
4
Reflect on the purpose of the enumeration
The author could have just stated the principle; why list verses? This shows that the principle is not abstract but applies to specific, well-known texts. It trains the student to recognize such expressions and respond correctly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما ورد من الآيات القرآنية والأحاديث النبوية من وصفه تعالى بما يوهم ظاهره ذلك كاليد والأصبع والقدم وكذا النفس والوجه؛ كقوله تعالى: (يَدُ اللهِ فَوْقَ أَيْدِيهِمْ ﴾ [سورة الفتح آية: ١٠)، (مَا مَنَعَكَ أَن تَسْجُدَ لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَى [سورة ص آية: ٧٥)، (فَتَم وَجهُ اللهِ ﴾ [سورة البقرة آية: ١١٥]، ﴿وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ) [سورة الرحمن آية: (۲۷)، (تَعْلَمُ مَا فِي نَفْسِي وَلَا أَعْلَمُ مَا فِي نَفْسِكَ ) (سورة المائدة آية: ١١٦] ، وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: أَنتَ كَما أَثْنَيْتَ عَلَى نَفْسِكَ» (۱)، وقوله : ( إِنَّ قُلُوبَ بَنِي آدَمَ كُلَّهَا بَيْنَ أَصْبُعَينِ مِنْ أَصَابِعِ الرَّحْمَنِ كَقَلْبِ وَاحِدٍ يُصَرِّفُهُ كَيْفَ
As for what has come in the Quranic verses and Prophetic hadith of His description, may He be exalted, in a manner whose outward appearance suggests that – such as the hand (yad), finger (iṣbaʿ), foot (qadam), as well as soul (nafs) and face (wajh) – like His saying: 'The hand of Allah is above their hands' (Quran 48:10), 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands' (Quran 38:75), 'So wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' (Quran 2:115), 'And there remains the face of your Lord' (Quran 55:27), 'You know what is in my soul and I do not know what is in Your soul' (Quran 5:116), and his saying, peace be upon him: 'You are as You have praised Yourself,' and his saying: 'Indeed, the hearts of the children of Adam, all of them, are between two fingers of the fingers of the Merciful, like one heart; He turns it however...'
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is an illustrative enumeration of Quranic verses and hadith that contain expressions potentially suggesting anthropomorphism (tashbīh) – such as 'hand' (yad), 'finger' (iṣbaʿ), 'foot' (qadam), 'soul' (nafs), and 'face' (wajh). The author lists these as examples of the mutashābih (ambiguous) texts that require the method of tafwīḍ (delegation). The commentary implies that these should not be interpreted literally or metaphorically by human intellect; rather, one must submit to them and abstain from interpretation, as stated in the previous lessons. The passage serves as a practical demonstration of the principle that the proper approach to such texts is to affirm them without modality (tamthīl) and without taʿṭīl (negation), leaving the true meaning to Allah.

Misconception: That verses mentioning Allah's hand, face, etc., prove Allah has literal human-like body parts.
Correction: These are mutashābihāt whose true meaning is known only to Allah; we affirm them as revealed without modality (tafwīḍ), not as literal anthropomorphism.

Ruling on Anthropomorphic Hadiths: Literal Acceptance and Delegation
The author rules that hadiths about Allah's hand, foot, etc. must be taken literally with tafwid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Salafi approach to anthropomorphic hadiths: affirming their literal wording while delegating true knowledge to Allah and maintaining tanzih.

Core Idea
Affirm the words, delegate the meaning, transcend the Creator.

When we encounter hadiths that describe Allah with hand, foot, and other bodily parts, how should a Muslim respond? Imam al-Tahawi (through this commentary) lays down the principle: accept the literal wording without interpretation, entrust the true reality to Allah, and negate any resemblance to creation. This lesson unpacks that rule.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadiths cited
Read the two hadith examples provided: one about Allah spreading His hand for repentance, and another about placing His foot in Hell. Notice their literal wording.
These are authentic hadiths from Sahih Muslim and other sources.
2
Identify the three components of the ruling
The passage states the wajib (obligatory) approach: 1) apply them literally (zahir), 2) delegate knowledge of their reality to Allah (tafwid), and 3) declare Allah transcendent of limbs and resembling created attributes (tanzih).
3
Understand the balance between affirmation and negation
The ruling balances affirming the wording as it came without ta’wil (interpretation) while negating any physical similarity to creation. This is the middle path between tashbih (anthropomorphism) and ta’til (denial of attributes).
This is the position of the Salaf as understood by Ahl al-Sunnah.
4
Reflect on a common misunderstanding
Some think that taking these hadiths literally implies affirming a body for Allah. However, the author immediately pairs it with tanzih, showing that literal acceptance does not mean corporeality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يَشَاءُ)، وقوله: «إِنَّ اللهَ يَبْسُطُ يَدَهُ بِاللَّيلِ لِيَتُوبَ مُسِيءُ النَّهَارِ وَيَبْسُطُ يَدَهُ بِالنَّهَارِ لِيَتُوبَ مُسِيءُ اللَّيْلِ ، حَتَّى تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ مِنْ مَغْرِيها (۲)، وقوله: «لَا تَزَالُ جَهَنَّمُ تَقُولُ هَلْ مِنْ مَزِيدٍ حَتَّى يَضَعَ فِيهَا رَبُّ العِزَّةِ قَدَمَهُ (۳) ونحو ذلك؛ فالواجب إجراؤه على ظاهره وتفويض علمه إلى قائله مع تنزيه الباري عن الجارحة ومشابهة الصفات المحدثة.

Commentary
This passage presents the rule for dealing with hadiths that attribute physical body parts to Allah (such as hand and foot). The author cites two hadiths: one about Allah extending His hand, and another about placing a foot in Hell. He then states the obligatory approach: these texts must be taken in their apparent meaning (zahir) without interpretation (ta'wil), but their true nature is delegated (tafwid) to Allah who spoke them. At the same time, one must negate any resemblance to created beings and transcend Allah above having a body or limbs. This is the position of the Salaf.

Al-Bazdawi on the Known Origin and Ambiguous Description of Attributes
Al-Bazdawi affirms hand and face as known in origin but ambiguous in description.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the known origin of divine attributes and their ambiguous description, and why rejecting the origin due to ignorance of modality is a deviation.

Core Idea
The reality of Allah's attributes is affirmed even if the 'how' is unknown.

Al-Bazdawi provides a concise and powerful principle for understanding divine attributes. He distinguishes between the established fact that Allah has certain attributes and the human inability to comprehend their exact nature. This passage warns against the error of denying what is affirmed simply because we cannot fully grasp it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Note the key terms: 'asl' (origin) and 'wasf' (description).
The passage is a direct quote from al-Bazdawi's work on usul.
2
Identify the core distinction
Al-Bazdawi distinguishes between the origin (asl) of the attributes, which is known (ma'lum), and their description (wasf), which is ambiguous (mutashabih). This is the foundation of his argument.
Understanding this distinction is crucial for avoiding anthropomorphism without denying the attributes.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila error
The Mu'tazila rejected the affirmation of hand and face entirely because they could not comprehend the modality. Al-Bazdawi says they 'went astray from this aspect.'
The error is a logical fallacy: nullifying the origin due to inability to grasp the description.
4
Reflect on the broader principle
This principle applies to all divine attributes: we affirm what Allah and His messenger have affirmed, while delegating the reality of the 'how' to Allah.
This is a key principle of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الإمام فخر الإسلام البزدوي في أصوله: «إثبات اليد والوجه عندنا معلوم بأصله متشابه بوصفه، ولن يجوز إبطال الأصل بالعجز عن درك الوصف وإنما ضلت المعتزلة من هذا الوجه» اهـ.
Imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi said in his Principles: 'The affirmation of the hand and the face is, in our view, known in its origin, ambiguous in its description, and it is not permissible to nullify the origin due to inability to grasp the description; indeed the Mu'tazila went astray from this aspect.' End.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is a direct quote from Imam al-Bazdawi's work on usul (principles). He makes a key distinction: the existence and affirmation of the attributes 'hand' (yad) and 'face' (wajh) are established and known in their asl (origin, i.e., that Allah has them), but their kayfiyyah (how) is ambiguous (mutashabih) and unknown to us. Therefore, one cannot reject the origin simply because one cannot comprehend the modality. The Mu'tazila deviated precisely because they denied the attributes outright, claiming that affirming them would lead to anthropomorphism, thus nullifying the origin due to their inability to understand the description.

Key Terms
أصل
وصف
إثبات
تشابه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If we don't know exactly how an attribute exists, then the attribute cannot be real.
Correction: Al-Bazdawi clarifies that the origin is known even if the description is ambiguous; rejecting the origin because of ignorance of modality is a logical fallacy.

Checkpoint
According to al-Bazdawi, why did the Mu'tazila go astray regarding Allah's hand and face?
A) They denied the origin due to inability to understand the description
B) They affirmed the description literally
C) They claimed the attributes are eternal
D) They rejected the hadiths

Key Takeaway
Affirming Allah's attributes is based on the known origin, not on comprehending the modality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever rejected a truth about Allah—whether an attribute or a decree—because you could not fully comprehend how it could be? What does al-Bazdawi’s principle demand of you in that moment? Will you commit to affirming the known origin, even when the description remains veiled?
?
The Mu'tazila nullified the origin because they were unable to grasp the description. In which area of your faith might you be subtly doing the same—denying a revealed truth because it clashes with your finite reasoning? What specific step will you take this week to submit your intellect to the revelation?
?
Think of an attribute of Allah that you find difficult or uncomfortable to affirm. Does your discomfort stem from an inability to understand the 'how'? If so, how does al-Bazdawi’s distinction between origin and description free you to accept it? What prayer or practice will you adopt to strengthen your affirmation of that attribute?

Allah's Istiwa over the Throne without Need
Affirmation of istiwa with negation of need and resting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author affirms Allah's istiwa while negating any need or physical relation to the Throne.

Core Idea
Allah's istiwa is without need, resting, or spatial dependence.

This passage from the Sharh Tahawiyyah addresses a key attribute of Allah: His istiwa over the Throne. The author carefully affirms the scriptural term while guarding against anthropomorphic misconceptions. You will see how he uses two logical proofs to show that Allah is free from any need of the Throne or physical resting upon it.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Start by reading the Arabic text slowly, noticing the key terms: الاستواء, العرش, الحاجة, الاستقرار. Then read the English translation.
The passage begins with an affirmation followed by two conditional arguments.
2
Identify the core affirmations
Find the three affirmations: (1) Allah istawa over the Throne, (2) without need, (3) without resting. Also note that He is the Preserver of the Throne and all else.
3
Examine the two proofs
The author gives two 'if-then' arguments: first, if He were in need, He could not create; second, if He needed to sit, where would He be before the Throne? Understand how each refutes the idea of need.
These are logical reductions to absurdity.
4
Connect to divine transcendence
Reflect on how this passage upholds tanzih (transcendence) by negating any likeness to creatures. Allah is not in need of anything and is not spatially limited.
5
Test your understanding
Take the checkpoint quiz to confirm you can identify the correct statement about Allah's relation to the Throne.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الإمام: نقر بأن الله على العرش استوى من غير أن يكون له حاجة إليه واستقرار عليه وهو الحافظ للعرش وغير العرش؛ فلو كان محتاجا لما قدر على إيجاد العالم وتدبيره كالمخلوق، ولو كان محتاجا إلى الجلوس والقرار فقبل خلق العرش أين كان الله تعالى؛ 'تعالى الله' عن ذلك علوا كبيرًا اهـ.
The Imam said: We affirm that Allah established Himself (istawa) over the Throne without having any need of it or resting upon it, and He is the Preserver of the Throne and other than the Throne; for if He were in need, He would not be able to create the world and manage it like a created being; and if He were in need of sitting and settling, then before the creation of the Throne, where was Allah, the Exalted? 'Exalted is Allah' above that, greatly exalted. End.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement affirming the verse of istiwa (Allah's establishment over the Throne) while negating any anthropomorphic implications. The author clarifies three points: (1) Allah's istiwa does not imply need (hajah) for the Throne, (2) it does not imply resting (istiqrar) upon it, and (3) Allah is the Preserver of both the Throne and everything else. The proof is given by way of reductio: if Allah needed the Throne, He would be like a created being and would not be able to create and manage the universe. Furthermore, if He needed to sit, where would He have been before the Throne was created? This is impossible, so Allah is completely transcendent.

Key Terms
الاستواء
العرش
الاستقرار
الحاجة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'istiwa' implies Allah is physically sitting or resting on the Throne, or that He needs the Throne for support.
Correction: The author explicitly negates need (hajah) and resting (istiqrar), and provides proofs showing such ideas would imply incapacity or absurdity.

Checkpoint

A) He is in need of it
B) He rests upon it
C) He established Himself without need or resting and preserves it
D) He is limited to it

Key Takeaway
Allah's istiwa over the Throne is affirmed without any need, resting, or spatial dependence, preserving His absolute transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Before the Throne was created, where was Allah? This question exposes the absurdity of tying Allah to creation. When you feel anxious about your own place or status in this world, how can remembering Allah's eternal independence free you from that anxiety? Write one concrete way you will apply this truth today.

Allah's Independence from the Throne and His Encompassing Knowledge
Explains Allah's independence and encompassing knowledge, quoting Abu Hanifa's will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah is independent of the Throne and all creation, and that His knowledge encompasses everything while His essence is beyond human comprehension.

Core Idea
Allah is independent; His knowledge encompasses all; His essence is beyond comprehension.

Imam Abu Hanifa’s will provides a concise yet profound statement on two fundamental aspects of Allah’s nature: His absolute self-sufficiency and His all-encompassing knowledge. This passage, quoted by Imam al-Maydani, affirms Allah’s transcendence and the limits of human intellect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the words of the Imam sink in before interpreting.
Notice the careful phrasing: 'He is independent in His essence of the Throne and all that is beneath it.'
2
Understand the first part: independence
Reflect on the meaning of 'independent in His essence' (mustaghni bi-dhatihi). This refutes any notion of Allah needing or being confined to the Throne.
3
Examine the second part: guardianship and knowledge
Allah is the Guardian (Hafiz) of the Throne and everything else. His knowledge encompasses everything, including the heavens, earth, and what is between them.
This affirms His complete control and awareness without limitation.
4
Reflect on the conclusion: incapacity to comprehend
Allah has rendered creatures incapable of comprehending His essence (kunnuh). The tasbih emphasizes that describers cannot describe Him nor measure His power.
This underscores tanzih (transcendence) and the limits of human intellect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو مستغن بذاته عن العرش وما دونه، قال الإمام في وصيته: «وهو الحافظ للعرش وغير العرش، محيط علمه بكل شيء، وبسما فوقه وبما تحته وما والاه، وهو سبحانه وتعالى قد أعجز عن الإحاطة بكنهه خلقه؛ سبحان من لا يبلغ الواصفون وصفه ولا يقدر أحد قدره.»
And He is independent in His essence of the Throne and all that is beneath it. The Imam said in his will: 'He is the Guardian of the Throne and other than it, His knowledge encompasses everything, and above the heavens and beneath them and what is between them, and He, exalted and high, has rendered His creatures incapable of comprehending His essence; glory be to Him whom the describers cannot describe nor can anyone measure His power.'
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage discusses two key theological points: Allah's absolute self-sufficiency (ghinā) and His encompassing knowledge (iḥāṭat al-‘ilm). The author begins by stating that Allah is independent in His essence of the Throne (al-‘Arsh) and all that is beneath it. This refutes any notion that Allah needs or is confined to the Throne. Then he quotes the will (wasiyyah) of Imam Abu Hanifa, which elaborates: Allah is the Guardian (Ḥāfiẓ) of the Throne and everything besides it, emphasizing His preservation and control. His knowledge encompasses everything (muḥīṭ ‘ilmuhu bi-kulli shay’), including the heavens above, the earth beneath, and whatever is between them. Finally, the Imam declares that Allah has rendered all creatures incapable of comprehending His essence (kunnuh), meaning that no created being can fully grasp His reality. The passage concludes with a tasbīḥ (glorification) stating that describers cannot adequately describe Him nor can anyone measure His power. This underscores tanzīh (transcendence) and the limitations of human intellect regarding Allah's essence.

Key Terms
مستغن بذاته (independent in essence)
الحافظ (the Guardian)
محيط علمه (His encompassing knowledge)
إحاطة بكنهه (comprehending His essence)
سبحان (glory)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah is physically located on or dependent on the Throne for His rule.
Correction: This passage affirms Allah's absolute independence from the Throne and everything beneath it. He is not reliant on any created thing.

Checkpoint

A) Allah sits on the Throne.
B) Allah is independent of the Throne and everything beneath it.
C) Allah is confined to the Throne.
D) Allah is only known through the Throne.

Key Takeaway
Allah is utterly independent, His knowledge encompasses all, and His essence is beyond human comprehension.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that Allah is independent of the Throne and all creation. Yet do you act as if you are independent of Him? In what area of your life do you feel self-sufficient, ignoring that your very existence depends on Him? Will you repent today?
?

?
The passage says no describer can describe Allah nor can anyone measure His power. How does this humble your attempts to confine Allah to your own limited understanding? In what ways have you tried to 'measure' Allah or reduce Him to fit your preferences?

God's Preservation and All-Encompassing Knowledge
The author affirms God as Preserver of the Throne and declares His knowledge encompasses all things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah is the Preserver of all creation and that His knowledge encompasses everything, while His essence remains beyond human comprehension.

Core Idea
Allah preserves all and knows all, but none can know His essence.

This lesson from the Sharh Tahawiyyah affirms two foundational attributes of Allah: His preservation (hifdh) and His all-encompassing knowledge (ihata). The author emphasizes that while Allah's knowledge covers every detail of creation, His creatures are utterly incapable of grasping His true essence. This sets a clear boundary between divine and human knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Let the rhythm of the author's statement settle in your mind.
Pay attention to the footnote marker—it indicates a variant reading or commentary.
2
Identify the three affirmations
The passage makes three distinct affirmations: (1) Allah is the Preserver of the Throne and everything else, (2) His knowledge encompasses all creation, (3) creatures cannot fully know His essence. Locate each part in the text.
These three points form the core of the lesson.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why the author ends with a statement of incapacity. What does this teach about the relationship between Creator and creature?
This guards against the misconception that humans can fully comprehend God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحافظ للعرش وغير العرش (۱)، محيط علمه بكل شيء حواه وبما فوقه وبما تحته وما والاه، وهو سبحانه وتعالى قد أعجز عن الإحاطة بكنهه خلقه؛ سبحان من لا يبلغ الواصفون وصفه ولا يقدر أحد قدره.
The Preserver of the Throne and other than the Throne, His knowledge encompasses everything that it contains, and what is above it, and what is beneath it, and what is adjacent to it, and He, exalted and majestic, has rendered His creatures incapable of encompassing the reality of His essence; glory be to Him, whose description the describers cannot reach, and no one can measure His measure.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a concise statement of God's attributes of preservation (hifdh) and all-encompassing knowledge (ihata). It begins by affirming that Allah is the Preserver of the Throne and everything else. Then it declares that His knowledge encompasses everything that the Throne contains (i.e., all creation), including what is above, beneath, and adjacent to it. This is a comprehensive assertion of divine omniscience. Finally, the passage emphasizes that despite this, His creatures are incapable of fully grasping the reality of His essence (kannah). It ends with a glorification: no one can truly describe God's full attributes or measure His power. The lesson guards against the misconception that human beings can fully comprehend God's essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some mistakenly think that God's preservation is limited to the Throne alone.
Correction: The text explicitly states 'الحافظ للعرش وغير العرش' (the Preserver of the Throne and other than the Throne), showing that His preservation covers all creation.

Checkpoint
What does the phrase 'أعجز عن الإحاطة بكنهه' indicate?
A) God's knowledge is limited.
B) Creatures cannot know God's essence.
C) God is unable to encompass.
D) The Throne is the only object of preservation.

Key Takeaway
Allah preserves all things, knows all things, but His essence is beyond the grasp of any creature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as if Allah's knowledge encompasses every detail of your life—your thoughts, your secret actions, and even what is above and beneath you? If you truly believed this, what would you change about how you spend your time today?
?
The passage says no one can fully describe Allah or measure His power. Have you ever been content with a limited, comfortable image of Allah that you can fully 'comprehend'? What would it mean to accept that He is beyond your grasp? How should that humble you in worship?
?
When you realize that Allah has rendered all creatures incapable of knowing His essence, does it make you feel distant or draw you closer? How does this truth affect the way you approach Him in prayer and reliance?

Allah Spoke to Musa Directly: Affirmation and Submission
Affirmation of Allah's direct speech to Musa and the necessity of taslim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the emphatic infinitive 'takliman' is used to affirm the literal speech of Allah to Musa and the proper response of faith, affirmation, and submission without metaphorical interpretation.

Core Idea
Allah's speech to Musa is literal and emphatically affirmed, not metaphorical.

This creedal passage from the Tahawiyyah establishes a key belief about Allah's attribute of speech. It affirms that Allah spoke directly to Musa (peace be upon him) and emphasizes that this speech is literal, not metaphorical. The passage also teaches the correct attitude of believers: firm faith, necessary affirmation, and complete submission to Allah's descriptions without resorting to allegorical interpretation (ta'wil). Let's explore how the author explains this.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Notice the emphatic construction 'تكليما' and the list of three responses: إيمانًا, تصديقًا, تسليمًا.
The passage uses a very direct style typical of creedal statements.
2
Identify the three affirmations
Find the three words: إيمانًا (faith), تصديقًا (affirmation), تسليمًا (submission). Understand that they represent the proper response to Allah's descriptions of Himself.
Each is an infinitive that emphasizes the action.
3
Understand the reason for the emphatic infinitive
The text says the emphatic infinitive 'تكليما' is brought to repel interpreting the speech as metaphorical (مجاز). This shows the importance of taking Allah's speech literally.
This guards against both anthropomorphism and excessive figurative interpretation.
4
Reflect on the rejection of ta'wil
The passage ends by declaring transcendence above impossible attributes like human emotions or speech requiring letters and sounds. This maintains God's transcendence while affirming the reality of His speech.
Ta'wil is rejected when it changes the apparent meaning without clear evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَنَقُولُ: إِنَّ اللهَ اتَّخَذَ إِبْرَاهِيمَ خَلِيلًا وَكَلَّمَ مُوسَى تَكْلِيمًا إِيمَانًا وَتَصْدِيقًا وَتَسْلِيمًا. (ونقول: إن الله) قد اتخذ إبراهيم خليلا وكلم موسى تكليما، أتي بالمصدر المؤكد لدفع حمل الكلام على المجاز كما نص في كتابه تعالى تنويها في شأنهما وتعليما؛ فنؤمن أنه موصوف بذلك على المعنى الذي أراده (إيمانًا) ثابتا (و) نصدق به تصديقا لازما (و) نسلم بجميع ما وصف به ذاته العلية في كتابه أو على لسان نبيه (تسليما) خالصا عن التأويل، وننزهه عما يستحيل في حقه من ميل القلب وعطفه والكلام الذي هو بالآلة من الحرف والصوت وغير ذلك.
And we say: Indeed Allah took Ibrahim as a close friend (khalil) and spoke to Musa directly with a speech (takliman) – as an act of faith, affirmation, and submission. (And we say: Indeed Allah) has taken Ibrahim as a friend and spoken to Musa with a speech, bringing the emphatic infinitive to repel interpreting the speech as metaphorical, as He stated in His noble book as an honor for them both and as a teaching. So we believe that He is described with that in the meaning that He intended – a firm faith – and we affirm it with a necessary affirmation, and we submit to all that He described His exalted essence with in His book or upon the tongue of His prophet – a submission free from interpretive alteration (ta'wil) – and we declare Him transcendent above what is impossible for Him, such as inclination of the heart and affection, and speech that is by means of a tool consisting of letters and sound and the like.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a creedal affirmation and its explanation. The core statement: we say that Allah took Ibrahim as khalil (close friend) and spoke to Musa directly (takliman). The emphatic infinitive is used to prevent metaphorical interpretation. The author then explains that we believe it in the sense Allah intended, with firm faith and necessary affirmation. Then he adds that we submit to all descriptions of Allah's essence without ta'wil (allegorical interpretation) and we declare God transcendent above anything impossible for Him, such as human-like emotions or speech that requires bodily organs, letters, and sounds. This guards against both anthropomorphism and metaphorical reduction.

Key Terms
خليل
تكليما
مجاز
تأويل
الحرف
الصوت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the emphatic infinitive is merely rhetorical or that Allah's speech to Musa could be interpreted metaphorically.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that the emphatic infinitive is brought to repel interpreting the speech as metaphorical, thus affirming its literal reality while maintaining transcendence.

Checkpoint
Why is the emphatic infinitive 'تكليما' used in the Qur'an regarding Musa?
A) To indicate quantity.
B) To repel metaphorical interpretation.
C) To show duration.
D) To emphasize the voice.

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech to Musa is literal and emphatically affirmed, and our response must be firm faith, necessary affirmation, and submission free from ta'wil.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah spoke to Musa directly, do you truly believe it is literal, or does your heart harbor doubts that it might be metaphorical? What would change in your reverence for Allah's speech if you settled on literal belief?
?
The passage calls for 'submission free from ta'wil'. Is there any attribute of Allah that you are tempted to reinterpret because it makes you uncomfortable? What is it, and why do you resist full submission?
?
If you were to stand before Allah and He asked you about your belief in His speech to Musa, could you say with certainty that you affirmed it with faith, affirmation, and submission, or is there hesitation? What step do you need to take today to strengthen that conviction?

Can Internal Speech Be Heard? Ash'ari vs. Maturidi
Disagreement on whether internal speech is heard, with Ash'ari and Maturidi positions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the disagreement between Ash'ari and Maturidi on whether internal speech (al-kalam al-nafsi) is something that can be heard, and the reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
Hearing internal speech: Ash'ari says yes by analogy; Maturidi says no, hearing requires sound.

This lesson examines a key dispute in Islamic theology about the nature of divine speech. The question is: when the Qur'an mentions that Prophet Musa heard the speech of Allah, what exactly did he hear? Was it the eternal internal speech itself, or was it a sound that pointed to that speech? The two major Sunni theological schools, Ash'ari and Maturidi, gave different answers, and the author of al-Musayara weighs in.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
Read the opening sentence which sets up the disagreement: Is the heard thing (al-masmu') the internal speech (al-kalam al-nafsi) or that which indicates it?
2
Examine Ash'ari's position
Ash'ari argues that internal speech can be heard, using an analogy: just as we can conceive seeing something without color or body, we can conceive hearing something without sound.
This is a rational analogy (qiyas) extending the realm of possibility.
3
Examine Maturidi's position
Maturidi rejects this, saying hearing without sound is impossible. For him, Musa heard a sound that indicated Allah's internal speech, and this is why Musa is called al-Kalim (the one spoken to directly).
The author finds Maturidi's view more appropriate (awjah).
4
Understand the author's reasoning
The author explains that the term 'hearing' is specifically for sound perception; perception of non-sound might be called 'seeing' or simply 'knowledge'. This linguistic precision supports Maturidi.
This shows how careful definition of terms shapes theological conclusions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد اختلف في أن المسموع هل هو الكلام النفسي أو ما يدل عليه، قال في المسايرة: «قال الإمام الأشعري الكلام النفسي مما يسمع، قاسه على رؤية ما ليس بلون؛ فكما عقل رؤية ما ليس بلون ولا جسم فليعقل سماع ما ليس بصوت واستحال الماتريدي سماع ما ليس بصوت، وعنده سمع موسى عليه السلام صوتاً دالا على كلام الله تعالى وخص به أعني باسم الكليم لأنه بغير واسطة الكتاب والملك، وهو أوجه؛ لأن المخصوص باسم السمع من العِلم ما يكون إدراك صوت وإدراك ما ليس بصوت قد يخص باسم الرؤية، وقد يكون له الاسم الأعم؛ أعني العلم مطلقا» (۱) أي عن التقييد بمتعلق خاص. ثم قال: (وبعد اتفاق أهل السنة على أنه تعالى متكلم لم يزل متكلما به اختلفوا في أنه تعالى هل هو مكلم لم يزل مكلما ؟ فعن الأشعري: نعم، وعن بعض أهل السنة، ونقله بعض متكلمي الحنفية عن أكثرهم: لا، وهو عندي حسن؛ فإن معنى المكلمية لا يراد به هنا نفس الخطاب الذي (۱) المسايرة بشرح محمد محيي الدين ص (٣٣-٣٤).
And there is disagreement concerning that which is heard: is it the internal speech (al-kalam al-nafsi) or that which indicates it? He said in al-Musayara: 'Imam al-Ash'ari said that internal speech is something that is heard, drawing an analogy to seeing that which is not a color; just as one can rationally conceive seeing what is not a color and not a body, so too can one conceive hearing what is not a sound. Al-Maturidi deemed hearing what is not a sound impossible, and according to him Musa, peace be upon him, heard a sound indicating the speech of Allah Most High, and he was distinguished thereby – meaning by the name al-Kalim – because it was without the intermediary of a book or an angel, and this view is more appropriate (awjah); because that which is specifically called hearing (sam') from among the modes of knowledge is the perception of sound, and perception of what is not a sound may be specifically called seeing (ru'ya), and it may have the more general name, meaning knowledge absolutely.' (1) i.e., free from restriction to a particular object. Then he said: 'And after the Ahl al-Sunna unanimously agree that He, Most High, is a speaker (mutakallim) and has never ceased to be a speaker, they differed concerning whether He, Most High, is one who speaks (mukallim) and has never ceased to be one who speaks? It is reported from al-Ash'ari: yes, and from some of the Ahl al-Sunna – and some Hanafite theologians transmitted it from the majority of them –: no, and in my view this is good; for the meaning of being "one who speaks" (mukallimiyyah) is not intended here as the very address (khitab) which... (1) al-Musayara, commentary of Muhammad Muhyi al-Din, pp. 33-34.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a theological discussion about the nature of God's speech as heard by Musa. It begins by noting the disagreement: is the heard thing the internal speech (kalam nafsi) itself or something that indicates it? The author quotes al-Musayara, where Imam al-Ash'ari holds that internal speech can be heard, drawing an analogy to seeing something that is not a color. Al-Maturidi rejects hearing what is not a sound; for him, Musa heard a sound that indicates God's speech. The author finds the Maturidi view stronger (awjah), because the term 'hearing' specifically applies to sound, while perception of non-sound would be called 'seeing' or simply 'knowledge'. Then a second disagreement: after the consensus that God is eternally speaking (mutakallim), is He also eternally 'mukallim' (one who speaks to someone)? Ash'ari says yes, while some Hanafites say no, and the author favors the latter, because the meaning of mukallimiyyah here is not the same as actual address (khitab). The text cuts off at 'الخطاب الذي', but the overall argument is clear.

Key Terms
الكلام النفسي
المسموع
الماتريدي
الأشعري
الكليم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that internal speech cannot be heard at all, considering it purely mental.
Correction: Ash'ari argues that internal speech can be heard, not as sound, but as an object of perception analogous to seeing a non-color. The debate is about the definition of 'hearing'.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did al-Maturidi reject Ash'ari's view that internal speech can be heard?
A) Because internal speech is metaphorical.
B) Because hearing requires a sound.
C) Because Musa heard directly without medium.
D) Because internal speech is not real.

Key Takeaway
The key issue is whether 'hearing' is defined strictly as perception of sound or more broadly; Maturidi's narrow definition prevails according to the author.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you hear only the sound of your own voice, or do you perceive the internal speech of Allah behind it? What would change in your heart if you truly heard His words as Musa did?
?
Are you satisfied with a superficial hearing of the Quran, or do you long for the deeper understanding that comes from knowing that the speech you recite is not just sound but the eternal attribute of Allah? Ask yourself: am I content with the shell, or do I seek the kernel?
?
The author sides with Maturidi, saying hearing is specifically perception of sound. Does this narrow definition make you more careful about how you listen to the Quran? Will you now strive to hear not just the audible recitation but also the intended meaning as divine internal speech?

Eternal or Contingent? The Attribute of Being Mukallim
Debate on whether Allah is eternally mukallim (one who addresses) after consensus on mutakallim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the disagreement among Sunni theologians on whether Allah is eternally mukallim (one who addresses another), and the reasoning behind each view.

Core Idea
Allah is eternally speaking (mutakallim), but being mukallim (addressing others) may be contingent on the existence of others.

After establishing that Allah is eternally mutakallim (speaker), theologians debated whether He is also eternally mukallim (one who speaks to someone). Is the attribute of addressing others intrinsic or does it depend on the existence of creatures? This passage presents the two positions and the author's preference, based on the meaning of the term 'mukallim'.

Guided Path
1
Note the consensus and the point of disagreement
The passage begins by stating that Ahl al-Sunna agree Allah is eternally mutakallim (speaker). The new question is whether He is also eternally mukallim (one who speaks to others).
This shows the precision of theological terms: mutakallim vs mukallim.
2
Identify the two positions
Ash'ari is reported to say yes (Allah is eternally mukallim), while some Hanafite theologians and a majority of Ahl al-Sunna say no.
The author finds the 'no' view good (hasan).
3
Understand the author's reasoning
The author explains that the meaning of 'mukallimiyyah' (being one who speaks to someone) is not the same as the actual address (khitab). This suggests that while Allah's attribute of speech is eternal, the act of addressing (and thus being mukallim) may be temporal.
The passage cuts off, but the reasoning is that mukallim implies a recipient.

Source Text

?

Affirmation of Divine Speech and Ibrahim's Khalil
The author affirms literal divine speech and refutes metaphorical interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ahl al-Sunna affirm that Allah literally spoke to Musa and how the Qur'anic use of the emphatic verbal noun refutes metaphorical interpretation.

Core Idea
Allah's speech to Musa is real and not metaphorical, as emphasized by the emphatic verbal noun.

In this passage, the author states a core Sunni belief: Allah took Ibrahim as a close friend and spoke to Musa directly. The Qur'an uses an emphatic verbal noun to block any attempt to interpret this speech figuratively. The author also instructs us to submit to all divine attributes without distorting interpretation (tawil) and to declare Allah transcendent above any anthropomorphic qualities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Focus on the overall meaning: the affirmation of two specific acts of Allah towards prophets.
Notice the emphatic verbal noun 'تكليماً' at the end.
2
Identify the linguistic tool
Find the phrase 'بالمصدر المؤكد' and understand its purpose: it is used to repel any interpretation of the speech as metaphorical (majaz). This is key to the lesson.
The masdar mu'akkad removes ambiguity.
3
Understand the response required from us
Note the three actions: faith (iman), affirmation (tasdiq), and submission (taslim). Also note the declaration of transcendence (tanzih) from impossible attributes like physical inclination or sound-based speech.
These actions show the proper Sunni stance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَنَقُولُ: إِنَّ اللهَ اتَّخَذَ إِبْرَاهِيمَ خَلِيلًا وَكَلَّمَ مُوسَى تَكْلِمًا إِيمَانًا وَتَصْدِيقًا وَتَسْلِيمًا. (ونقول: إن الله) قد اتخذ إبراهيم خليلا وكلم موسى تكليما)، أتي بالمصدر المؤكد لدفع حمل الكلام على المجاز كما نص في كتابه تعالى تنويها في شأنهما وتعليما؛ فنؤمن أنه موصوف بذلك على المعنى الذي أراده (إيمانًا) ثابتا (و) نصدق به تصديقا لازما . (و) نسلم بجميع ما وصف به ذاته العلية في كتابه أو على لسان نبيه (تسليما) خالصا عن التأويل، وننزهه عما يستحيل في حقه من ميل القلب وعطفه والكلام الذي هو بالآلة من الحرف والصوت وغير ذلك.
And we say: Indeed Allah took Ibrahim as a close friend and spoke to Musa with speech, as faith, affirmation, and submission. (And we say: Indeed Allah) took Ibrahim as a close friend and spoke to Musa with speech); the emphatic verbal noun was brought to repel the interpretation of the speech as metaphorical, as He decreed in His exalted Book, as an honor for them and a teaching. So we believe that He is described with that according to the meaning He intended, with firm faith, and we affirm it with necessary affirmation, and we submit to all that He described His lofty Essence with in His Book or upon the tongue of His Prophet, with a submission free from interpretation, and we declare Him transcendent of what is impossible for Him, such as inclination of the heart and affection, and speech that is by means of the instrument of letters and sound and other than that.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal affirmation and explanation. The author states the Ahl al-Sunna position: we say that Allah took Ibrahim as a close friend (khalil) and spoke to Musa directly (takleem). The use of the emphatic verbal noun (masdar mu'akkad) 'تكليماً' is to prevent interpreting this divine speech figuratively (majaz). The author explains that this emphatic form is used in the Qur'an to honor both prophets and to teach us. We believe (iman) that Allah is truly described with these attributes in the meaning He intended, we affirm (tasdiq) it necessarily, and we submit (tasleem) to all of Allah's self-descriptions in the Qur'an and Sunnah without tawil (interpretative distortion). Furthermore, we declare Allah transcendent (nunazzihu) from anything impossible for Him, such as emotional inclination or affection (miall qalb) and speech that involves physical instruments, letters, or sounds. The passage thus affirms the reality of divine speech without anthropomorphism.

Key Terms
خليل
تكليما
مصدر مؤكد
مجاز
تأويل
تنزيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The belief that Allah's speech to Musa might be metaphorical or created.
Correction: The emphatic verbal noun in the Qur'an ('تكليماً') explicitly removes the possibility of metaphorical interpretation, affirming that Allah's speech is real and not like human speech.

Checkpoint
Why is the masdar mu'akkad (تكليماً) used in the statement?
A) To indicate that the speech is created.
B) To deny that it is metaphorical.
C) To show that Musa heard a voice.
D) To emphasize the action but allow for figurative interpretation.

Key Takeaway
The Ahl al-Sunna affirm Allah's literal speech to Musa, reject metaphorical interpretation through the emphatic verbal noun, and maintain transcendence from physical attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah spoke to Musa with real speech, does your heart truly accept that Allah's speech is unlike any sound you've ever heard? Are you willing to submit to that mystery without trying to imagine it?
?
The author says we must submit without interpretation (taslim). Is there an attribute of Allah that you have struggled to accept literally? What would it cost you to simply submit?
?
If you truly believed that Allah's speech is real and direct to Musa, how would that change the way you listen to the Quran today? What would it mean for your relationship with Allah if you felt He is speaking to you through it?

Dispute on Hearing the Eternal Speech
Reports the Ash'ari-Maturidi disagreement on hearing kalam nafsi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari-Maturidi disagreement on whether Allah's internal speech (kalam nafsi) can be heard by prophets, and the reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
Hearing Allah's eternal speech is either direct perception of meaning or indirect hearing of a sound.

In classical Sunni theology, one of the debated issues is whether the prophets, particularly Musa (AS), heard Allah's eternal internal speech itself or only a created sound that indicated it. Imam al-Ash'ari and Imam al-Maturidi held different views, and understanding their reasoning clarifies the nature of divine speech and its relation to creation. This lesson presents the argument from al-Musayara and the author's preference.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins by stating the disagreement.
2
Identify the two positions
The passage presents Ash'ari's view that kalam nafsi can be heard, and Maturidi's view that only a sound is heard. Find the reasoning for each.
Ash'ari uses an analogy with sight.
3
Understand the author's preference
The author finds the Maturidi view more correct and explains why 'hearing' is specific to sound.
He says the perception of what is not sound would be called 'seeing' or 'knowledge'.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this affects our understanding of Musa hearing Allah at Sinai – was it the eternal speech or a created sound?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد اختلف في أن المسموع هل هو الكلام النفسي أو ما يدل عليه، قال في المسايرة: «قال الإمام الأشعري الكلام النفسي مما يسمع، قاسه على رؤية ما ليس بلون؛ فكما عقل رؤية ما ليس بلون ولا جسم فليعقل سماع ما ليس بصوت واستحال الماتريدي سماع ما ليس بصوت، وعنده سمع موسى عليه السلام صوتاً دالا على كلام الله تعالى وخص به أعني باسم الكليم لأنه بغير واسطة الكتاب والملك، وهو أوجه؛ لأن المخصوص باسم السمع من العِلم ما يكون إدراك صوت وإدراك ما ليس بصوت قد يخص باسم الرؤية، وقد يكون له الاسم الأعم؛ أعني العلم مطلقا» (۱) أي عن التقييد بمتعلق خاص. ثم قال: (وبعد اتفاق أهل السنة على أنه تعالى متكلم لم يزل متكلما به اختلفوا في أنه تعالى هل هو مكلم لم يزل مكلما ؟ فعن الأشعري: نعم، وعن بعض أهل السنة، ونقله بعض متكلمي الحنفية عن أكثرهم: لا، وهو عندي حسن؛ فإن معنى المكلمية لا يراد به هنا نفس الخطاب الذي يتضمنه الأمر والنهي كـ (فَاقْتُلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ) [سورة التوبة آية: ٥]، (لَا تَقْرَبُوا الزنى) [سورة الإسراء آية: ٣٢]؛ لأن معنى الطلب يتضمنه ولا يختلف فيه؛ إذ هو داخل في الكلام القديم، وإنما يراد به إسماع لمعنى اخلع نعليك) [سورة طه آية: ١٢]... وحاصل هـذا عـروض إضافة خاصة للكلام القديم بإسماعه المخصوص (١) بلا واسطة معتادة، ولا شك في انقضاء هذه الإضافة بانقضاء الإسماع؛ فإن أريد به غير هذين الأمرين فليبين حتى يُنظر فيه، والله أعلم (٢) اهـ.
And it was differed concerning whether the heard is the internal speech (kalam nafsi) or that which indicates it. He said in al-Musayara: 'Imam al-Ash'ari said: internal speech is something that can be heard; he analogized it to seeing that which is not a color. For just as one can conceive seeing that which is not a color and not a body, so one can conceive hearing that which is not a sound. And al-Maturidi deemed impossible hearing what is not a sound, and according to him Musa (peace be upon him) heard a sound indicating the speech of Allah Most High, and he was distinguished with the name al-Kalim because it was without the intermediary of the Book or an angel, and this is more correct; because that which is specifically designated by the name 'hearing' from knowledge is the perception of sound, and the perception of what is not sound may be specifically designated by the name 'seeing', and it may have the more general name, meaning knowledge absolutely' (1) i.e., unrestricted by a specific object. Then he said: 'And after the agreement of Ahl al-Sunna that He Most High is Mutakallim (speaker) eternally, they differed concerning whether He Most High is Mukallim (the one who addresses) eternally. From al-Ash'ari: yes, and from some of Ahl al-Sunna, and some Maturidi theologians related it from the majority of them: no, and in my view this is good. For the meaning of mukallimiyya (being the one who addresses) here does not intend the very address which contains command and prohibition, like (kill the polytheists) [Surah al-Tawbah 9:5], (do not approach adultery) [Surah al-Isra' 17:32]; because the meaning of demand is included in it and is not disagreed upon; indeed it is included in the eternal speech. Rather what is intended by it is making hear the meaning of (take off your sandals) [Surah Taha 20:12]... The summary of this is the occurrence of a special attribution of the eternal speech by making it heard in a specific manner (1) without the usual intermediary, and there is no doubt that this attribution ceases with the cessation of the making to hear. So if something other than these two matters is intended, let it be clarified so that it may be examined. And Allah knows best (2). End.'
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a report and analysis of two theological disagreements among Ahl al-Sunna. The first disagreement is about whether the eternal internal speech (kalam nafsi) of Allah can be heard by the prophets. The author quotes al-Musayara: Imam al-Ash'ari held that kalam nafsi can be heard, drawing an analogy: just as one can conceive seeing something that is not a color or body (like a mental image), so too one can conceive hearing something that is not a sound (i.e., the eternal speech without letters or voice). Al-Maturidi, however, rejected the possibility of hearing what is not a sound. According to him, Musa (peace be upon him) heard a sound that indicated the speech of Allah. Because Musa heard this directly without an intermediary (book or angel), he was specifically called 'al-Kalim'. The author finds the Maturidi view more correct (أوجه). He explains that the term 'hearing' specifically applies to the perception of sound, whereas perceiving something without sound would more properly be called 'seeing' or, generally, 'knowledge'. The second disagreement is about whether Allah is described as 'Mukallim' (the One who addresses) eternally. After the agreement that Allah is Mutakallim (speaker) eternally, al-Ash'ari said yes, He is Mukallim eternally. But some Hanafi theologians said no, and the author likes this view. He clarifies that the term 'mukallimiyya' here does not refer to the eternal address containing command and prohibition (which is part of the eternal speech and not disputed). Rather, it refers to the temporal act of making someone hear a specific meaning, as in 'Take off your sandals' (Quran 20:12) addressed to Musa. This act of 'making hear' is a special attribution (idafa khassa) of the eternal speech to a particular listener without the usual means (angel or written book). Such an attribution is temporary; it ceases when the hearing ends. If there is another intended meaning, it should be clarified.

Key Terms
كلام نفسي
سماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that all hearing must be of sounds, so Allah's speech cannot be heard at all.
Correction: The passage shows that while al-Maturidi restricts hearing to sounds, al-Ash'ari allows hearing of non-sounds by analogy with sight. The debate is live, but the author sides with the sound-based definition.

Checkpoint
According to the view the author prefers, why is Allah not described as 'mukallim' eternally?
A) Because speech is created.
B) Because 'mukallim' implies a temporal act of making someone hear.
C) Because He never spoke to anyone.
D) Because the Quran is created.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari-Maturidi disagreement centers on whether 'hearing' can apply to non-sounds; the author favors restricting hearing to sounds and thus takes kalam nafsi as inaudible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you ever feel you are 'hearing' Allah directly? How does this lesson challenge that feeling, and what should your heart be focused on instead?
?
If Allah's speech is not heard as sound, how does that affect your understanding of the Qur'an's majesty? Are you willing to adjust your assumptions about how you encounter divine words?
?
This lesson reveals a disagreement among scholars about how we understand divine attributes. Does it humble you to realize that your own categories might not apply to Allah? What category in your thinking about Allah might need refinement?

Dispute on Allah Being Eternally Mukallim
Reports the disagreement on whether Allah is eternally Mukallim and the author's analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the disagreement among Ahl al-Sunna on whether Allah is described as 'Mukallim' (the One who addresses) eternally, and why the author prefers the view that it is temporal.

Core Idea
Allah is eternally Mutakallim (speaker) but His act of addressing (takleem) is temporal.

After establishing that Allah's speech is eternal, theologians debated whether the attribute of being 'Mukallim' (the One who addresses) is also eternal. Imam al-Ash'ari affirmed it, while many Hanafi theologians denied it. The author sides with the latter, explaining that 'mukallimiyya' refers to a temporal act of making someone hear a specific meaning, such as when Allah said to Musa, 'Take off your sandals'. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the second part of the passage focusing on the dispute about Mukallim.
Notice the consensus on Mutakallim first.
2
Identify the two positions
Find al-Ash'ari's view (yes, eternal Mukallim) and the Hanafi majority view (no).
The author says his view is 'good'.
3
Understand the author's clarification
He distinguishes between the eternal address (containing command/prohibition) and the temporal act of making hear a specific meaning.
The example is 'Take off your sandals' to Musa.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The 'special attribution' (idafa khassa) of making hear ceases when the hearing ends, so mukallimiyya is not eternal.
If another meaning is meant, it should be clarified.

Divine Speech: Eternal Commands and Temporal Hearing
Clarification of divine speech encompassing command/prohibition and its special temporal hearing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the divine speech is eternal and includes command and prohibition, while the hearing of that speech is a temporal event that does not affect the eternity of the speech.

Core Idea
Divine speech is eternal; its hearing is temporal.

This passage from the Sharh al-Tahawiyyah clarifies a subtle point about the divine attribute of speech. It affirms that the divine speech includes command and prohibition as part of its eternal nature. But when we speak of hearing that speech—like Musa hearing 'Remove your sandals'—that hearing is a temporal event, not the speech itself. The passage distinguishes between the eternal speech and the temporal attribution of hearing, a key distinction in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the literal translation. Notice the examples and the flow from command/prohibition to the special hearing.
Pay attention to the Quranic citations.
2
Identify the two main points
The passage makes two central claims: (1) divine speech contains command and prohibition as part of its eternal nature, and (2) the hearing of that speech is a special temporal attribution.
3
Understand the key distinction
Reflect on the difference between eternal speech (unchanging) and the temporal act of hearing. The passage emphasizes that the attribution of hearing ends when the hearing ends.
This guards against thinking the speech itself becomes temporal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يتضمنه الأمر والنهي كـ (فَاقْتُلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ) [سورة التوبة آية: ٥]، (لَا تَقْرَبُوا الزنى) [سورة الإسراء آية: ٣٢]؛ لأن معنى الطلب يتضمنه ولا يختلف فيه؛ إذ هو داخل في الكلام القديم، وإنما يراد به إسماع لمعنى اخلع نعليك) [سورة طه آية: ١٢]... وحاصل هذا عروض إضافة خاصة للكلام القديم بإسماعه المخصوص بلا واسطة معتادة، ولا شك في انقضاء هذه الإضافة بانقضاء الإسماع؛ فإن أريد به غير هذين الأمرين فليبين حتى يُنظر فيه، والله أعلم.
It [the divine speech] contains command and prohibition, such as (Kill the polytheists) [Surah at-Tawbah: 5], (Do not approach fornication) [Surah al-Isra: 32]; because the meaning of demand (talab) is included in it and there is no difference regarding it; for it is part of the eternal speech. Rather, what is intended by it is the hearing of the meaning of 'Remove your sandals' [Surah Taha: 12]... The summary of this is that it is the occurrence of a special attribution of the eternal speech by hearing it in a specific manner without the customary medium, and there is no doubt that this attribution ends with the ending of the hearing. So if something other than these two matters is intended, let it be clarified so that it can be considered. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a clarification of a specific point regarding the divine attribute of speech. It begins by stating that the divine speech includes command and prohibition, citing Quranic verses as examples: 'Kill the polytheists' and 'Do not approach fornication'. It argues that the meaning of 'demand' (talab) is inherent in this speech and that there is no disagreement about it being part of the eternal speech. The passage then addresses a particular case: the hearing of the meaning (samā‘) not through ordinary means, illustrated by Allah's words to Musa 'Remove your sandals'. The conclusion is that this hearing is a special attribution (idāfa khāṣṣa) of the eternal speech which occurs temporally and ends when the hearing ends. The passage warns that if anyone intends something other than these two matters (i.e., command and prohibition or the specific attribution), they must clarify to be considered. This guards against the misunderstanding that the eternal speech itself becomes temporal, whereas it is only the attribution of hearing that is temporal.

Key Terms
الأمر والنهي
الطلب
الكلام القديم
الإسماع
الإضافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the divine speech itself becomes temporal when heard.
Correction: The passage clarifies that it is only a temporal attribution of hearing, not the speech itself.

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about the hearing of the divine speech?
A) It is identical to the eternal speech.
B) It is a special attribution that ends when hearing ends.
C) It is a created entity.
D) It is only for prophets.

Key Takeaway
The divine speech is eternal and includes command/prohibition; its hearing is a temporal attribution that ends when the hearing ends.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the commands of Allah are eternal, what does it mean for your hesitation to obey them? In what area of your life are you delaying a divine command that you know is as real and present today as it was when revealed?
?
When you hear or recite the Quran, you are experiencing a temporal hearing of the eternal speech. Does this awareness change how you listen to it? If not, what is holding you back from this awe?
?
The special hearing granted to Musa (عليه السلام) without a medium was unique. But you still hear Allah's words through revelation. How should this affect your reverence for the Quran? Are you treating it as an ordinary book or as the speech of the One whose words are eternal?

Prohibitions and Affirmation of Quran as Uncreated Speech
Prohibits three actions and affirms Quran as uncreated speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three prohibitions concerning Allah's essence, disputation, and arguing about the Quran, and the belief that the Quran is Allah's uncreated speech.

Core Idea
Do not delve, dispute, or argue; affirm the Quran as Allah's uncreated speech.

This lesson presents the foundational principle of avoiding theological speculation and debate. Imam al-Tahawi instructs believers to refrain from discussing Allah's essence, disputing in religion, and arguing about the Quran, and instead to affirm the Quran as the speech of Allah revealed to Prophet Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the three prohibitions (لا نخوض، لا نماري، لا نجادل) and the affirmation (نعلم أنه كلام رب العالمين).
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the three prohibitions
Find each prohibition: not delving into Allah, not disputing in religion, not arguing about the Quran. Reflect on why each is forbidden.
3
Understand the affirmation about the Quran
The passage states that the Quran is Allah's speech, revealed by Jibril to Prophet Muhammad, and that it is incomparable to created speech.
This affirms the Quran as uncreated and eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا نَخُوضُ فِي اللهِ وَلَا تُمَارِي فِي دِينِ اللهِ تَعَالَى وَلَا تُجَادِلُ فِي القُرْآنِ، وَنَعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ كَلامُ رَبِّ العَالَمِينَ نَزَلَ بِهِ الرُّوحُ الأَمِينُ فَعَلَّمَهُ سَيِّدَ المُرْسَلِينَ مُحَمَّدًا صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَعَلَى آلِهِ وَصَحْبِهِ أَجْمَعِينَ، وَكَلَامُ الله تَعَالَى لَا يُسَاوِيهِ شَيْءٌ مِنْ كَلَامِ المَخْلُوقِينَ. مما يجب علينا أننا لا نخوض في ذات الله تعالى؛ روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه قال: «لا ينبغي لأحد أن ينطق في ذات الله بشيء بل يصفه بما وصف به نفسه. ولا نماري أي لا نداهن وهي عدم المبالاة في دين الله تعالى، ولا نجادل أحدًا في القرآن العظيم؛ بل نعتقد ونعلم أنه كلام رب العالمين نزل به جبرائيل الروح الأمين فعلمه سيد الأنبياء والمرسلين نبينا محمدا صلى الله عليه وعلى آله الأكرمين وصحبه أجمعين؛ روي عن أبي يوسف أنه قال: كنت عند أبي حنيفة إذ دخل عليه جماعة في أيديهم رجلان فقالوا: إن أحد هذين يقول : إن القرآن مخلوق والآخر ينازعه ويقول: القرآن غير مخلوق؛ فقال : لا تصلوا خلفهما، فقلت: أما الذي يقول القرآن مخلوق فنعم؛ لأنه لا يقول بقدم القرآن، وأما الآخر فما باله لا يصلى خلفه؟ قال: إنهما تنازعا في الدين والمنازعة في الدين بدعة. و كلام الله تعالى لا يساويه ولا يشبهه شيء من كلام المخلوقين؛ لأنه صفة من صفات رب العالمين، وقد تقدم لك أن من شَبَّه من صفات الله بشيء من صفات المخلوقين كان من الكافرين.
And we do not delve into Allah, nor do we dispute in the religion of Allah Most High, nor do we argue about the Quran, and we know that it is the speech of the Lord of the worlds, the Trustworthy Spirit brought it down and taught it to the master of messengers Muhammad (may Allah bless him and his family and all his companions), and the speech of Allah Most High nothing of the speech of created beings equals it. It is obligatory upon us that we do not delve into the essence of Allah Most High; it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he said: 'No one should speak about the essence of Allah with anything, but rather describe Him as He described Himself.' And we do not dispute—i.e., we do not be false, which is lack of concern—in the religion of Allah Most High, nor do we argue with anyone about the Mighty Quran; rather we believe and know that it is the speech of the Lord of the worlds, Jibril (the Trustworthy Spirit) brought it down and taught it to the master of the prophets and messengers, our Prophet Muhammad (may Allah bless him and his noble family and all his companions); it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he said: I was with Abu Hanifa when a group entered upon them with two men, and they said: One of these two says the Quran is created, and the other disputes him and says the Quran is uncreated. He said: Do not pray behind them. I said: As for the one who says the Quran is created, yes (that is clear), because he does not say the Quran is eternal; but as for the other, why should one not pray behind him? He said: They both disputed in the religion, and disputation in the religion is bid'ah. And the speech of Allah Most High nothing of the speech of created beings equals or resembles it, because it is an attribute of the attributes of the Lord of the worlds, and it has preceded for you that whoever likens any of the attributes of Allah to anything of the attributes of created beings is among the disbelievers.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage addresses three prohibitions: not delving into the essence of Allah, not disputing in the religion, and not arguing about the Quran. It then affirms the Quran as the speech of Allah revealed by Jibril to Prophet Muhammad, and that it is incomparable to created speech. The commentary provides reports from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf illustrating the prohibition of disputation: Abu Hanifa states that one should not speak about Allah's essence beyond what He describes Himself. The narration from Abu Yusuf shows that both disputing parties in the issue of Quran's creation are considered to have committed bid'ah, and thus one should not pray behind them. The passage concludes by reaffirming that the Quran is not similar to created speech, and likening Allah's attributes to creatures is disbelief.

الخوض في الله
المماراة
المجادلة في القرآن
كلام الله

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that discussing Allah's essence is permissible if done respectfully, but the tradition prohibits it entirely.
Correction: The passage explicitly forbids 'khawd' (delving) into Allah, meaning any speculation beyond what He describes Himself.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT prohibited?
A) Delving into Allah
B) Disputing in religion
C) Arguing about the Quran
D) Seeking knowledge about Allah's attributes through revelation

Key Takeaway
We must avoid speculating about Allah, disputing in religion, and arguing about the Quran; rather, we affirm the Quran as Allah's uncreated speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a recent conversation where you debated a religious topic. Was your intention to seek truth or to win the argument? How does this passage call you to change your approach?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly believe you are uttering the uncreated speech of Allah, or does it feel like any other text? What would change in your heart if you fully internalized this truth?
?
Have you ever caught yourself speculating about Allah's essence or attributes beyond what is revealed? Will you commit to stopping such thoughts and instead focusing on what He has taught us?

Prohibition of Delving into Allah's Essence
Prohibits delving into Allah's essence with evidence from Abu Hanifa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why it is forbidden to speak about Allah's essence beyond what He describes Himself, as reported from Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Describe Allah only as He describes Himself.

Imam al-Tahawi emphasizes that we must not delve into Allah's essence. The passage includes a narration from Abu Hanifa that prohibits speaking about Allah's essence with anything beyond His self-description. This teaches profound respect and limits theological speculation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the phrase 'لا ينبغي لأحد أن ينطق في ذات الله بشيء'.
2
Understand the quote from Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa forbids speaking about Allah's essence except with what Allah has described Himself. This is a principle of tanzih.
This is a strong restriction.
3
Reflect on the principle
Think about why the early scholars set this boundary. It preserves divine transcendence and avoids anthropomorphism.

Prohibition of Disputation about the Quran and the Story of Abu Yusuf
Prohibits disputation and narrates a story about avoiding arguments over the Quran's nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why arguing about the Quran is considered innovation (bid'ah) and how the early scholars handled disputes about the Quran being created or uncreated.

Core Idea
Disputation in religion is bid'ah, even if about the Quran.

Imam al-Tahawi forbids arguing about the Quran and provides a vivid narration from Abu Yusuf about a dispute concerning whether the Quran is created or uncreated. Abu Hanifa declared that praying behind both disputants is invalid because disputation is bid'ah. This teaches the importance of avoiding theological arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the definition of 'mumara' (disputation) as lack of concern.
2
Understand the story of the two men
Two men disputed about the Quran being created or uncreated. Abu Hanifa forbade praying behind both because they engaged in disputation.
Note that both positions (created and uncreated) were considered problematic due to the argument itself.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends by reaffirming that the Quran is incomparable to created speech and that likening Allah's attributes to creation is disbelief.

?

?

?
Are you willing to refrain from debating about the Quran or other theological topics, even if you feel you have the correct understanding? What does your willingness (or unwillingness) say about your attachment to being seen as knowledgeable?
