The Quran Uncreated and Following the Community
Imam Maydani affirms the Quran's uncreatedness and argues for following the Muslim community.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran is considered uncreated and how the obligation to follow the Muslim community is derived from the Quranic verse and rational argument.

Core Idea
Uncreated Quran, obligatory community: unity of word and unity of flock.

In this lesson, Imam Maydani affirms two foundational Sunni beliefs: the Quran is not created but is the pre-eternal speech of Allah, and it is obligatory to adhere to the majority community of Muslims (Ahl al-Sunnah). The second point is supported by a careful analysis of Quran 4:115, showing that following any path other than that of the believers is itself a sin, and thus following their path is mandatory.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify affirmations
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the two clear affirmations at the start: 'We do not say the Quran is created' and 'We do not oppose the community.'
These two statements form the main doctrines of this lesson.
2
Understand the reason for uncreatedness
The author explains that creation is an attribute of originated (hādith) and deficient things, while the Quran is the pre-eternal (qadīm) speech of Allah, so it cannot be created.
This is a concise proof from the nature of the Quran.
3
Analyze the Quranic verse and the objection
Read verse 4:115 and the objection that the threat applies to the combination of two actions. Then follow the refutation: if the threat were only for the combination, mentioning 'following another path' would be redundant, like 'eats bread'.
This is a key logical argument for the individual sinfulness of following other paths.
4
Grasp the conclusion on obligation
From the argument, the author concludes that following the path of the believers is obligatory (wājib) because following another path is forbidden, and one of the two must be chosen.
This establishes the authority of the community (ijma').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا نَقُولُ بِخَلْقِ القُرْآنِ، وَلَا نُخَالِفُ جَمَاعَةَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ. ( ولا نقول بخلق القرآن)؛ لأن الخلق صفة المحدّث العديم والقرآن كلام الله قديم. (و) مما يجب علينا أننا لا نخالف جماعة المسلمين) السواد الأعظم أهل السنة والجماعة؛ فإن الله تعالى عصم هذه الأمة عن الاتفاق على الضلالة، فمن خالفها كان ضالًا؛ قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يُشَاقِقِ الرَّسُولَ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا تَبَيَّنَ لَهُ الْهُدَى وَيَتَّبِعْ غَيْرَ سَبِيلِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ نُوَلِهِ مَا تَوَلَّى وَنُصْلِهِ جَهَنَّمَ وَسَاءَتْ مَصِيرًا ﴾ [سورة النساء آية ١١٥]؛ فإن قيل: الوعيد متعلق بالمجموع وهو المشاققة والاتباع، قلنا: بل بكل واحد وإلا لم يكن في ضمه إلى المشاققة فائدة؛ وذلك لأنه تعالى جمع بين مشاققة الرسول واتباع غير سبيل المؤمنين في الوعيد، ولا شك أن مشاققة الرسول وحدها توجب الوعيد، فلولا أن الاتباع المذكور كذلك لم يكن في ضمه إلى المشاققة فائدة وكان الكلام حينئذ ركيكا؛ كما لو قال: من يشاقق الرسول ويأكل الخبز، وإذا كان اتباع غير سبيل المؤمنين حراما، ولا شك أن اتباع سبيل. من السبل واجب؛ لقوله تعالى: (قُلْ هَذِهِ سَبِيلِى ) ... الآية سورة يوسف آية: ١٠٨] ، فيكون الواجب اتباع سبيل المؤمنين، ثم سبيل المؤمنين لا يمكن أن يكون عين ما أتى به النبي ؛ لأنه إذا كان كذلك فاتباع غيره يكون مخالفة
And we do not say that the Quran is created, and we do not oppose the community of Muslims. (And we do not say that the Quran is created) because creation is an attribute of the originated and deficient, and the Quran is the speech of Allah, pre-eternal. (And) from what is obligatory upon us is that we do not oppose the community of Muslims, the great majority (al-sawad al-a'zam), the people of the Sunnah and the community; for Allah, the Exalted, has protected this nation from agreeing upon misguidance, so whoever opposes it is misguided. Allah the Exalted said: 'And whoever opposes the Messenger after guidance has become clear to him and follows other than the path of the believers - We will give him what he has taken and drive him into Hell, and evil is the destination' [Surah al-Nisa, verse 115]. If it is said: The threat is attached to the combination, i.e., opposition and following, we say: Rather it is attached to each one, otherwise there would be no benefit in joining it with opposition; and that is because He, the Exalted, combined opposing the Messenger and following other than the path of the believers in the threat, and there is no doubt that opposing the Messenger alone necessitates the threat. Were it not that the aforementioned following is likewise, there would be no benefit in joining it with opposition, and the speech would then be tasteless; as if He said: 'Whoever opposes the Messenger and eats bread.' And if following other than the path of the believers is forbidden, and there is no doubt that following one of the paths is obligatory due to His saying: 'Say: This is my path' ... the verse [Surah Yusuf, verse 108], then it becomes obligatory to follow the path of the believers. Then the path of the believers cannot be exactly what the Prophet brought; because if it were so, then following other than it would be opposition to the Messenger.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement and a proof. It begins with two affirmations: (1) We do not say the Quran is created, and (2) We do not oppose the community of Muslims. The author explains that creation is an attribute of originated things that are deficient, whereas the Quran is the pre-eternal (qadim) speech of Allah. Then he explains the obligation to follow the community (al-sawad al-a'zam, the great majority of Ahl al-Sunnah) because Allah protects the nation from agreeing on misguidance. He supports this with the verse from Surah al-Nisa (4:115) which threatens those who oppose the Messenger and follow a path other than that of the believers. The author then addresses a potential objection: that the threat in the verse applies only to the combination of both actions. He refutes this by arguing that if the threat applied only to the combination, then following another path would be harmless by itself, making the mention of it redundant (like saying 'whoever opposes the Messenger and eats bread'). Since the verse is not redundant, each action individually incurs the threat. Then he argues that since following a path other than the believers' is haram, it follows that following the believers' path is wajib, citing the verse from Surah Yusuf. Finally, he subtly argues that the believers' path is not exactly identical to what the Prophet brought, because if it were, following anything else would be opposing the Prophet, and the structure of the verse (mentioning both) would still be redundant. This is a classic Ash'ari argument for the authority of the community (ijma').

Key Terms
خلق القرآن
قدم القرآن
جماعة المسلمين
السواد الأعظم
الوعيد
سبيل المؤمنين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the threat in Quran 4:115 applies only to the combination of opposing the Messenger and following another path, so following another path alone is not sinful.
Correction: Imam Maydani argues that if the threat were only for the combination, mentioning 'following another path' would be meaningless; thus both actions individually incur the threat.

Checkpoint
How does Imam Maydani prove that following the path of the believers is individually obligatory from the verse in Surah al-Nisa?
A) By citing a hadith that commands following the majority.
B) By arguing that if the threat only applied to the combination, the mention of following would be redundant.
C) By saying that the verse explicitly states that following the believers is wajib.
D) By using a logical proof from the nature of the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The Quran is uncreated and following the community of Muslims is obligatory; both are protected by divine decree and rational proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a belief held by the vast majority of Muslims over centuries, such as the Quran being uncreated, do you ever feel tempted to doubt it because it seems 'old' or 'non-rational'? What does this passage demand of you in that moment of doubt?
?
This passage equates opposing the community with opposing the Prophet. Have you ever separated yourself from the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah on a matter of belief or practice because of personal reasoning or cultural influence? Are you willing to return, even if it costs you your comfort?
?
The author uses a sharp reductio argument: if following a wrong path were not itself a sin, it would be like eating bread—trivial. Is there any area of your faith where you treat deviations as 'not a big deal'? What would it truly mean to see them as worthy of Hell, as the verse warns?

The Nature of Divine Books as Eternal Speech
Definition of divine books as eternal speech sent down.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunna position on the divine books as the eternal, uncreated speech of Allah, distinct from their temporal physical forms.

Core Idea
Allah's books are His eternal speech, not created in time.

In this lesson, we explore a foundational belief about the revealed books: that their essence is Allah's eternal attribute of speech, far above any physical letters or sounds. The commentator clarifies this distinction to prevent confusion between the divine attribute and its temporal expression in the world.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic sentence carefully, noting the three key affirmations about the books: their eternal nature, their transcendence, and their temporal descent.
The sentence is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two aspects of the books
Notice the commentator distinguishes between the essence of the books (eternal speech) and their manifestation in the world (temporal words on tablets or through angels).
This distinction is crucial against the Mu'tazila.
3
Understand why this matters
Ask yourself: why does it matter that Allah's speech is eternal and not created? This ties into the attribute of kalam and the integrity of revelation.
Connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكُتُبِهِ) بأنها كلام الله تعالى الأزلي القديم المنزه عن الحروف والأصوات، وبأنه تعالى أنزلها على بعض رسله بألفاظ حادثة في ألواح أو على لسان ملك، وبأن جميع ما تضمنته حق وصدق.
And His books: that they are the eternal, pre-eternal speech of Allah Most High, transcendent above letters and sounds, and that He Most High sent them down to some of His messengers with newly-occurring words on tablets or through the tongue of an angel, and that all they contain is true and truthful.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage explains the third pillar: belief in the revealed books. It makes a crucial theological distinction: the essence of the books is the eternal (qadim) speech of Allah, which is an attribute of His essence, free from letters and sounds (i.e., not composed of physical elements). This is the position of Ahl al-Sunna against the Mu'tazila who said the Qur'an is created. However, the actual revelation in the world involves 'alfaz haditha' (newly-occurring words) on physical media like tablets, conveyed by angels. The content is affirmed as absolute truth and sincerity.

Key Terms
كلام الله
أزلي قديم
منزه عن الحروف والأصوات
ألفاظ حادثة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Qur'an as recited is eternal in its letters and sounds.
Correction: The eternal speech of Allah is not composed of letters or sounds; the physical words are temporal expressions of that eternal attribute.

Checkpoint

A) It consists of eternal letters and sounds
B) It is transcendent above letters and sounds
C) It is created in letters and sounds
D) It is neither eternal nor created

Key Takeaway
The divine books are Allah's eternal speech, transcendent above physical elements, yet sent down with temporal words.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Qur'an is Allah's eternal speech, not a created book, how does that change the weight you give to its commands? What area of your life are you treating the Qur'an as optional rather than as the unchangeable word of your Creator?
?
The passage says Allah's speech is transcendent above letters and sounds. When you recite or hear the Qur'an, do you sense that you are encountering something beyond this physical world? If not, what is distracting you from that awe?
?
The content of the books is 'haqq wa sidq' — all truth and truthfulness. In which area of your life do you find yourself doubting or disputing what Allah has revealed? Will you today pick one specific command and submit to it fully, without reservation?

Hanafi and Ash'ari Views on Punishing the Obedient
A footnote explaining Hanafi and Ash'ari views on punishing the obedient.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Hanafi position that punishing the obedient is intrinsically impossible for Allah, and how it differs from the Ash'ari view that it is merely prevented by Allah's promise.

Core Idea
Punishing the obedient contradicts divine wisdom and justice, making it impossible for Allah.

This footnote from al-Musayara contrasts two major theological schools on a key issue: can Allah punish someone who spent their life in obedience? While both agree it will never happen, they differ on why. The Hanafis argue it is inherently impossible, while the Ash'aris say it is only impossible because Allah promised not to. Let's explore the reasoning behind these positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how the author presents the Hanafi view first, then the clarification about occurrence.
Pay attention to the Quranic verse cited as evidence.
2
Identify the Hanafi argument
Find the logical chain: why do the Hanafis say punishing the obedient is impossible? They tie it to the principle that Allah cannot impose obligations beyond capacity (takleef ma la yutaq).
The verse from Surah al-Jathiyah is used to show that such an act is ugly (qabeeh).
3
Distinguish possibility from occurrence
The passage makes a key distinction: possibility (tajweez) versus actual occurrence (wuqoo'). Both schools agree it will never happen, but their reasons differ.
4
Compare Hanafi and Ash'ari reasoning
Note the difference: Ash'aris base the impossibility on Allah's promise (wa'd), while Hanafis add that it is intrinsically ugly and thus impossible for Allah.
This highlights a fundamental difference in how each school views divine attributes and justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ محمد البيطار في الحاشية: تتمة: قال في المسايرة واعلم أن الحنفية لما استحالوا عليه تكليف ما لا يطاق فهم لتعذيب المحسن الذي استغرق عمره في الطاعة مخالفا لهوى نفسه في رضا مولاء أمنع؛ بمعنى أنه يتعالى عن ذلك؛ فهو من باب التنزيهات؛ إذ التسوية بين المسيء والمحسن غير لائق بالحكمة في فطر سائر العقول، وقد نص تعالى على قبحه حيث قال: أم حَسِبَ الَّذِينَ اجْتَرَحُوا السَّيِّئَاتِ أَن تَجْعَلَهُمْ كَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّلِحَتِ سَوَاءً حيَاهُمْ وَمَمَاهُمْ سَاءَ مَا تَحْكُمُونَ ﴾ [سورة الجاثية آية: ٢١) ، فجعله سيئًا. هذا في التجويز عليه وعدمه؛ أما الوقوع فمقطوع بعدمه؛ غير أنه عند الأشاعرة للوعد بخلافه وعند الحنفية وغيرهم لذلك ولقبح خلافه اهـ . انظر: المسايرة بشرح محمد محيي الدين ص (١١١-١١٢).
Sheikh Muhammad al-Bitar said in the margin: Supplement: He said in al-Musayara: And know that the Hanafiyyah, since they deem impossible for Him the obligation of what cannot be borne, they deem impossible for Him the punishment of the benefactor who spent his life in obedience, opposing his own desires for the pleasure of his Master; meaning that He is exalted above that; so it is from the category of declarations of transcendence; for equating the evildoer and the benefactor is not befitting to wisdom in the natural disposition of all intellects, and Allah the Exalted has stated its ugliness where He said: 'Or do those who commit evil deeds think that We will make them like those who believe and do righteous deeds, [in] their life and their death? Evil is that which they judge.?' [Surah al-Jathiyah: 21] so He made it evil. This is regarding the possibility or impossibility of it; as for occurrence, it is definitively non-occurring; except that according to the Ash'aris it is due to the promise being otherwise, and according to the Hanafiyyah and others it is due to that and the ugliness of its opposite. End. See: al-Musayara with commentary of Muhammad Muhyi al-Din, pp. 111-112.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a marginal note (hasheeya) that elaborates on a theological principle. It explains that the Hanafiyyah consider it impossible (mustahil) for Allah to punish an obedient person who spent his life in devotion, because that would be akin to burdening someone beyond capacity (takleef ma la yutaq), which is also impossible for Allah. They argue that such an act is not befitting divine wisdom, and it would be a form of injustice (zulm) which is impossible for Allah. They support this with the Quranic verse condemning the equal treatment of evildoers and believers. The note then clarifies that the discussion is about the possibility (tajweez) or impossibility; as for actual occurrence (wuqoo'), all agree it will never happen. The difference lies in the underlying reason: Ash'aris base it on Allah's promise not to do so, while Hanafis add that it is also intrinsically ugly (qabeeh) and impossible for Allah to do.

Key Terms
استحالة
تكليف ما لا يطاق
تنزيه
حكمة
قبح
وعد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Hanafi and Ash'ari positions are identical, both only relying on Allah's promise.
Correction: The Hanafis argue additionally that punishing the obedient is intrinsically ugly (qabeeh) and impossible for Allah, not just prevented by a promise.

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafiyyah as explained in this footnote, why is it impossible for Allah to punish the obedient?
A) Because Allah promised not to.
B) Because it would contradict divine wisdom and be unjust.
C) Because the obedient never sin.
D) Because punishment is only for disbelievers.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafis hold that punishing the obedient is rationally impossible for Allah due to divine wisdom and justice, while the Ash'aris attribute the impossibility solely to Allah's promise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah cannot punish the obedient because of His wisdom and justice, how does that reshape your understanding of His mercy? Do you truly trust that your efforts in obedience are secure from any divine injustice, or do you still carry a hidden fear that your good deeds might be in vain? Let this certainty free you from anxiety about your standing with Allah.
?
The Hanafis argue that punishing the good is intrinsically evil, and Allah is far above it. Has your heart ever secretly doubted Allah's justice—perhaps when you saw evil people prosper while believers suffered? How does this passage challenge you to align your sense of fairness with Allah's perfect wisdom? Make a firm resolve to never question His justice again.
?
If you believe that Allah will never punish you for your obedience, what then drives your worship? Is it love, gratitude, or fear of punishment? Reflect: Are you content with serving a God whose justice is so profound that it would be impossible for Him to wrong you, even an atom's weight? Let this teaching move you to worship Him solely out of love and reverence, not transactional fear.

The Noble Recording Angels and Their Comprehensive Role
Maydani explains the comprehensive recording of actions by the noble scribing angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the recording angels guard every human action, intentional or not, and that this includes disbelievers.

Core Idea
Every word, groan, and deed is recorded without exception.

Imam Maydani elaborates on the Tahawiyyah's article of faith regarding the noble scribing angels. He emphasizes that their guardianship is all-encompassing, leaving no action unrecorded, whether done intentionally or forgetfully, in health or illness. He cites Imam Malik's explicit statement and the Quranic verse from Surah Qaf to support this comprehensive record.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the first part of the passage focusing on the phrase 'حافظين' and the explanation that follows.
2
Identify the scope of recording
Note that the passage states the angels record everything, even the groan of a sick person, citing Imam Malik.
3
Understand the Quranic evidence
Reflect on the verse from Surah Qaf: every word is observed by a ready observer.
4
Recognize the inclusion of disbelievers
The passage explicitly says the disbelieving servant is included in this recording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونؤمن بـ) الملائكة (الكرام الكاتبين، وأن الله قد جعلهم لأفعال العباد مما لهم وعليهم (حافظين)؛ أي لا يهملون من شأنهم شيئًا فعلوه قصدًا أو ذهولا أو نسيانًا صحةً أو مرضًا؛ قال الإمام مالك: يكتبون على العبد كل شيء حتى أنينه في مرضه؛ محتجاً بإفادة الآية العموم، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿ما يَلْفِظُ مِن قَوْلٍ إِلَّا لَدَيْهِ رَقِيبٌ عَتِيدٌ ﴾ [سورة ق آية: ۱۸]؛ وحينئذ يدخل في العبد الكافر لأنه تضبط أنفاسه وأعماله له أو عليه ; قال النووي: «والصواب الذي عليه المحققون، بل نقل فيه بعضهم الإجماع، أن الكافر إذا فعل أفعالا جميلة كالصدقة وصلة الرحم ثم أسلم ومات على الإسلام أن ثواب عمله يكتب له، أما دعوى مخالفته للقواعد فغير مسلمة .اهـ. :قلت وضابطه كما قاله بعضهم: إذا كانت لا تتوقف على نية. وذكر بعضهم أن المعقبات في قوله تعالى: لَهُ مُعَقِّبَنتُ مِنْ بَيْنِ يَدَيْهِ وَمِنْ خَلْفِهِ مَحفَظُونَهُ مِن أَمر الله) [سورة الرعد آية: (۱۱) غير الكاتبين بلا خلاف، وعن عثمان أنه سأل النبي كم ملكا على الإنسان فذكر عشرين ملكا قال المهدوي في الفيصل: وذكر الآبي أنه يحفظ لابن عطية أن كل آدمي
And we believe in the noble scribing angels, and that Allah has made them guardians of the actions of the servants – what is for them and what is against them; that is, they do not neglect anything of their affair that they did, intentionally or forgetfully or from forgetfulness, in health or illness. Imam Malik said: They write everything for the servant, even his groan in his illness, using the general implication of the verse: 'He does not utter a word except that there is with him an observer ready' [Qaf 50:18]. And then the disbelieving servant is included because his breaths and deeds are recorded for him or against him. Al-Nawawi said: 'The correct view, which is that of the investigators – indeed some have transmitted consensus on it – is that if a disbeliever does beautiful deeds like charity and maintaining family ties, then becomes Muslim and dies upon Islam, the reward of his deed is written for him. As for the claim that it contradicts the principles, it is not conceded.' I say: Its criterion, as some have said, is if they do not depend on intention. And some have mentioned that the mu'aqqibat (those who follow) in the verse 'For him are mu'aqqibat from before him and from behind him, guarding him from the command of Allah' [Ra'd 13:11] are other than the scribes, without disagreement. And from Uthman that he asked the Prophet how many angels are upon a person, and he mentioned twenty angels. Al-Mahdawi said in al-Faysal: And al-Abi said that he preserved from Ibn Atiyyah that every Adamite...
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the foundational creedal statement about belief in the noble scribing angels. It begins by quoting the text of the Tahawiyyah: 'And we believe in the noble scribing angels, and that Allah has made them guardians.' The commentator then explains that 'guardians' means they do not neglect any of the servants' actions, whether done intentionally, forgetfully, unintentionally, in health or illness. He then cites Imam Malik, who said the angels write everything, even the groan of a sick person, based on the general import of the verse in Surah Qaf (50:18) that every word is recorded. This includes the disbelieving servant, as his breaths and deeds are recorded for or against him. Then comes a discussion about the reward of a disbeliever's good deeds upon his later Islam. The commentator quotes Imam Nawawi, who states that the correct view – upon which the investigators agree, and some even claim consensus – is that if a disbeliever performs good deeds such as charity and maintaining family ties, then later becomes Muslim and dies upon Islam, the reward of those deeds is written for him. The objection that this contradicts principles is not conceded. The commentator then adds his own remark: the criterion is that these deeds should not depend on intention (i.e., they are inherently good acts). The passage then mentions that the 'mu'aqqibat' in Surah Ra'd (13:11) are different angels from the scribes, without disagreement. Finally, a report from Uthman is narrated: he asked the Prophet how many angels are on a person, and the Prophet said twenty angels. The passage ends with references to al-Mahdawi and al-Abi preserving from Ibn Atiyyah that every human has twenty angels.

Key Terms
الكرام الكاتبين
الحافظين
الرقيب العتيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only Muslims' deeds are recorded by the angels.
Correction: All deeds, including those of disbelievers, are recorded.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Imam Malik say about what the angels write?
A) Only intentional sins
B) Everything including the groan of a sick person
C) Only good deeds
D) Only words

Key Takeaway
The noble scribing angels record every human action without exception, including disbelievers' deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Knowing that every groan you make in illness is recorded, does it change how you perceive your suffering? How will you use that awareness to seek closeness to Allah in your trials?
?
If every word you speak is recorded by a scribe, what is one specific habit of speech you commit to changing today, starting now?
?
The passage says even your forgetful actions are recorded. How does this truth confront your casual attitude toward sins you commit without thinking? What step will you take to become more mindful?

Ruling on Disbeliever's Good Deeds and Other Angelic Matters
Maydani discusses the reward of disbeliever's good deeds after Islam and distinguishes angelic roles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that a disbeliever's good deeds are rewarded upon embracing Islam, provided they do not depend on intention, and that the mu'aqqibat are distinct from the scribing angels.

Core Idea
Good deeds done before Islam can be rewarded after sincere faith.

In this continuation, Imam Maydani addresses a subtle theological point: the fate of a disbeliever's good deeds such as charity and family ties when he later becomes Muslim. Citing Imam Nawawi, he presents the consensus view that these deeds are rewarded. He also clarifies that the 'mu'aqqibat' mentioned in Surah Ra'd are different angels, and mentions a hadith that each person has twenty angels.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read from 'قال النووي' to the end of the passage.
2
Understand al-Nawawi's ruling
Al-Nawawi states the correct view that a disbeliever's good deeds are rewarded upon embracing Islam.
3
Consider the criterion given by the commentator
The criterion is that the deeds do not depend on intention, meaning they are inherently good.
4
Distinguish between scribes and mu'aqqibat
The passage notes that mu'aqqibat are different angels, not the scribes.
5
Note the hadith about twenty angels
The Prophet informed Uthman that each person has twenty angels.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونؤمن بـ) الملائكة (الكرام الكاتبين، وأن الله قد جعلهم لأفعال العباد مما لهم وعليهم (حافظين)؛ أي لا يهملون من شأنهم شيئًا فعلوه قصدًا أو ذهولا أو نسيانًا صحةً أو مرضًا؛ قال الإمام مالك: يكتبون على العبد كل شيء حتى أنينه في مرضه؛ محتجاً بإفادة الآية العموم، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿ما يَلْفِظُ مِن قَوْلٍ إِلَّا لَدَيْهِ رَقِيبٌ عَتِيدٌ ﴾ [سورة ق آية: ۱۸]؛ وحينئذ يدخل في العبد الكافر لأنه تضبط أنفاسه وأعماله له أو عليه ; قال النووي: «والصواب الذي عليه المحققون، بل نقل فيه بعضهم الإجماع، أن الكافر إذا فعل أفعالا جميلة كالصدقة وصلة الرحم ثم أسلم ومات على الإسلام أن ثواب عمله يكتب له، أما دعوى مخالفته للقواعد فغير مسلمة .اهـ. :قلت وضابطه كما قاله بعضهم: إذا كانت لا تتوقف على نية. وذكر بعضهم أن المعقبات في قوله تعالى: لَهُ مُعَقِّبَنتُ مِنْ بَيْنِ يَدَيْهِ وَمِنْ خَلْفِهِ مَحفَظُونَهُ مِن أَمر الله) [سورة الرعد آية: (۱۱) غير الكاتبين بلا خلاف، وعن عثمان أنه سأل النبي كم ملكا على الإنسان فذكر عشرين ملكا قال المهدوي في الفيصل: وذكر الآبي أنه يحفظ لابن عطية أن كل آدمي
And we believe in the noble scribing angels, and that Allah has made them guardians of the actions of the servants – what is for them and what is against them; that is, they do not neglect anything of their affair that they did, intentionally or forgetfully or from forgetfulness, in health or illness. Imam Malik said: They write everything for the servant, even his groan in his illness, using the general implication of the verse: 'He does not utter a word except that there is with him an observer ready' [Qaf 50:18]. And then the disbelieving servant is included because his breaths and deeds are recorded for him or against him. Al-Nawawi said: 'The correct view, which is that of the investigators – indeed some have transmitted consensus on it – is that if a disbeliever does beautiful deeds like charity and maintaining family ties, then becomes Muslim and dies upon Islam, the reward of his deed is written for him. As for the claim that it contradicts the principles, it is not conceded.' I say: Its criterion, as some have said, is if they do not depend on intention. And some have mentioned that the mu'aqqibat (those who follow) in the verse 'For him are mu'aqqibat from before him and from behind him, guarding him from the command of Allah' [Ra'd 13:11] are other than the scribes, without disagreement. And from Uthman that he asked the Prophet how many angels are upon a person, and he mentioned twenty angels. Al-Mahdawi said in al-Faysal: And al-Abi said that he preserved from Ibn Atiyyah that every Adamite...
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the foundational creedal statement about belief in the noble scribing angels. It begins by quoting the text of the Tahawiyyah: 'And we believe in the noble scribing angels, and that Allah has made them guardians.' The commentator then explains that 'guardians' means they do not neglect any of the servants' actions, whether done intentionally, forgetfully, unintentionally, in health or illness. He then cites Imam Malik, who said the angels write everything, even the groan of a sick person, based on the general import of the verse in Surah Qaf (50:18) that every word is recorded. This includes the disbelieving servant, as his breaths and deeds are recorded for or against him. Then comes a discussion about the reward of a disbeliever's good deeds upon his later Islam. The commentator quotes Imam Nawawi, who states that the correct view – upon which the investigators agree, and some even claim consensus – is that if a disbeliever performs good deeds such as charity and maintaining family ties, then later becomes Muslim and dies upon Islam, the reward of those deeds is written for him. The objection that this contradicts principles is not conceded. The commentator then adds his own remark: the criterion is that these deeds should not depend on intention (i.e., they are inherently good acts). The passage then mentions that the 'mu'aqqibat' in Surah Ra'd (13:11) are different angels from the scribes, without disagreement. Finally, a report from Uthman is narrated: he asked the Prophet how many angels are on a person, and the Prophet said twenty angels. The passage ends with references to al-Mahdawi and al-Abi preserving from Ibn Atiyyah that every human has twenty angels.

المعقبات
الرقيب العتيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A disbeliever's good deeds are never rewarded, even if he later becomes Muslim.
Correction: They are rewarded if he embraces Islam and dies on Islam, provided the deeds do not depend on intention.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the criterion for a disbeliever's good deeds to be rewarded upon embracing Islam?
A) They must be done with intention
B) They must be performed after Islam
C) They must not depend on intention
D) They must be acts of worship

Key Takeaway
A disbeliever's inherently good deeds are rewarded when he embraces Islam, and the mu'aqqibat are distinct from the scribing angels.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever looked down on a non-Muslim's charitable act as worthless? How does this teaching force you to reconsider the value of good deeds regardless of the doer, and what can you learn from it about your own past good deeds before you truly knew Allah?
?
Knowing that the mu'aqqibat angels guard you from dangers while the scribes record your deeds, are you more aware of Allah's constant surveillance and protection? How does this awareness change your response to fear, sin, or gratitude in your daily life?

Belief in the Punishment of the Grave
Maydani affirms the punishment of the grave with Quranic and hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the punishment of the grave is an established belief in Sunni Islam, supported by explicit Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths.

Core Idea
The punishment of the grave is a real, physical reality, confirmed by scripture.

In this lesson, we examine the doctrinal affirmation of the punishment of the grave. Imam Maydani presents direct textual evidence from the Quran and hadith, demonstrating that this belief is not merely a metaphorical concept but a tangible event beginning in the grave. Let's read his arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: first an affirmation, then scriptural proofs. Pay attention to the phrase 'as the verses indicate'.
2
Identify the Quranic evidence
Find the two Quranic verses cited. One mentions 'lower punishment' (Surah al-Sajdah 21) and the other 'exposed to the Fire morning and evening' (Surah Ghafir 46). These are classic proof texts for the punishment of the grave.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
The passage includes two hadiths: the first about testing in graves like the trial of the Dajjal, and the second about two men punished for minor sins (urine and gossip). What do these tell us about the nature and immediacy of the punishment?
The hadith of the two companions shows punishment for seemingly small sins.
4
Reflect on the lesson's core idea
Consider how these proofs affirm a real, bodily punishment in the grave. How does this counter those who deny it?
Connect to the common misunderstanding that the punishment is only metaphorical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) نؤمن بعذاب القبر لمن كان له أي للعذاب (أهلا) كما دلت عليه الآيات؛ كقوله تعالى: (وَلَنُذِيقَنَّهُم مِّنَ الْعَذَابِ الأدنى) [سورة السجدة آية: (۲۱] وقوله: (النَّارُ يُعْرَضُونَ عَلَيْهَا عُدُوا وَعَشِيا ) (سورة غافر آية: ٤٦]، وكذلك الأخبار كقوله : ( أُوحِيَ إِلَيَّ أَنَّكُم تُفتَنُونَ في قُبُورِكُم مِثْلَ أَوْ قَرِيبًا مِنْ فِتْنَةِ الدَّجَّالِ»... الحديث (۳)، وقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في صاحبي القبرين اللذين غرز عليهما الجريدة: «إِنَّها لَيُعذِّبَانِ وَمَا يُعَذِّبَانِ في كَبِيرٍ ، ثم قال: « بَلَى أَمَّا أَحَدُهُمَا فَكَانَ لَا يَسْتَنْزِهُ مِنَ البَولِ وَأَمَّا الْآخَرُ فَكَانَ يَمشِي بِالنَّمِيمَةِ (4) كذا في المسايرة ().
And we believe in the punishment of the grave for whoever deserves it, as the verses indicate, such as His statement (Exalted): 'And We will surely let them taste the lower punishment' [Surah al-Sajdah, verse 21], and His statement: 'The Fire, they are exposed to it morning and evening' [Surah Ghafir, verse 46]. And likewise the traditions, such as his statement: 'It was revealed to me that you will be tested in your graves like or close to the trial of the Dajjal'... the hadith, and his statement (peace be upon him) concerning the two grave companions for whom a palm branch was placed: 'Indeed, they are being punished, and they are not being punished for something great.' Then he said: 'Yes, as for one of them, he used not to protect himself from urine, and as for the other, he used to go about with gossip.' As in al-Masayira.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage affirms the Sunni belief in the punishment of the grave. The author presents three forms of evidence: two Quranic verses and one hadith. The first verse from Surah al-Sajdah (21) speaks of a 'lower punishment' (al-‘adhab al-adna), which is interpreted by scholars as referring to the punishment of the grave. The second verse from Surah Ghafir (46) describes the people of Pharaoh being exposed to the Fire morning and evening, which is understood as occurring in the grave before the Day of Judgment. Then the author cites two hadith: the first is a well-known report that the Prophet (s) was told that his community would be tested in their graves like or close to the trial of the Dajjal. The second is the hadith of the two graves where the Prophet placed a palm branch, saying that the occupants were being punished not for a great sin: one for not cleansing himself from urine, the other for spreading gossip. This hadith is explicit that punishment occurs in the grave. The author concludes by referencing al-Masayara, a commentary on al-Masayira, to confirm this. The passage's purpose is to provide scriptural proof for this article of faith.

الآيات
الأخبار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The punishment of the grave is only spiritual or metaphorical.
Correction: The Quran and hadith cited here indicate a real, physical punishment experienced in the grave, as shown by the explicit verses and the hadith of the two companions being punished for physical sins.

Key Takeaway
The punishment of the grave is a real and immediate consequence for sins, as proven by the Quran and authentic hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Two Types of Human Ability (Istita'a)
Defines two types of istita'a and answers an objection from taklif.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari distinction between two types of human ability and how it resolves the theological objection regarding obligation (taklif).

Core Idea
Ability has two meanings: one with the act, one before it—both needed for taklif.

This passage from the Sharh al-Tahawiyyah explains a key Ash'ari doctrine on human ability (istita'a). It distinguishes between the ability that necessitates action (like divine facilitation) and the ability of health and capacity. This distinction is crucial for understanding why Allah can obligate actions even though the effective power is created only at the moment of action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of istita'a
Read the passage and find the two definitions: one that is with the action and one that is before it. Note the terminology used for each.
The first type is associated with tawfiq, the second with health and capacity.
2
Understand the relationship to action and obligation
Observe how each type relates to the action: the first necessitates the action and is simultaneous; the second is a prerequisite for obligation and precedes the action.
3
Examine the Qur'anic proof
Read the verse cited (2:286) and see how it supports the second type of ability as the basis for obligation.
The verse mentions 'wus'aha' (its capacity), which aligns with the second type.
4
Follow the objection and answer
Understand the opponent's argument that obligation requires ability before the action, and see how the author responds by affirming the second type of ability as capacity, not effective power.
This clarifies why the first type (real power) is not needed before the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالاسْتِطَاعَةُ الَّتِي يَجِبُ بِهَا الفِعْلُ مِنْ نَحْوِ التَّوْفِيقِ الَّذِي لَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يُوصَفَ المَخْلُوقُ بِهَا تَكُونُ مَعَ الفِعْلِ، وَأَمَّا الاسْتِطَاعَةُ مِنَ الصِّحَّةِ وَالوُسْعِ وَالتَّمَكُنِ وَسَلَامَةِ الْآلَاتِ فَهِيَ قَبْلَ الفِعْلِ وَبِهَا يَتَعَلَّقُ الخِطَابُ، وَهُوَ كَمَا قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: ﴿لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا﴾ [سورة البقرة آية: ٢٨٦]. والاستطاعة التي يجب أن يكون بها الفعل من نحو التوفيق الذي لا يجوز أن يوصف المخلوق بها وهي حقيقة القدرة تكون مع الفعل)؛ قال صاحب التبصرة: إنها عرض يخلقه الله في الحيوان يفعل به الأفعال الاختيارية، وهي علة للفعل، والجمهور على أنها شرط لأداء الفعل لا علة. وبالجملة هي صفة يخلقها الله تعالى عند قصد اكتساب الفعل بعد سلامة الأسباب والآلات؛ فإن قصد فعل الخير خلق الله تعالى قدرة فعل الخير، وإن قصد فعل الشر خلق الله قدرة فعل الشر وكان هو المضيع القدرة فعل الخير فيستحق الذم والعقاب؛ ولهذا ذم الله تعالى الكافرين بأنهم لا يستطيعون السمع، وإذا كانت الاستطاعة عرضًا وجب أن تكون مقارنة للفعل بالزمان لا سابقة عليه وإلا لزم وقوع الفعل بلا استطاعة وقدرة عليه لما مر من امتناع بقاء الأعراض. كذا في شرح العقائد. ولما استدل القائلون بكون الاستطاعة قبل الفعل بأن التكاليف قبل الفعل؛ ضرورة أن الكافر مكلف بالإيمان وتارك الصلاة مكلف بها بعد دخول الوقت فلو لم تكن الاستطاعة محققة حينئذ لزم تكليف العاجز وهو باطل - أشار إلى الجواب بقوله: (وأما الاستطاعة من الصحة والوسع والتمكن من الفعل وسلامة الآلات والأسباب فهي قبل الفعل) والحاصل أن القدرة لها إطلاقان؛ فتطلق تارة ويراد بها حقيقة القدرة وهي مع الفعل، وتطلق أخرى ويراد بها الوسع والسلامة وهي قبل الفعل، (وبها) أي الاستطاعة بالمعنى الثاني يتعلق الخطاب والتكليف (وهو كما قال الله تعالى لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا) [سورة البقرة آية : ٢٨٦].
And the ability (al-istitāʿa) by which the action is necessitated, like the tawfīq that it is not permissible for the created to be described with, is with the action. As for the ability of health, capacity, capability, and soundness of limbs, it is before the action, and by it the address is connected. And it is as Allah Most High said: 'Allah does not burden a soul except with its capacity' [Sūrat al-Baqara, 2:286]. And the ability by which the action must occur, like the tawfīq that it is not permissible for the created to be described with, and it is the reality of power, is with the action. The author of al-Tabṣira said: It is an accident (ʿaraḍ) that Allah creates in the living being by which it performs voluntary actions, and it is a cause for the action. The majority hold that it is a condition for performing the action, not a cause. In summary, it is an attribute that Allah Most High creates at the intention of acquiring the action after the soundness of causes and instruments. For if he intends to do good, Allah Most High creates the power to do good; if he intends to do evil, Allah creates the power to do evil—and he is the one who wasted the power to do good, so he deserves blame and punishment. For this reason, Allah Most High blamed the disbelievers that they cannot hear. And if ability is an accident, it must be concurrent with the action in time, not preceding it; otherwise, the action would occur without ability and power over it, because of the previously mentioned impossibility of the subsistence of accidents. So it is in Sharḥ al-ʿAqāʾid. And when those who claim that ability is before the action adduced as proof that obligations are before the action—necessarily the disbeliever is obligated to believe and the one who abandons prayer is obligated to it after the entrance of the time, so if ability were not actual at that time, it would necessitate obligating the incapable, and that is false—he pointed to the answer by his saying: 'As for the ability of health, capacity, capability of the action, and soundness of limbs and causes, it is before the action.' The conclusion is that power (al-qudra) has two applications: sometimes it is used meaning the reality of power, which is with the action; and sometimes it is used meaning capacity and soundness, which is before the action. And by it—that is, ability in the second sense—the address and obligation are connected. And it is as Allah Most High said: 'Allah does not burden a soul except with its capacity' [Sūrat al-Baqara, 2:286].
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage defines two types of ability (istitāʿa) in Ashʿarī theology and answers an objection. The author begins by distinguishing the ability that necessitates action—like tawfīq (divine facilitation)—which cannot be attributed to the created and occurs with the action. The second type is ability in the sense of health, capacity, capability, and soundness of limbs, which precedes the action and is the basis for divine address (khiṭāb) and obligation (taklīf). He quotes Qurʾān 2:286 as proof that obligation is based on capacity (wusʿ), not on the power that necessitates action. Then he elaborates on the first type: the reality of power (ḥaqīqat al-qudra) is an accident (ʿaraḍ) created by Allah in the living being at the moment of intending an action, after the means are sound. It is either a cause or a condition for the action, with the majority deeming it a condition. If one intends good, Allah creates the power for good; if evil, He creates power for evil. The human is then the one who uses or wastes that power, deserving reward or punishment. This explains why Allah blames disbelievers for not being able to hear: they lacked the created power to do good because they intended evil. Since ability is an accident, it cannot subsist and thus must be simultaneous with the action. The objection from opponents is that obligations are before the action, e.g., a disbeliever is obligated to believe now, or a person must pray after time enters, so ability must exist before the action, otherwise it would be obligating the incapable. The author answers that the ability before the action is not the reality of power but rather the capacity and soundness of means (wusʿ wa salāma). Thus, power (qudra) has two senses: (1) the reality of power, simultaneous with the act, and (2) capacity, which precedes the act and is the basis for obligation. He reaffirms the proof from the Qurʾānic verse. This passage clarifies the Ashʿarī position that actual effective ability is created at the moment of action, while obligation rests on the more general ability of health and means.

Key Terms
الاستطاعة
التوفيق
الوسع
التكليف
العرض
حقيقة القدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that ability must exist before the action to justify obligation, so the Ash'ari position seems to obligate the incapable.
Correction: The Ash'aris distinguish between two senses of ability: real power (simultaneous with act) and capacity (before act). Obligation is based on capacity, not real power, so it is valid.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between the ability that is the reality of power (ḥaqīqat al-qudra) and the action?
A) It precedes the action.
B) It is with the action.
C) It is after the action.
D) It is not related to the action.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari doctrine distinguishes between real power (simultaneous with act) and capacity (before act), allowing obligation to be based on capacity while effective power is created at the moment of intention.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly believe that Allah created in you the power to do good at that moment, but you chose to waste it? How does this change the way you view your own excuses for disobedience?
?
This lesson teaches that your intention determines whether Allah creates power for good or evil in you. In the quiet moments of your day, what are you intending? Are you nurturing an intention to obey, or are you leaving your heart open to neglect?
?
You know that obligation is based on capacity (wus'). But what if your capacity is hindered by your own choices—like neglecting prayer until it becomes hard? Are you using your God-given capacity before the act, or are you relying on a false sense that you can always act later? What will you change today to honor the capacity Allah has given you?

The Foundation: Only God Exists by Essence
Al-Kurani establishes the principle that only God exists by essence and attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the foundational principle that only God has existence by essence, and how this entails that all power and perfection belong to Him alone.

Core Idea
Everything other than God is dependent on Him for existence and perfection.

Before we can grasp how human actions relate to divine creation, we must first establish the ultimate reality: only God exists by His own essence. Everything else—including our power—is a gift from Him. Ibrahim al-Kurani begins his treatise by laying this foundation, quoting the Quran and reasoning from the nature of contingency. This lesson unpacks that foundational insight.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the principle of exclusive existence
Read the opening sentence: 'When it is clear that there is no existent by essence except Allah...' Understand that this means all other beings have existence only through Him.
2
Trace the dependency chain
Notice that al-Kurani extends this dependency from existence to perfections, especially power. He uses the Quranic verse 'There is no power except through Allah' to support it.
3
Conclude: no real power but God's
The logical conclusion: if an attribute is acquired from another, it really belongs to that other. So real power is only Allah's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أقول: وقد توسع العارف المثلا إبراهيم الكوراني بأكثر من هذا في رسالته "مسلك الاعتدال إلى فهم آية خلق الأعمال "؛ حيث قال: «إذا تبين أنه لا موجود بالذات إلا الله فلا وجود لغيره إلا به ؛ فما سواه مفتقر إليه في وجوده وكمالاته التابعة لوجوده؛ فكما أنه لا وجود للممكن إلا بالله فكذلك لا كمال وجوديا إلا بالله ومن كمالات العبد القدرة؛ فلا قدرة له إلا بالله كما قال تعالى: (لَا قُوَّةَ إِلَّا بالله) [سورة الكهف آية: (۳۹)، ومن المعلوم أن كل وصف حاصل لشيء بغيره فهو في الحقيقة لذلك الغير لا للشيء؛ فلا قدرة حقيقية إلا الله ... إلى أن قال: «إذا تبين لك توحيد الصفات علمت أن تأثير قدرة العبد بإذن الله لا ينافي قصر الخالقية لكل شيء على الله ؛ لأن العبد لا فعل له إلا بقوة بالضرورة، ولا قوة إلا بالله عقلا ونقلا وكشفًا؛ فلا فعل له إلا بالله، وما هو بالله فهو الله كما تبين؛ فلا فعل حقيقة إلا بالله فمكسوبُ العبد بتأثير قدرته بإذن الله لا بالاستقلال عين المخلوق الله بالعبد؛ فالمخلوق الله بالعباد والمكسوب للعباد بالله متحدان بالذات مختلفان بالاعتبارات لكونه صادرًا من قدرة واحدة بالذات متعددة بالاعتبارات التي هي التعيينات الحاصلة في مظاهر العباد؛ فالله خالق كل شيء على الإطلاق مع إثبات الكسب بالتأثير إلى تخصيص العمومات الدالة على أن الله خالق كل شيء بما عدا الأفعال الاختيارية للمكلفين كما اختاره المحقق ابن الهمام في المسايرة حيث قال:... وساق ملخص عبارته إلى أن قال: وقد علمت أنه لا موجب تحقيقا لتخصيص العمومات»، ثم قال: «هذا ولا حاجة في الجمع بين إثبات الكسب وتوحيد الأفعال إلى تفسير الكسب بتعلق قدرة العبد بالفعل المراد مجردًا عن التأثير أصلا كما هو المشهور عن الأشاعرة؛ لإمكان الجمع بين القول بتأثير قدرة العبد بإذن الله لا بالاستقلال مع القول بتوحيد الأفعال كما تبين وسيزداد وضوحًا بتوفيق المنعم المتعال»، وشيده بالنقول والأقوال وعضده بما نقله عن الأشعري في الإبانة وأطال.
I say: The gnostic, the exemplary, Ibrahim al-Kurani expanded on this in his treatise 'Maslak al-I'tidal ila Fahm Ayat Khalq al-A'mal', where he said: 'When it is clear that there is no existent by essence except Allah, then there is no existence for other than Him except through Him; so what is other than Him is dependent on Him for its existence and the perfections that follow its existence. Just as there is no existence for the contingent except through Allah, so too there is no existential perfection except through Allah. Among the perfections of the servant is power; so he has no power except through Allah, as He said: "There is no power except through Allah" [Surah al-Kahf, verse 39]. And it is known that every attribute that something acquires from another is in reality for that other, not for the thing itself; so there is no real power except Allah's... until he said: 'When tawhid of the attributes becomes clear to you, you know that the effect of the servant's power by Allah's permission does not contradict restricting creatorship of everything to Allah; because the servant has no act except by power necessarily, and there is no power except through Allah by reason, transmission, and unveiling; so he has no act except through Allah, and what is through Allah is Allah, as was shown; so there is no act in reality except through Allah. Thus, the servant's acquisition (maksub) by the effect of his power with Allah's permission, not independently, is identical with the creation of Allah through the servant; so the creation by Allah through the servants and the acquisition by the servants through Allah are one in essence, different in considerations, because they emanate from a single power in essence that is multiple in considerations, which are the determinations occurring in the manifestations of the servants. So Allah is the Creator of absolutely everything while affirming acquisition (kasb) through effect, without needing to specify the general texts indicating that Allah is the Creator of everything by excluding the voluntary acts of the responsible agents, as chosen by the investigator Ibn al-Humann in al-Musayara where he said: ... and he summarized his statement until he said: 'You have known that there is no justification, in verification, for specifying the general texts.' Then he said: 'There is no need, in reconciling the affirmation of acquisition and the tawhid of acts, to interpret acquisition (kasb) as the mere relation of the servant's power to the intended act devoid of any effect at all, as is well-known from the Ash'aris; because it is possible to reconcile the statement that the servant's power has effect by Allah's permission not independently, with the statement of tawhid of acts, as has been shown and will become clearer with the success of the Most High Bestower.' And he supported it with transmitted reports and statements, and strengthened it with what he transmitted from al-Ash'ari in al-Ibana, and he elaborated at length.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is a quote from Ibrahim al-Kurani's treatise, arguing for a sophisticated tawhid of actions that simultaneously affirms human acquisition (kasb) as having real effect, but only by God's permission and not independently. He begins by establishing that only God has existence by essence; all else exists through Him and is dependent. Therefore, any perfection, including power, belongs to God alone. Human power is derivative. He then states that any attribute obtained from another is in reality that other's attribute, so true power is only God's. After an ellipsis, he argues that tawhid of attributes does not negate the servant's power having an effect by God's permission, because the servant cannot act without power, and all power is from God. The act is through God, and what is through God is in a sense God (i.e., a manifestation of His power). The creation and the acquisition are the same act considered from different perspectives: from God's side as creation, from the servant's side as acquisition. Thus, God is Creator of everything, including human acts, without needing to exclude voluntary acts from general statements about creation. He cites Ibn al-Humann and concludes that there is no need to interpret kasb as mere relation without effect; one can affirm both divine agency and human acquisition as effect by permission. He supports this with textual evidence from al-Ash'ari.

Key Terms
توحيد الأفعال
قدرة العبد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that humans possess power independently of God.
Correction: Al-Kurani shows that all power is derived from God; the servant has no power except through Allah.

Checkpoint
According to al-Kurani, what is the source of the servant's power?
A) An innate quality of the servant
B) Allah alone
C) A combination of Allah and the servant
D) The servant's own effort

Key Takeaway
All power and perfection belong solely to Allah; human power is derivative and exists only through Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You recite 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' often. But do you truly live as if your power to resist sin, to pray, to earn a living is not your own? What would change in your daily actions if you fully internalized that every strength you have is borrowed from Allah and actually belongs to Him?
?
Think of a recent moment when you felt proud of your own ability—a success, a skill, a moral victory. Can you, in that moment, genuinely attribute it to Allah alone? If not, what needs to shift in your heart so that your gratitude becomes as absolute as the truth that 'la quwwata illa billah'?
?
If every good quality you have is truly Allah's, then your sins are yours alone, but your virtues are His. How should this reshape your self-perception and your relationship with others? Will you start today to consciously redirect praise to Him when others compliment you?

Reconciling Divine Creation and Human Acquisition
Al-Kurani reconciles tawhid of acts with human acquisition as effect by permission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Kurani reconciles divine omnipotence with human acquisition (kasb) by affirming that the servant's power has effect by God's permission, without compromising tawhid of actions.

Core Idea
Creation and acquisition are one act seen from two perspectives.

Having established that all power belongs to God, al-Kurani now faces the question: how can human actions be genuinely ours? He argues that affirming the servant's power has a real effect—by God's permission and not independently—does not contradict the fact that God is the sole creator. In fact, creation and acquisition are identical in essence, differing only in how we consider them. This lesson explores his reconciliation and why he rejects the idea that kasb is merely a relation without effect.

Guided Path
1
Follow the argument that effect by permission is not contradiction
Read the passage starting from 'When tawhid of the attributes becomes clear to you...' Notice that al-Kurani insists that the servant's power having an effect does not negate Allah being the sole creator.
2
Understand the identity of creation and acquisition
He states that the creation by Allah through the servant and the servant's acquisition are 'one in essence, different in considerations'. Grasp this nuanced position.
3
See the rejection of the Ash'ari interpretation
Al-Kurani explicitly rejects the common Ash'ari view that kasb is merely the relation of power to act without effect. He affirms instead that the servant's power genuinely influences the act, but by God's permission.
4
Note the textual support
He supports his view with transmissions from Ibn al-Humann and al-Ash'ari himself, showing his position is grounded in the tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Checkpoint
According to al-Kurani, why is there no need to specify the general texts about Allah being Creator of everything?
A) Because voluntary acts are not really created by Allah

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now understand that every action you perform is both Allah's creation and your acquisition. Do you truly live with this awareness, or do you slip into thinking that your successes are your own doing and your failures are Allah's decree? What is one small action you can consciously perform today while affirming 'There is no power except through Allah'?
?
The passage says 'what is through Allah is Allah'. If you take that seriously, your entire life becomes a manifestation of the Divine. How would your attitude toward prayer, work, and even your mistakes change if you saw each moment as Allah acting through you? What fear or attachment would you need to surrender to make that shift?
?
Al-Kurani rejected a comfortable theological shortcut (the Ash'ari view that kasb has no effect) to affirm a heavier truth: you are truly responsible for your actions, yet utterly dependent on Allah. Are you willing to hold both truths without minimizing either? Which one do you tend to downplay, and what will you do today to live in the tension of both?

Charging Beyond Capacity: Distinctions and Dispute
Examination of taklif ma la yutaq with sectarian views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key positions on the issue of taklif ma la yutaq (charging beyond capacity), including the distinction between types of impossibility and the disagreement between Mu'tazila and Ash'ari on its permissibility.

Core Idea
God does not charge beyond capacity, but the debate is whether it is permissible in principle.

This passage addresses a deep theological question: can God command someone to do what is beyond their ability? The author first clarifies what is meant by 'beyond capacity' and notes universal agreement that God does not actually do so, citing Quranic evidence. Then, he presents the Mu'tazila-Ash'ari dispute on whether it would even be permissible. The argument and its critique are partially covered.

Guided Path
1
Understand the distinction
Notice how the author categorizes things impossible in themselves vs. things possible but rendered impossible by God's knowledge/will. This is crucial for the debate.
2
Identify the point of consensus
Look for the verse and the author's confirmation that God does not charge beyond capacity.
The verse is used for actual practice.
3
Recognize the dispute on permissibility
The Mu'tazila forbid based on rational evil; al-Ash'ari permits because nothing is evil for God. This is the core disagreement.
4
Examine the argument and its solution
The author presents a logical argument from the verse and then presents a solution that challenges it. Note that the solution is incomplete in this passage.
The argument shows the complexity of the issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يكلفهم الله تعالى إلا ما يطيقونه ولم يكلفهم بما ليس في وسعهم؛ سواء كان ممتنعا في نفسه كجمع الضدين أو ممكنا كخلق الجسم، وأما ما يمتنع بناء على أن الله تعالى علم خلافه أو أراد خلافه كإيمان الكافر وطاعة العاصي فلا نزاع في وقوع التكليف به لكونه مقدور المكلف بالنظر إلى نفسه. ثم عدم التكليف بما ليس في الوسع متفق عليه لقوله تعالى: (لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا) [سورة البقرة آية: ٢٨٦]، والأمر في قوله تعالى: (أَنْبِتُونِي بِأَسْمَاءِ هَؤُلَاءِ) [سورة البقرة آية: ٣١] للتعجيز لا للتكليف، وقوله تعالى حكاية عن حال المؤمنين: (رَبَّنَا وَلَا تُحَمِّلْنَا مَا لَا طَاقَةَ لَنَا بِهِ) [سورة البقرة آية: ٢٨٦] ليس المراد بالتحميل هو التكليف بل إيصال ما لا يطاق من العوارض إليهم. وإنها النزاع في الجواز؛ فمنعه المعتزلة بناء على القبح العقلي وجوزه الأشعري لأنه لا يقبح من الله تعالى شيء، وقد يستدل بقوله تعالى: لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا على نفي الجواز، وتقريره أنه لو كان جائزا لما لزم من فرض وقوعه محال؛ ضرورة أن استحالة اللازم توجب استحالة الملزوم، لكنه لو وقع لزم كذب كلام الله تعالى وهو محال، وهذه نكتة في بيان استحالة وقوع كل ما يتعلق علم الله تعالى وإرادته واختياره بعدم وقوعه. وحلها: أنا لا نسلم أن كل ما يكون ممكنا في نفسه لا يلزم من فرض وقوعه محال، وإنما يجب ذلك لو لم يعرض له الامتناع بالغير وإلا لجاز أن يكون لزوم المحال بناء على الامتناع بالغير؛ ألا يرى أن الله تعالى لما أوجد العالم بقدرته
And He did not obligate them except with what they can bear, and He did not obligate them with what is beyond their capacity; whether it is impossible in itself like combining two opposites, or possible like creating a body. As for what is impossible due to the fact that God knows otherwise or wills otherwise, like the faith of the disbeliever and the obedience of the sinner, there is no dispute about the occurrence of obligation with it because it is within the capacity of the obligated person in himself. Then, the absence of obligation with what is beyond capacity is agreed upon due to His statement: 'God does not charge a soul except with its capacity' [Surah al-Baqara, verse 286]; and the command in His statement: 'Inform Me of the names of these' [Surah al-Baqara, verse 31] is for incapacitation, not for obligation; and His statement, reporting about the believers: 'Our Lord, do not burden us with what we cannot bear' [Surah al-Baqara, verse 286]—what is meant by 'burden' is not obligation, but rather causing what cannot be borne of accidents to reach them. However, the dispute is concerning permissibility; the Mu'tazila forbade it based on rational evil, and al-Ash'ari permitted it because nothing is evil from God. And one may argue using His statement: 'God does not charge a soul except with its capacity' to negate permissibility. Its explanation is that if it were permissible, then assuming its occurrence would not necessitate a contradiction; necessarily, the impossibility of the consequent entails the impossibility of the antecedent. But if it occurred, it would necessitate the falsity of God's speech, which is impossible. And this is a subtle point in explaining the impossibility of the occurrence of everything that God's knowledge, will, and choice entail not occurring. Its solution is: we do not concede that every possible thing in itself does not, from assuming its occurrence, entail a contradiction. Rather, this is necessary only if it is not subject to impossibility from another; otherwise, it is possible that the entailment of contradiction is based on impossibility from another. Do you not see that when God brought the world into existence by His power...
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage discusses the theological issue of whether God can obligate a person beyond their capacity (taklif ma la yutaq). The author first clarifies that God does not actually obligate beyond capacity, distinguishing between two types of impossibility: inherent impossibility (e.g., combining opposites) and that which is possible in itself but rendered impossible by God's knowledge and will (e.g., a disbeliever's faith). There is consensus that God does not charge beyond capacity, as per the Quranic verse. However, the dispute concerns whether it is permissible (ja'iz) for God to do so. The Mu'tazila deny permissibility on the grounds of rational evil, while al-Ash'ari affirms it because nothing is evil for God. The author then presents an argument that uses the verse to negate permissibility: if it were permissible, assuming its occurrence would not entail a contradiction. But assuming its occurrence would entail that God's speech (the verse) is false, which is impossible. Therefore, it is impossible. However, the author notes a subtle point: this argument only works if the impossibility is inherent. The solution is that the impossibility may be due to an external factor (God's decree), so the argument does not prove inherent impossibility. The passage is cut off at the example of the world's creation.

Key Terms
التكليف بما لا يطاق
المعتزلة
الأشعري
القبح العقلي
الامتناع بالغير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The debate is about whether God actually charges beyond capacity.
Correction: The passage clarifies that there is consensus that God does not actually charge beyond capacity; the dispute is about whether it is permissible (ja'iz) for Him to do so.

Checkpoint
What is the basis on which the Mu'tazila forbid God from charging beyond capacity?
A) It contradicts the Quranic verse
B) Rational evil (qabah 'aqli)
C) It would lead to contradiction
D) It is impossible in itself

Key Takeaway
The debate on taklif ma la yutaq centers on permissibility, not actual occurrence, and involves a sophisticated logical argument about impossibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that a trial in your life was beyond your capacity to bear? How does the consensus that God does not actually charge beyond capacity (even if the debate is about permissibility) challenge or comfort you in that feeling? Commit to reciting verse 286 of Surah al-Baqara when you face such moments.
?
The Mu'tazila argued that charging beyond capacity is rationally evil, while the Ash'ari said nothing is evil from God. Which perspective makes you more accountable for your own actions? Does believing that God's commands are always within your capacity change how you respond to difficult obligations in your life? Decide today to stop using 'I can't' as an excuse for a command you know is from God.
?
The solution in the passage distinguishes between impossibility in itself and impossibility due to God's decree. When you fail to obey God, do you tend to blame your own weakness (inherent impossibility) or God's decree (external impossibility)? How can this distinction help you take responsibility and repent sincerely? Write down one specific sin you have rationalized as 'beyond your capacity' and ask God for forgiveness and strength.

God's Absolute Ownership and the Impossibility of Independence
Creedal statement and commentary affirming God's absolute ownership and the sin of claiming independence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why claiming even momentary independence from Allah constitutes disbelief, based on Quranic text and rational reasoning.

Core Idea
No one can be independent of Allah for even an instant.

This lesson unpacks a foundational creedal statement from Imam al-Tahawi: Allah owns everything and nothing owns Him, and no one can claim independence from Him for even the blink of an eye. The commentary provides both scriptural and rational proof, showing that independence is an attribute exclusive to Allah, while neediness defines the creature.

Guided Path
1
Read the creedal statement
Read the first sentence of the passage in Arabic and its translation. Notice the three negations: nothing owns Him, no independence from Him, and the severe consequence of claiming independence.
This is the matn of the Tahawiyyah.
2
Study the Quranic evidence
The commentary quotes Surah Fatir 35:15. Reflect on how this verse establishes that all humans are poor to Allah and only Allah is Self-Sufficient.
The verse is a direct proof for the second part of the statement.
3
Understand the rational argument
The commentary argues that independence is an attribute of lordship and neediness of servitude. Ask yourself: why would claiming independence be equivalent to claiming divinity?
This connects to the concept of tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَمْلُكُ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ وَلَا يَمْلِكُهُ شَيْءٌ، وَلَا يُسْتَغْنَى عَنِ اللَّهِ طَرْفَةَ عَيْنٍ؛ وَمَنِ اسْتَغْنَى عَنِ الله طَرْفَةَ عَيْنِ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ وَكَانَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْخُسْرَانِ. ويملك كل شيء ولا يملكه شيء، ولا يستغنى عن الله طرفة عين)؛ لقوله تعالى ( يَا النَّاسُ أَنتُمُ الْفُقَرَاء إِلَى اللهِ وَاللهُ هُوَ الْغَنِيُّ الْحَمِيدُ ) [سورة فاطر آية: (۱٥)، (ومن زعم أنه (استغنى عن الله تعالى (طرفة عين فقد كفر وكان من أهل الخسران لمصادمته نص القرآن، ولأن الاستغناء صفة الربوبية والافتقار صفة العبودية.
And He owns everything and nothing owns Him, and there is no independence from Allah for the blink of an eye; and whoever claims independence from Allah for the blink of an eye has disbelieved and becomes among the losers. And He owns everything and nothing owns Him, and there is no independence from Allah for the blink of an eye); by His saying the Most High: 'O mankind, you are the poor to Allah, and Allah is the Self-Sufficient, the Praiseworthy' [Surah Fatir, verse (15)], (and whoever claims that he is independent of Allah the Most High for the blink of an eye has disbelieved and becomes among the losers because he contradicts the text of the Quran, and because independence is an attribute of lordship and neediness is an attribute of servitude.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a creedal statement followed by a commentary. The creedal part (matn) from the Tahawiyyah declares that Allah owns everything and nothing owns Him, and that no one can be independent of Allah even for the blink of an eye. It then states that whoever claims such independence disbelieves and is among the losers. The commentary then repeats the creedal text and provides evidence: it quotes the Quranic verse 'O mankind, you are the poor to Allah, and Allah is the Self-Sufficient, the Praiseworthy' (Fatir 35:15). The commentary further argues that claiming independence contradicts the explicit Quranic text, and it gives a rational justification: independence (al-istighna') is an attribute of lordship (rububiyya), while neediness (al-iftiqar) is an attribute of servitude (ubudiyya). Therefore, anyone who attributes independence to themselves is claiming a divine attribute, which is disbelief.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'independence for a blink of an eye' refers only to a specific action, not a state of heart.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that any claim or feeling of self-sufficiency, even momentarily, constitutes disbelief, because it contradicts the essential relationship of creature to Creator.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on someone who claims to be independent of Allah for the blink of an eye?
A) He is sinful but remains a Muslim
B) He has disbelieved and becomes among the losers
C) He is only a hypocrite
D) He is excused because it is a minor sin

Key Takeaway
The creed affirms that absolute ownership belongs solely to Allah, and any claim to self-sufficiency—even momentarily—is a contradiction of tawhid and constitutes disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Reflect on a moment today when you acted—even inwardly—as if your success was entirely your own doing. Did that feeling of self-sufficiency not contradict the very words you just read: 'you are the poor to Allah'? How will you consciously redirect that feeling to Allah the next time it rises?
?
The lesson declares that claiming independence for a blink of an eye is disbelief. Now consider your own heart: when you worry about your future, your health, or your provision, where does that worry stem from? Is it not a subtle claim that you are the one responsible for these things? What concrete step will you take tonight to replace that worry with reliance on Allah?
?
If you truly believe that 'independence is an attribute of lordship and neediness an attribute of servitude,' then examine one habit you have—perhaps in your worship or daily choices—where you feel entitled to Allah's blessings. How does that entitlement violate the pure servitude He requires? Write down one change you will make starting tomorrow to correct that.
