Divine Attributes of Anger and Pleasure are Real but Unlike Creation
Affirms divine anger and pleasure as real attributes, rejects ta'wil, outlines Sunni methodology of tafwid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on divine attributes of anger and pleasure: they are real but not like human attributes, and why ta'wil is rejected in favor of affirming without modality.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are real but incomparable; we affirm them without asking how.

This passage from Imam Tahawi's creed deals with attributes like anger and pleasure. It affirms them as real attributes of Allah, but immediately clarifies that they are not like the attributes of any created being. The author then refutes the Mu'tazilite tendency to reinterpret these attributes, and explains the correct methodology of Ahl al-Sunna: affirm what is known from the text and stop at the modality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the flow: affirmation, then principle, then refutation.
Notice the verse citation at the end.
2
Identify the key affirmations
Find the sentences that affirm anger and pleasure as real, and the sentence that extends to all attributes.
3
Understand the basis for incomparability
The passage says Allah is unique in His attributes as in His essence. Note the verse 'Laysa kamithlihi shay'.
This is the foundational principle of tanzih.
4
Analyze the refutation of ta'wil
See how the passage explicitly rejects two types of ta'wil: reducing anger to will for revenge, or to its consequence.
This guards against the Mu'tazilite approach.
5
Grasp the Sunni methodology
The quotes from Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma explain the method: affirm the origin, stop at the modality, and do not busy with seeking how.
This is the path of the rāsikhūn fī al-‘ilm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى يَغْضَبُ وَيَرْضَى لَا كَأَحَدٍ مِنَ الوَرَى. وَنَقُولُ: إِنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى يَغْضَبُ وَيَرْضَى وَيُحِبُّ وَيَرْحَمُ وَكَذَلِكَ كُلُّ صِفَةٍ وَصَفَ بِهَا نَفْسَهُ أَوْ صَحَّ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِهَا وَصَفَهُ، وَلَكِنْ عَلَى الْمَعْنَى الَّذِي أَرَادَهُ، وَلَا يَصِحُّ أَنْ يُتَخَيَّلَ أَنَّهَا صِفَةٌ كَأَحَدٍ مِنْ صِفَاتِ الْوَرَى؛ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَالَى مُنْفَرِدٌ بِصِفَاتِهِ كَذَاتِهِ؛ فَكَمَا ذَاتُهُ لَا تُشْبِهُ الذَّوَاتَ فَصِفَاتُهُ لَا تُشْبِهُ الصِّفَاتَ لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ. وَلَا يُؤَوَّلَانِ بِأَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِبُغْضِهِ وَرِضَاهُ إِرَادَةَ الِانْتِقَامِ وَمَشِيئَةَ الْإِنْعَامِ أَوِ الْمُرَادُ بِهِمَا غَايَتَيْهِمَا مِنَ النِّقْمَةِ وَالنِّعْمَةِ؛ قَالَ فَخْرُ الْإِسْلَامِ: إِثْبَاتُ الْيَدِ وَالْوَجْهِ حَقٌّ عِنْدَنَا لَكِنَّهُ مَعْلُومٌ بِأَصْلِهِ مُتَشَابِهٌ بِوَصْفِهِ، وَلَا يَجُوزُ إِبْطَالُ الْأَصْلِ بِالْعَجْزِ عَنْ تَرْكِ الْوَصْفِ، وَإِنَّمَا ضَلَّتِ الْمُعْتَزِلَةُ مِنْ هَذَا الْوَجْهِ؛ فَإِنَّهُمْ رَدُّوا الْأُصُولَ لِجَهْلِهِمْ بِالصِّفَاتِ عَلَى وَجْهِ الْمَعْقُولِ فَصَارُوا مُعَطِّلَةً. كَذَا ذَكَرَهُ شَمْسُ الْأَئِمَّةِ. ثُمَّ قَالَ: وَأَهْلُ السُّنَّةِ وَالْجَمَاعَةِ أَثْبَتُوا مَا هُوَ الْأَصْلُ الْمَعْلُومُ بِالنَّصِّ أَيِ الْآيَاتِ الْقَطْعِيَّةِ وَالدَّلَالَاتِ الْيَقِينِيَّةِ وَتَوَقَّفُوا فِيمَا هُوَ الْمُتَشَابِهُ، وَهُوَ الْكَيْفِيَّةُ، وَلَمْ يُجَوِّزُوا الِاشْتِغَالَ بِطَلَبِ ذَلِكَ كَمَا وَصَفَ بِهِ الرَّاسِخِينَ فِي الْعِلْمِ فَقَالَ: يَقُولُونَ آمَنَّا بِهِ كُلٌّ مِنْ عِنْدِ رَبِّنَا (آل عمران ٧).
And indeed Allah the Exalted becomes angry and becomes pleased, not like any of mankind. And we say: Indeed Allah the Exalted becomes angry and becomes pleased and loves and shows mercy, and likewise every attribute with which He has described Himself or which it is authentic that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) described Him with, but upon the meaning that He intended. And it is not valid to imagine that they are attributes like any of the attributes of mankind, because He the Exalted is unique in His attributes like His essence; so just as His essence does not resemble essences, His attributes do not resemble attributes. There is nothing like unto Him, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing. And they are not interpreted [by ta'wil] that the intended meaning of His hatred and His pleasure is the will for revenge and the will for bestowing favors, or that the intended meaning of them is their consequences of punishment and blessing. Fakhr al-Islam said: 'Affirmation of the Hand and the Face is true with us, but it is known in its origin, ambiguous in its description, and it is not permissible to nullify the origin due to inability to leave the description. The Mu'tazila only went astray from this angle, for they rejected the origins due to their ignorance of the attributes in a rational way, so they became those who negate [the attributes].' Thus Shams al-A'imma mentioned it. Then he said: 'Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a affirmed what is the origin that is known by the text – that is the definitive verses and certain indications – and they stopped regarding what is ambiguous, and that is the modality (kayfiyya), and they did not permit occupying oneself with seeking that, as He described those firmly rooted in knowledge, saying: "They say: We believe in it; all is from our Lord." (Surah Al Imran 7).'
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage affirms the divine attributes of anger and pleasure as real but incomparable to human attributes. It begins by stating that Allah becomes angry and pleased, but not like any of mankind. Then it expands to all attributes that Allah described Himself with or the Prophet described Him with, but only with the meaning that Allah intended. It emphasizes that these attributes are not like human attributes because Allah is unique in His attributes as He is unique in His essence, citing the verse 'There is nothing like unto Him'. Then it refutes the Mu'tazilite interpretation (ta'wil) that would reduce anger and pleasure to mere will or consequence. It quotes Fakhr al-Islam (al-Bazdawi) who affirms attributes like Hand and Face as true in origin but ambiguous in modality, and condemns the Mu'tazila for rejecting the origins due to their ignorance. Finally, it quotes Shams al-A'imma (al-Sarakhsi) saying that Ahl al-Sunna affirm what is known by definitive texts and stop at the modality (kayfiyya), following the example of those firmly rooted in knowledge who say 'We believe in it; all is from our Lord.'

يرضى
صفات
تشبيه
تعطيل
تأويل
متشابه
كيفية
راسخون في العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming divine anger and pleasure means Allah has emotions like humans.
Correction: The passage affirms them as real but asserts that they are incomparable, not like human attributes, and that we must not imagine them as such.

Checkpoint
How does this passage respond to the Mu'tazilite interpretation of divine anger and pleasure?
A) It accepts the interpretation for rational consistency.
B) It rejects the interpretation and affirms the attributes as real without ta'wil.
C) It remains silent on the issue.
D) It equates anger to punishment and pleasure to reward.

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes of anger and pleasure are real but unlike creation; we affirm them without ta'wil or asking how.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah’s anger is real but unlike any human anger, does your heart tremble with fear of His displeasure as it would with a human? Or do you find yourself trying to minimize His anger by explaining it away as mere metaphor? Commit to reading the verse 'There is nothing like unto Him' (42:11) daily for a week and reflect on how it shapes your understanding of His attributes.
?
The Mu'tazila went astray because they prioritized their rational understanding over the texts. Where in your life do you find yourself doing the same – rationalizing a command or attribute of Allah because it doesn't fit your logic? Will you repent and submit to the text now, or will you continue to let your intellect judge His revelation?
?
The firmly rooted in knowledge say 'We believe in it; all is from our Lord.' Do you truly have that certainty, or do you secretly wish for a more 'reasonable' explanation? Make a sincere du'a tonight asking Allah to make you among those who accept without questioning the how, and then act on that acceptance by prostrating in gratitude.

Loving the Companions: Quranic and Hadith Evidence
Scriptural proof for the obligation to love the Companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that loving the Companions is a religious obligation firmly rooted in the Quran and Sunnah, and that harming them incurs severe consequences.

Core Idea
Love for the Companions is love for the Prophet, and hatred for them is hatred for him.

The author of Sharh al-Tahawiyyah now brings scriptural proof to show that our relationship with the Companions is not optional—it is a matter of faith. This passage gathers three powerful Quranic verses and a hadith that together establish the unique rank of the Sahaba and the obligation to love them.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Begin by reading the original Arabic text slowly. Notice the author's phrase 'something much has come'—he is emphasizing the abundance of evidence.
The passage is a collection of proof texts, so expect quotations.
2
Identify the three Quranic verses
Find each verse and note what specific quality of the Companions it highlights (e.g., their harshness against disbelievers, their humility, their emigration).
The verses are from Surah al-Fath, al-Ma'idah, and al-Hashr.
3
Understand the hadith's structure
The hadith from al-Tirmidhi builds a chain: love for Sahaba = love for Prophet, hatred = hatred for Prophet, harming = harming Allah, with a stern warning.
Notice the repetition of 'whoever' — it creates a logical escalation.
4
Reflect on the obligation
Ask yourself: how do these texts turn love for the Companions from a mere preference into a religious duty? What are the consequences of opposing them?
This connects to the lesson's objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ورد في الحث على حبهم من الآيات القرآنية والأحاديث النبوية شيء كثير كقوله تعالى: (مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللهِ وَالَّذِينَ مَعَهُ أَشِدَّاءُ عَلَى الْكُفَّارِ رُحَمَاءُ بَيْنَهُمْ تَرَاهُمْ رُكَّعًا سُجَّدًا يَبْتَغُونَ فَضْلًا مِّنَ اللَّهِ وَرِضْوَانًا .... إلى أجْرًا عظِيمًا) [سورة الفتح آية: 29]، وقوله تعالى: (فَسَوْفَ يَأْتِي اللَّهُ بِقَوْمٍ يُحِبُّهُمْ وَيُحِبُّونَهُ أَذِلَّةٍ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ أَعِزَّةٍ عَلَى الْكَافِرِينَ يُجَاهِدُونَ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ وَلَا يَخَافُونَ لَوْمَةَ لَائِمٍ ... الآية [سورة المائدة آية: 54]، وقوله: (لِلْفُقَرَاءِ الْمُهَاجِرِينَ ... إلى قوله: هُمُ الصَّادِقُونَ) [سورة الحشر آية: 8]، وإلى غير ذلك من الآيات، وروى الترمذي عن عبدالله بن مغفل قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الله اللهَ في أَصْحَابِي لَا تَتَّخِذُوهُمْ غَرَضًا بَعْدِي فَمَنْ أَحَبَّهُمْ فَبِحُبِّي أَحَبَّهُمْ وَمَنْ أَبْغَضَهُمْ فَبِبُغْضِي أَبْغَضَهُمْ وَمَنْ آذَاهُمْ فَقَدْ آذَانِي وَمَنْ آذَانِي فَقَدْ آذَى اللهَ وَمَنْ آذَى اللهَ يُوشِكُ أَنْ يَأْخُذَهُ»
And much has come urging love for them from the Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths, such as His saying, the Most High: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, and those with him are severe against the disbelievers, merciful among themselves. You see them bowing and prostrating, seeking bounty from Allah and [His] pleasure... to a great reward' [Surah al-Fath, verse 29], and His saying, the Most High: 'So Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him, humble toward the believers, stern toward the disbelievers, striving in the way of Allah and not fearing the blame of any blamer... the verse' [Surah al-Ma'idah, verse 54], and His saying: 'For the poor emigrants... to His saying: they are the truthful' [Surah al-Hashr, verse 8], and other such verses. And al-Tirmidhi narrated from 'Abdullah ibn Mughaffal that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Allah, Allah regarding my Companions! Do not take them as targets after me. Whoever loves them loves them out of love for me, and whoever hates them hates them out of hatred for me. Whoever harms them has harmed me, and whoever harms me has harmed Allah, and whoever harms Allah, He is about to seize him.'
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a scriptural evidence section where the author gathers Quranic verses and a hadith to establish the obligation of loving the Companions (Sahaba). The author begins by stating that there is abundant material on this topic. He then quotes three Quranic verses: Surah al-Fath 29 describes the Companions' characteristics and their reward; Surah al-Ma'idah 54 praises a people (understood as the Companions) whom Allah loves and who love Him; Surah al-Hashr 8 praises the Muhajirun specifically. The author then cites a hadith from al-Tirmidhi in which the Prophet commands reverence for his Companions, warns against taking them as targets of criticism, and declares that love for them is love for him and hatred for them is hatred for him, and harming them is harming Allah. The hadith emphasizes the severe consequence of opposing them. The passage establishes that love for the Sahaba is not merely recommended but is a matter of faith and loyalty to the Prophet.

Key Terms
الصحابة
حب الصحابة
الآيات القرآنية
الأحاديث النبوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think love for the Companions is merely a cultural preference or optional courtesy.
Correction: The provided verses and hadith show it is a religious obligation: the Prophet directly links love for them to love for himself, and hatred to hatred for him.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, what is the relationship between loving the Companions and loving the Prophet?
A) Loving them is optional but recommended
B) Loving them is a sign of loving the Prophet
C) Loving them is equivalent to loving Allah directly
D) Loving them has no connection to loving the Prophet

Key Takeaway
Loving the Companions is not optional; it is a commanded act of faith tied directly to love of the Prophet and fear of Allah's punishment for harming them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you genuinely feel love in your heart for every single Companion, including those you may disagree with? If there is any hesitation, are you willing to repent and ask Allah to purify your heart from resentment?
?
The Prophet said that loving the Companions is loving him. Does your daily speech and attitude reflect that love—or do you sometimes join in discussions that criticise or mock them?
?
Imagine your love for the Companions is put on the scale on the Day of Judgement. What specific action will you take today to increase that love and prove your loyalty to the Prophet?

God's Eternal Attributes and Names
Al-Tahawi enumerates divine attributes and argues they are eternal, not acquired by creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's attributes (such as Living, Creator, Provider) are eternal and not acquired through His act of creation.

Core Idea
God's attributes are eternal and not dependent on creation.

This lesson from the 'Aqidah al-Tahawiyyah affirms that God's attributes are inherent and pre-eternal. Al-Tahawi lists several divine attributes and then clarifies that God did not acquire new attributes when He created. The lesson establishes the transcendence of God beyond temporal change.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to grasp the overall meaning. Notice the list of attributes and the subsequent argument about their eternity.
The passage ends abruptly due to a page break; focus on the complete sentences available.
2
Identify the attributes listed
The passage begins with six attributes: Living (حي), Self-Subsisting (قيوم), Creator (خالق), Provider (رازق), He causes death (مميت), He resurrects (باعث). Note how each is paired with a negation or qualification.
These attributes are essential to God's nature.
3
Understand the argument for eternity
Al-Tahawi then states that God has always been with His attributes, pre-eternal before creation, and that He did not increase by creation. This means attributes are not acquired.
The key phrase: 'ليس منذ خلق الخلق استفاد اسم الخالق' – He did not become Creator only when He created.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this matters: if God's attributes were acquired, He would change, but God is changeless. This affirms divine transcendence and independence.
This refutes the idea that God becomes something new when He acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حَيٌّ لَا يَمُوتُ، قَيُّومٌ لَا يَنَامُ، خَالِقٌ بِلَا حَاجَةٍ، رَازِقٌ لَهُمْ بِلَا مُؤْنَةٍ، مُمِيتٌ بِلَا تَخَافَةٍ، بَاعِثٌ بِلَا مَشَقَّةٍ. مَا زَالَ بِصِفَاتِهِ قَدِيمًا قَبْلَ خَلْقِهِ، لَمْ يَزْدَدْ بِكَوْنِهِمْ شَيْئًا لَمْ يَكُنْ قَبْلَهُمْ مِنْ صِفَاتِهِ، وَكَمَا كَانَ بِصِفَاتِهِ أَزَلِيًّا كَذَلِكَ لَا يَزَالُ عَلَيْهَا أَبَدِيًّا. لَيْسَ مُنْذُ خَلَقَ الخَلْقَ اسْتَفَادَ اسْمَ الخَالِقِ، وَلَا بِإِحْدَاثِهِ البَرِيَّةَ اسْتَفَادَ اسْمَ البَارِي، لَهُ مَعْنَى الرُّبُوبِيَّةِ وَلَا مَرْبُوبَ، وَمَعْنَى الخَالِقِيَّةِ وَلَا مَخْلُوقَ، وَكَمَا أَنَّهُ يُحْيِي
Living, He does not die; Self-Subsisting, He does not sleep; Creator without need; Provider for them without difficulty; He causes death without fear; He resurrects without effort. He has always been with His attributes, pre-eternal before His creation; He did not increase by their coming into existence something that was not of His attributes before them; and just as He was with His attributes eternally, so shall He remain upon them forever. It is not that since He created creation He acquired the name 'Creator', nor by His bringing the creatures into existence did He acquire the name 'Maker'. He has the meaning of Lordship while there is no lord, and the meaning of Creatorship while there is no creation. And just as He gives life...
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage continues the creed by listing specific attributes of God and then arguing that these attributes are eternal, not acquired through creation. First, it affirms that God is Living (حي) without dying, Self-Subsisting (قيوم) without sleeping, Creator (خالق) without need, Provider (رازق) without difficulty, He causes death without fear, and He resurrects without effort. Then it makes the point that God's attributes are eternal: He has always been with His attributes, and He did not acquire any new attribute by creating. He was with His attributes in pre-eternity, and He will remain with them forever. The passage then emphasizes that God's names like Creator and Maker are not derived from the act of creation; rather, the meanings of Lordship (الربوبية) and Creatorship (الخالقية) are inherent in God even when there is no creation. The text ends with a comparison: just as He gives life..., but the OCR cuts off. The point is to establish that God's attributes are essential and not accidental.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God became 'Creator' only when He created, implying that His attribute of being Creator is not eternal.
Correction: The passage asserts that God did not acquire the name 'Creator' at creation; He has always had the meaning of Creatorship even when no creation existed.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when did God acquire the name 'Creator'?
A) When He created the universe
B) He always had it and did not acquire it
C) He will acquire it at the end of time
D) He acquired it before creation

Key Takeaway
God's attributes are eternal and not contingent upon creation; He has always been Living, Creator, Provider, etc., and did not acquire these names through His acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
God is 'Creator without need'. Think of one area in your life where you depend on something or someone to feel valuable or secure. How does the truth that God creates without any need confront your own sense of neediness? Will you today pray for the strength to detach your worth from created things and anchor it in the Eternal?
?
The passage states that God had the meaning of Lordship even when there was no one to rule over. Consider your leadership roles, whether at work, home, or community. Do you seek recognition from those you lead? How can you exercise authority with the same self-sufficiency and lack of need for validation that God embodies? What one step can you take this week to lead without expecting gratitude?
?
Al-Tahawi teaches that God did not acquire the name 'Creator' by creating. Your identity as a Muslim is not based on your actions—it is given by God. Are you living as if your worth comes from your deeds or from being a creation of the Eternal? Take a moment to ask God to give you the humility to see yourself as He sees you: a creature utterly dependent on the Creator who has no needs.

The Eternal Attributes of Allah: Pre-Eternity and Perfection
Affirmation of Allah's eternal attributes and their logical precedence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's attributes are eternal and that He did not acquire the name 'Creator' through creation.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are eternal; He was always the Creator, even before creation.

This passage from the Sharh Tahawiyyah affirms Allah's pre-eternity and everlastingness. It then clarifies a crucial point: Allah's attributes and names are not acquired through His actions; they are eternal just as He is eternal. This understanding safeguards against anthropomorphism and ensures true tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the rhythm and key affirmations.
Pay attention to the negations like 'without beginning' and 'without end'.
2
Identify the attributes mentioned
List the attributes (Living, Self-Subsisting, etc.) and notice how each is qualified (e.g., 'He does not die').
3
Grasp the argument about names
Focus on the lines about 'Creator' and 'Reviver' – how does the author prove that Allah deserved these names eternally?
The analogy with 'Reviver' before actual revival is key.
4
Reflect on the implication
Why does it matter that Allah's attributes are eternal? How does this protect tawhid?
It prevents thinking Allah changes or acquires new perfections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَدِيمٌ بِلَا ابْتِدَاءٍ دَائِمٌ بِلَا انْتِهَاءٍ، لَا يَفْنَى وَلَا يَبِيدُ، وَلَا يَكُونُ إِلَّا مَا يُرِيدُ. لَا تَبْلُغُهُ الْأَوْهَامُ وَلَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَفْهَامُ وَلَا تُشْبِهُهُ الْأَنَامُ. حَيٌّ لَا يَمُوتُ، قَيُّومٌ لَا يَنَامُ، خَالِقٌ بِلَا حَاجَةٍ، رَازِقٌ لَهُمْ بِلَا مُؤْنَةٍ، مُمِيتٌ بِلَا مَخَافَةٍ، بَاعِثٌ بِلَا مَشَقَّةٍ. مَا زَالَ بِصِفَاتِهِ قَدِيمًا قَبْلَ خَلْقِهِ، لَمْ يَزْدَدْ بِكَوْنِهِمْ شَيْئًا لَمْ يَكُنْ قَبْلَهُمْ مِنْ صِفَاتِهِ، وَكَمَا كَانَ بِصِفَاتِهِ أَزَلِيًّا كَذَلِكَ لَا يَزَالُ عَلَيْهَا أَبَدِيًّا. لَيْسَ مُنْذُ خَلَقَ الْخَلْقَ اسْتَفَادَ اسْمَ الْخَالِقِ، وَلَا بِإِحْدَاثِهِ الْبَرِيَّةَ اسْتَفَادَ اسْمَ الْبَارِئِ، لَهُ مَعْنَى الرُّبُوبِيَّةِ وَلَا مَرْبُوبَ وَمَعْنَى الْخَالِقِيَّةِ وَلَا مَخْلُوقَ، وَكَمَا أَنَّهُ مُحْيِي الْمَوْتَى بَعْدَمَا أَحْيَاهُمُ اسْتَحَقَّ هَذَا الِاسْمَ قَبْلَ إِحْيَائِهِمْ كَذَلِكَ اسْتَحَقَّ اسْمَ الْخَالِقِ قَبْلَ إِنْشَائِهِمْ: ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّهُ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ إِلَيْهِ فَقِيرٌ وَكُلُّ أَمْرٍ عَلَيْهِ يَسِيرٌ، لَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَى شَيْءٍ، لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ.
Pre-eternal without beginning, everlasting without end, He does not perish nor pass away, and nothing occurs except what He wills. Imaginations do not reach Him, understandings do not comprehend Him, and creatures do not resemble Him. Living, He does not die; Self-Subsisting, He does not sleep; Creator without need; Provider for them without effort; Causer of death without fear; Resurrector without difficulty. He has always been, with His attributes, pre-eternal before His creation; He did not increase by their coming into existence in anything that was not already His attribute; and just as He was with His attributes from eternity, so He will remain upon them forever. It is not that since He created the creation He acquired the name 'Creator', nor by His bringing forth the creatures did He acquire the name 'Originator'. He had the meaning of Lordship when there was no lorded-over, and the meaning of Creator when there was no created. And just as He is the Reviver of the dead after they have died—He deserved this name before reviving them—likewise He deserved the name 'Creator' before their origination. That is because He is over all things Powerful, all things are in need of Him, all affairs are easy for Him. He has no need of anything. There is nothing like Him, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of Allah’s eternal and perfect attributes. It first affirms His pre-eternity (qidam) and everlastingness (dawam), then negates human limitations: imaginations cannot reach Him, understandings cannot comprehend Him, and creatures do not resemble Him. It then enumerates attributes: Living, Self-Subsisting, Creator, Provider, Causer of death, Resurrector—all negating any need or fear. The key argument: His attributes are eternal; He did not acquire the name 'Creator' upon creating, just as He was 'Reviver of the dead' before actual revival. This is because His power is absolute, all things are needy, and nothing resembles Him. The passage concludes with a Qur'anic verse (42:11) confirming His transcendence.

صِفات
خالق
ربوبية
سميع بصير

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah became the Creator only when He created the universe.
Correction: The passage affirms that Allah has always been deserving of the name 'Creator', even before there was any creation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when did Allah deserve the name 'Creator'?
A) Only after He created the universe
B) From eternity, before creation
C) When He first willed to create
D) After He created the first creature

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes are eternal; He did not become the Creator through creation but was always the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe that Allah is eternally the Creator, but do your worries reflect a heart that trusts in a Creator who was always in control—even before your problems existed? What would change if you truly acted on that belief today?
?
The passage says Allah's attributes did not increase by creation. Are you secretly living as if your actions—your prayers, your sins, your good deeds—somehow add to or diminish His glory? How does this truth expose the pride in your heart?
?
If Allah was always the Creator even when there was no creation, what does that mean for the things you cling to—your health, your wealth, your relationships? Are you willing to let them go, knowing that He alone is eternal and everything else is a temporary gift?

The Qur'an as Allah's Uncreated Speech
Affirmation that the Qur'an is the uncreated speech of Allah, not resembling human speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Qur'an is the uncreated speech of Allah, originated without modality, and that claiming it is human speech constitutes disbelief.

Core Idea
The Qur'an is Allah's literal, uncreated speech, unlike any human word.

This passage from the Tahawiyyah affirms a core Sunni belief: the Qur'an is not created but is the very speech of Allah, sent down as revelation. The author warns that anyone who reduces it to human speech falls into disbelief, as Allah Himself has threatened such a person with Hell. Let's examine the text carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal translation. Notice the key phrases: 'بلا كيفية' (without modality) and 'غير مخلوق' (not created).
2
Identify the core affirmations
The passage affirms that the Qur'an is Allah's speech in reality, originated without modality, and sent down as revelation. It explicitly denies that it is created like human speech.
The term 'بلا كيفية' is crucial: we affirm the reality without asking how.
3
Understand the warning and proof
The author states that whoever claims the Qur'an is human speech has disbelieved, and cites Surah al-Muddaththir (74:25-26) as proof. Reflect on the severity of the threat: Allah will cast such a person into Saqar.
This shows the gravity of the issue.
4
Consider the general principle
The passage concludes that any description of Allah with human meanings leads to disbelief. This generalizes the rule: Allah's attributes are not like those of creation.
This is a reminder to practice tanzih (transcendence).
5
Reflect and take heed
The final phrase 'فمن أبصر هذا اعتبر' calls the reader to take heed. Ask yourself how this belief shapes your relationship with the Qur'an.
Consider the reverence due to Allah's speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنَّ الْقُرْآنَ كَلَامُ اللهِ تَعَالَى بَدَأَ بِلَا كَيْفِيَّةٍ قَوْلًا وَأَنْزَلَهُ عَلَى نَبِيِّهِ وَحْيًا وَصَدَّقَهُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ حَقًّا، وَأَيْقَنُوا أَنَّهُ كَلَامُ اللهِ تَعَالَى بِالْحَقِيقَةِ لَيْسَ بِمَخْلُوقٍ كَكَلَامِ الْبَرِيَّةِ؛ فَمَنْ سَمِعَهُ فَزَعَمَ أَنَّهُ كَلَامُ الْبَشَرِ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ، وَقَدْ ذَمَّهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى وَعَابَهُ وَأَوْعَدَهُ عَذَابَهُ حَيْثُ قَالَ: سَأُصْلِيهِ سَقَرَ [سورة المدثر آية: ٢٦] فَلَمَّا أَوْعَدَ اللهُ سَقَرَ لِمَنْ قَالَ إِنْ هَذَا إِلَّا قَوْلُ الْبَشَرِ [سورة المدثر آية: ٢٥] عَلِمْنَا أَنَّهُ قَوْلُ خَالِقِ الْبَشَرِ وَلَا يُشْبِهُ قَوْلَ الْبَشَرِ. مَنْ وَصَفَ اللهَ تَعَالَى بِمَعْنَى مِنْ مَعَانِي الْبَشَرِ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ؛ فَمَنْ أَبْصَرَ هَذَا اعْتَبَرَ.
And indeed the Qur'an is the speech of Allah the Exalted; He originated it without modality as speech, and sent it down upon His prophet as revelation. The believers affirm it as true regarding that, and are certain that it is the speech of Allah the Exalted in reality, not created like the speech of creatures. So whoever hears it and claims that it is human speech has disbelieved. Allah the Exalted has condemned him, criticized him, and threatened him with His punishment when He said: 'I will cast him into Saqar' (74:26). So when Allah threatened with Saqar the one who said: 'This is nothing but the word of a human' (74:25), we knew that it is the word of the Creator of humans, and it does not resemble the speech of humans. Whoever describes Allah the Exalted with a meaning from the meanings of humans has disbelieved. So whoever sees this should take heed.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is the classic Sunni affirmation that the Qur'an is the uncreated speech of Allah. It states: the Qur'an is Allah's speech; He originated it 'without modality' (bila kayfiyya), sent it down as revelation. Believers affirm it as true and know it is literally Allah's speech, not created like creature speech. Then it issues a severe warning: whoever claims it is human speech has committed kufr (disbelief). It cites Surah al-Muddaththir (74:25-26) as proof, where Allah threatens the one who called the Qur'an 'the word of a human' with Saqar (Hellfire). The conclusion: we know it is the word of the Creator of humans, incomparable to human speech. Finally, it generalizes: anyone who describes Allah with any human attribute has committed kufr, and whoever understands this should take heed.

Key Terms
كلام الله
غير مخلوق
بلا كيفية
كفر
سقر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'bila kayfiyya' means the Qur'an is not real speech but a metaphor or created meaning.
Correction: The passage explicitly says the Qur'an is 'speech of Allah in reality, not created'. 'Bila kayfiyya' affirms the reality while denying any modality we can comprehend.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence for one who claims the Qur'an is human speech?
A) He is a sinner but still a Muslim
B) He has disbelieved (kafara) and is threatened with Hell
C) He is merely mistaken and needs correction
D) He is a hypocrite but not a disbeliever

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an is the eternal, uncreated speech of Allah, and to claim otherwise is disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you truly believe you are hearing the uncreated speech of the Creator? Does that awareness change how you listen, or do you often read it as if it were just another text? What one habit must you change to treat it as kalam Allah?
?
The author warns that describing Allah with any human meaning leads to disbelief. In what subtle ways might you be imagining Allah with human-like qualities, even in your heart? Ask Allah to purify your understanding of His names and attributes.
?
Allah threatens with Saqar those who say the Qur'an is human speech. Yet many Muslims today neglect, mock, or selectively follow it. Where do you stand? If you claim it is divine, how must your relationship with the Qur'an change starting today?

Divine Attributes
beginner
5 min
Allah's Names Are Eternal, Not Dependent on Creation
Imam Tahawi argues Allah's names are eternal, not dependent on creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Allah's names and attributes are eternal and not contingent upon creation, based on Imam Tahawi's argument from analogy and divine attributes.

Core Idea
Allah's names are eternal; He was always the Creator even before creation.

This passage tackles a common theological question: Did Allah only become 'the Creator' when He created? Imam Tahawi uses a simple but powerful analogy involving the resurrection of the dead to show that Allah's names are not dependent on His actions. We'll walk through his reasoning and see how it ties to His absolute power and transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage aloud, then read the English translation. Notice the flow from analogy to reasoning to scriptural support.
The passage is dense; read it twice.
2
Identify the analogy
Imam Tahawi compares how Allah is called 'the One who gives life to the dead' even before actually giving life. This sets up the same for the name 'Creator' before creation.
The analogy shows that names are deserved based on what Allah is, not on when He acts.
3
Understand the reasoning
The passage gives three reasons: Allah's omnipotence, everything's need for Him, and the ease of all matters for Him. These show that His attributes are eternal and not acquired.
Notice the negation 'لا يحتاج إلى شيء' (He needs nothing) emphasizes His independence.
4
Connect to the Qur'anic verse
The verse 'ليس كمثله شيء وهو السميع البصير' affirms divine transcendence and two attributes. This reinforces that Allah is beyond comparison and still has perfect hearing and sight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المَوْتَى بَعْدَمَا أَحْيَاهُمْ اسْتَحَقَّ هَذَا الاسْمَ قَبْلَ إِحْيَائِهِمْ كَذَلِكَ اسْتَحَقَّ اسْمَ الخَالِقِ قَبْلَ إِنْشَائِهِمْ: ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّهُ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ إِلَيْهِ فَقِيرٌ وَكُلُّ أَمْرٍ عَلَيْهِ يَسِيرٌ، لَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَى شَيْءٍ، لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَىْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ (3) [سورة الشورى آية: ١١]
The dead after He gives them life deserved this name before their life. Likewise, He deserved the name 'Creator' before their creation. That is because He is over all things omnipotent, and everything is needy to Him, and every matter is easy upon Him. He needs nothing. There is nothing like Him, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing. (3) [Surah Ash-Shura, verse 11]
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument about Allah's names and attributes. Imam Tahawi begins with an analogy: just as Allah is called 'the One who gives life to the dead' even before actually giving life to them, similarly He is called 'the Creator' even before creating creation. This establishes that Allah's names and attributes are eternal and not dependent on the existence of creation. Then he explains the reason: because Allah is omnipotent (قدير over all things), everything is in need of Him (فقير إليه), and everything is easy for Him (عليه يسير). He then negates any need in Allah: لا يحتاج إلى شيء (He needs nothing). Finally, he affirms the verse of transcendence: ليس كمثله شيء (There is nothing like Him) and two attributes: السميع البصير (the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing). The citation of the Qur'anic verse supports this.

Key Terms
الخالق
القدير
السميع
البصير
الكيفية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Allah acquires names like 'Creator' only when He performs the act of creation.
Correction: Imam Tahawi shows that Allah deserved the name 'Creator' before creation because His power and attributes are eternal, not dependent on creation.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why did Allah deserve the name 'Creator' before creation?
A) Because creation was already known in His knowledge.
B) Because He is omnipotent and everything is easy for Him.
C) Because He needed the name to be known.
D) Because He created from pre-existing matter.

Key Takeaway
Allah deserved the name Creator before creation because His power and independence are eternal, and His attributes are not dependent on creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah's names are eternal and not dependent on your existence? How does that change the way you approach Him in worship, knowing that He was the Creator even before you were created?
?
If everything is in need of Allah and He needs nothing, what does that mean for your daily reliance on Him? Are there areas of your life where you act as if you are independent of His power?
?
The verse 'There is nothing like Him' demands that our conception of Allah be free from any similarity to creation. When you think of Allah's attributes, do you fall into the trap of imagining them in a human way? How will you guard your heart against that?

The Quran is Uncreated Speech of Allah
Tahawi affirms the Quran as Allah's uncreated speech and refutes the claim it is human speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah and the consequences of claiming it is human speech.

Core Idea
The Quran is Allah's speech in reality, not created like human speech.

This lesson from Imam Tahawi's creed definitively states the nature of the Quran as Allah's uncreated speech. It refutes those who say it is created or human speech, using a Quranic verse as proof. Understanding this distinction is essential for correct belief about Allah's attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own phrasing come through before you interpret.
Notice the strong affirmation 'وَإِنَّ القُرْآنَ كَلَامُ اللهِ تَعَالَى'.
2
Identify the key affirmation
The passage affirms that the Quran is Allah's speech, appearing 'without modality' (بلا كيفية). This means we believe it is speech but do not ask 'how'.
3
Understand the refutation
The passage warns that whoever claims the Quran is human speech has disbelieved. This is a severe warning.
The proof is from Surah Al-Muddaththir verse 26.
4
Reflect on the proof
Allah threatens with Saqar (Hell) those who say 'This is nothing but the speech of a human'. Therefore, the Quran is the speech of the Creator of humans.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنَّ القُرْآنَ كَلَامُ اللهِ تَعَالَى بَدَا بِلَا كَيْفِيَّةٍ قَوْلًا وَأَنْزَلَهُ عَلَى نَبِيِّهِ وَحْيًا وَصَدَّقَهُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ حَقًّا، وَأَيْقَنُوا أَنَّهُ كَلَامُ اللهِ تَعَالَى بِالحَقِيقَةِ لَيْسَ بِمَخْلُوقٍ كَكَلَامِ البَرِيَّةِ؛ فَمَنْ سَمِعَهُ فَزَعَمَ أَنَّهُ كَلَامُ البَشَرِ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ، وَقَدْ ذَمَّهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى وَعَابَهُ وَأَوْعَدَهُ عَذَابَهُ حَيْثُ قَالَ: سَأُصْلِيهِ سَقَرَ [سورة المدثر آية: ٢٦] فَلَمَّا أَوْعَدَ اللهُ سَقَرَ لِمَنْ قَالَ: إِنْ هَذَا إِلَّا قَوْلُ الْبَشَرِ [سورة المدثر آية: ٢٥] عَلِمْنَا أَنَّهُ قَوْلُ خَالِقِ البَشَرِ وَلَا يُشْبِهُ قَوْلَ البَشَرِ.
And indeed the Quran is the speech of Allah, Most High, appearing without modality as speech, and He sent it down to His prophet as revelation. And the believers affirm it as true, and they are certain that it is the speech of Allah in reality, not created like the speech of created beings. So whoever hears it and claims that it is the speech of humans has indeed disbelieved. And Allah has indeed condemned him, disparaged him, and threatened him with His punishment, where He said: 'I will burn him in Saqar' [Surah Al-Muddaththir, verse 26]. So when Allah threatened with Saqar the one who said: 'This is nothing but the speech of a human' [Surah Al-Muddaththir, verse 25], we know that it is the speech of the Creator of humans and does not resemble the speech of humans.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a definitive statement on the nature of the Quran: it is the uncreated speech of Allah. It begins by affirming that the Quran is the speech of Allah (كلام الله), described as 'بدا بلا كيفية قولا' (appearing without modality as speech), and that it was revealed to the Prophet as revelation (وحياً). The believers affirm it as true (صدقوه) and are certain that it is the speech of Allah in reality (بالحقيقة), not created like the speech of created beings (ليس بمخلوق ككلام البرية). Then it warns that anyone who claims the Quran is human speech has disbelieved (فقد كفر). It supports this by citing the verse where Allah threatens with Saqar (a name of Hell) those who say 'This is nothing but the speech of a human'. Therefore, we know the Quran is the speech of the Creator of humans and does not resemble human speech. This passage refutes the Mu'tazilite view that the Quran is created.

Key Terms
كلام الله
غير مخلوق
القرآن
الكيفية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran is created speech like human speech.
Correction: The Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah in reality, and believing it is created or human speech is disbelief.

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on someone who claims the Quran is human speech according to this passage?
A) They are mistaken but still Muslim.
B) They have disbelieved.
C) They are sinning but not disbelieving.
D) They are excused if ignorant.

Key Takeaway
The Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah, and believing otherwise is disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite or listen to the Quran, do you truly feel that you are hearing the uncreated speech of Allah, or do you treat it like an ordinary book? What would change if you lived in that reality every time you opened the Quran?
?
If someone you respect suggested that the Quran is a human composition, how would this passage call you to respond? Are you prepared to defend its divine origin with the same certainty the believers have?
?
The threat of Saqar is real for those who deny the Quran's divine speech. How does that truth affect your urgency to understand and live by the Quran? Are you using the Quran as a guide, or are you neglecting its authority?

Ru'ya is True Without How
Imam Tahawi affirms ru'ya and states its proper understanding.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the vision of Allah (ru'ya) is affirmed for the people of Paradise without modality or encompassing, and that its interpretation is known only to Allah.

Core Idea
Ru'ya is real but beyond our comprehension; we affirm it without asking how.

Imam Tahawi begins by stating a core belief of Ahl al-Sunna: the believers will see Allah in Paradise. But he immediately qualifies it—this seeing is without 'how' or 'encompassing'. The Quran itself affirms it, but we do not interpret it by our own reasoning. This passage sets the foundation for a proper approach to divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the rhythm and key terms.
2
Identify the affirmation and negations
Find where Imam Tahawi affirms ru'ya and what he negates (without ihata and without kayfiyya). Understand why these negations matter.
These negations protect tawhid by avoiding anthropomorphism.
3
Understand the Quranic proof
The verse from Surah al-Qiyama is the primary proof. Note that the passage says its tafsir is according to Allah's knowledge alone.
This sets the stage for the principle of taslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالرُّؤْيَةُ حَقٌّ لِأَهْلِ الْجَنَّةِ بِغَيْرِ إِحَاطَةٍ وَلَا كَيْفِيَّةٍ كَمَا نَطَقَ بِهِ كِتَابُ رَبِّنَا حَيْثُ قَالَ: {وُجُوهٌ يَوْمَئِذٍ نَاضِرَةٌ * إِلَى رَبِّهَا نَاظِرَةٌ} [سورة القيامة آية: ٢٢، ٢٣] وَتَفْسِيرُهُ عَلَى مَا أَرَادَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى وَعَلِمَهُ ، وَكُلُّ مَا جَاءَ فِي ذَلِكَ مِنَ الحَدِيثِ الصَّحِيحِ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَعَنْ أَصْحَابِهِ رُضْوَانُ اللَّه عَلَيْهِمْ أَجْمِينَ فَهُوَ كَمَا قَالَ، وَمَعْنَاهُ وَتَفْسِيرُهُ عَلَى مَا أَرَادَ لَا نَدْخُلُ فِي ذَلِكَ مُتَأَوَّلِينَ بِآرَائِنَا وَلَا مُتَوَفِّمِينَ بِأَهْوَائِنَا؛ فَإِنَّهُ مَا سَلِمَ فِي دِينِهِ إِلَّا مَنْ سَلَّمَ اللَّه تَعَالَى وَلِرَسُولِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَرَدَّ عِلْمَ مَا اشتبَه عَلَيْهِ إِلَى عَالِمِهِ. ولا يثبت قدَمُ الإسْلام إلا على ظهر التسليم والاستسلام؛ فَمَنْ رَامَ عِلْمَ مَا يَثْبُتُ حُظِرَ عَلَيْهِ وَلَمْ يَفْنَعْ بِالتَّسْلِيمِ فَهُمُهُ حَجَبَهُ مَرَامُهُ عَنْ خَالِصِ التَّوْحِيدِ وَصَافي المَعْرِفَةِ وَصَحِيحِ الإِيمَانِ فَيَتَذَبْذَبُ بَيْنَ الكُفْرِ وَالإِيمَانِ وَالتَّكْذِيبِ، وَالإِقْرَارِ وَالإِنْكَارِ ؛ مُوَسَوِسًا تَائِهَا زَائِعًا شَاكًا لَا مُؤْمِنًا مُصَدِّقًا وَلَا جَاحِدًا مُكَذِّبًا. وَلَا يَصِحُ الإِيمَانُ بِالرُّؤْيَةِ لِأَهْلِ دَارِ السَّلام مَنِ اعْتَبَرَهَا مِنْهُمْ بِوَهُم أَوْ تَأَوَّهَا بِفَهُم إِذَا كَانَ تَأْوِيلُ الرُّؤْيَةِ وَتَأْوِيلُ كُلِّ مَعْنَى يُضَافُ إِلَى الرُّبُوبِيَّةِ تَرْكَ التَّأْوِيلِ وَلُزُومَ التَّسْلِيمِ وَعَلَيْهِ دِينُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ وَشَرَائِعُ النَّبِيِّينَ.
And the vision (ar-ru'ya) is true for the people of Paradise, without encompassing (ihata) and without modality (kayfiyya), as the Book of our Lord spoke of it when He said: {Faces on that day are radiant, looking at their Lord} (Surah al-Qiyama, verses 22-23). And its interpretation (tafsir) is according to what Allah the Exalted intended and knew. And everything that has come in that regard from the authentic hadith from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and from his Companions, may Allah's good pleasure be upon them all, it is as he said, and its meaning and interpretation are according to what He intended. We do not enter into that by making ta'wil with our opinions nor by [؟] with our desires. For indeed, none is safe in his religion except one who submits to Allah the Exalted and to His Messenger, peace be upon him, and refers the knowledge of what is ambiguous to the One who knows it. The foot of Islam is not established except on the back of submission (taslim) and surrender (istislam). Whoever seeks knowledge of what is concealed from him, it is forbidden to him; despair [؟] does not benefit with submission [؟]. His aspiration veils him from pure tawhid, clear ma'rifa, and true iman, so he wavers between kufr and iman, between denial and affirmation, between acknowledgment and rejection, — obsessed, bewildered, straying, doubtful — neither a believing confirmer nor a denying rejecter. The belief in the vision for the people of the abode of peace is not valid for one who considers it [؟] with speculation or makes ta'wil of it with understanding [؟], since the ta'wil of the vision and the ta'wil of every meaning attributed to Lordship (rububiyya) is the abandonment of ta'wil and the adherence to submission. And upon this is the religion of the messengers and the laws of the prophets.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage defines and provides the rule for the belief in ru'ya (seeing Allah). It begins by affirming ru'ya as true for the people of Paradise, clarifying that it occurs without ihata (encompassing) or kayfiyya (modality). It cites the Quranic verse 'Faces on that day are radiant, looking at their Lord' as evidence. The commentary then outlines the methodological approach: the tafsir (interpretation) of such verses is known only to Allah, and authentic hadith on the topic are accepted as they are without engaging in ta'wil (rationalistic interpretation) based on personal opinion or desire. The passage warns that safety in religion lies only in submission (taslim) to Allah and His Messenger, and in referring ambiguous matters to Allah. It emphasizes that the foundation of Islam is complete submission. Those who seek knowledge of what is hidden from them are prevented from attaining pure tawhid and true iman, and they end up wavering between faith and disbelief. The correct belief in ru'ya is only valid when one avoids both speculation (wahm) and intellectualized ta'wil; indeed, the proper ta'wil of ru'ya and all divine attributes is to abandon ta'wil altogether and adhere to taslim. This, the passage concludes, is the religion of the prophets.

Key Terms
الرؤية
الإحاطة
الكيفية
التأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that ru'ya implies Allah is confined in a direction or that the seeing has a modality (kayfiyya) similar to human sight.
Correction: Imam Tahawi explicitly negates both encompassing and modality, affirming ru'ya without these limitations.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is the ru'ya (vision) of Allah described?
A) With encompassing and modality.
B) Without encompassing and without modality.
C) Only metaphorically, not literally.
D) As a vision that includes a specific direction.

Key Takeaway
The vision of Allah is true, but it is without 'how' or 'encompassing'; its interpretation belongs to Allah alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that seeing Allah is a real hope for you, or have you become comfortable with abstract theology that removes the intimacy of that promise? What would change in your daily life if you lived with that certainty?
?
When you think of standing before Allah, do you find yourself trying to imagine 'how'? What does this text say about that natural inclination, and are you willing to surrender that curiosity to Allah?
?
Are you content to leave the full meaning of ru'ya to Allah, or do you secretly wish to know more than He has revealed? What does your heart's attachment to 'figuring it out' reveal about your reliance on His wisdom?

The Principle of Taslim in Ambiguous Matters
Imam Tahawi instructs on the methodology of taslim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principle of taslim (submission) regarding ambiguous texts and the danger of engaging in ta'wil based on personal opinion.

Core Idea
True safety in religion lies in complete submission, not in rational interpretation of divine matters.

Having affirmed ru'ya, Imam Tahawi now teaches the methodology that protects one's faith. He warns against making ta'wil (interpretive speculation) based on personal opinion or desire. Instead, the foundation of Islam is submission (taslim). Those who insist on understanding hidden matters end up in confusion and doubt. This lesson explains why the correct 'ta'wil' of the attributes is to refrain from ta'wil altogether.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the warnings and the metaphor about the foot of Islam.
2
Identify the key principle: taslim
Find the sentence about safety in religion and the establishment of Islam. Notice that submission (taslim) is the foundation.
Taslim means surrendering the meaning to Allah.
3
Understand the consequence of rejecting taslim
The passage describes those who seek to know what is hidden: they waver between faith and disbelief. Identify the list of negative states.
This shows the gravity of engaging in ta'wil.
4
Learn the final definition of ta'wil
The passage concludes that the proper ta'wil of ru'ya and all divine attributes is to abandon ta'wil and adhere to taslim. This is the way of the prophets.
This resolves the apparent paradox: ta'wil becomes the act of not doing ta'wil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالرُّؤْيَةُ حَقٌّ لِأَهْلِ الْجَنَّةِ بِغَيْرِ إِحَاطَةٍ وَلَا كَيْفِيَّةٍ كَمَا نَطَقَ بِهِ كِتَابُ رَبِّنَا حَيْثُ قَالَ: {وُجُوهٌ يَوْمَئِذٍ نَاضِرَةٌ * إِلَى رَبِّهَا نَاظِرَةٌ} [سورة القيامة آية: ٢٢، ٢٣] وَتَفْسِيرُهُ عَلَى مَا أَرَادَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى وَعَلِمَهُ ، وَكُلُّ مَا جَاءَ فِي ذَلِكَ مِنَ الحَدِيثِ الصَّحِيحِ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَعَنْ أَصْحَابِهِ رُضْوَانُ اللَّه عَلَيْهِمْ أَجْمِينَ فَهُوَ كَمَا قَالَ، وَمَعْنَاهُ وَتَفْسِيرُهُ عَلَى مَا أَرَادَ لَا نَدْخُلُ فِي ذَلِكَ مُتَأَوَّلِينَ بِآرَائِنَا وَلَا مُتَوَفِّمِينَ بِأَهْوَائِنَا؛ فَإِنَّهُ مَا سَلِمَ فِي دِينِهِ إِلَّا مَنْ سَلَّمَ اللَّه تَعَالَى وَلِرَسُولِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَرَدَّ عِلْمَ مَا اشتبَه عَلَيْهِ إِلَى عَالِمِهِ. ولا يثبت قدَمُ الإسْلام إلا على ظهر التسليم والاستسلام؛ فَمَنْ رَامَ عِلْمَ مَا يَثْبُتُ حُظِرَ عَلَيْهِ وَلَمْ يَفْنَعْ بِالتَّسْلِيمِ فَهُمُهُ حَجَبَهُ مَرَامُهُ عَنْ خَالِصِ التَّوْحِيدِ وَصَافي المَعْرِفَةِ وَصَحِيحِ الإِيمَانِ فَيَتَذَبْذَبُ بَيْنَ الكُفْرِ وَالإِيمَانِ وَالتَّكْذِيبِ، وَالإِقْرَارِ وَالإِنْكَارِ ؛ مُوَسَوِسًا تَائِهَا زَائِعًا شَاكًا لَا مُؤْمِنًا مُصَدِّقًا وَلَا جَاحِدًا مُكَذِّبًا. وَلَا يَصِحُ الإِيمَانُ بِالرُّؤْيَةِ لِأَهْلِ دَارِ السَّلام مَنِ اعْتَبَرَهَا مِنْهُمْ بِوَهُم أَوْ تَأَوَّهَا بِفَهُم إِذَا كَانَ تَأْوِيلُ الرُّؤْيَةِ وَتَأْوِيلُ كُلِّ مَعْنَى يُضَافُ إِلَى الرُّبُوبِيَّةِ تَرْكَ التَّأْوِيلِ وَلُزُومَ التَّسْلِيمِ وَعَلَيْهِ دِينُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ وَشَرَائِعُ النَّبِيِّينَ.
And the vision (ar-ru'ya) is true for the people of Paradise, without encompassing (ihata) and without modality (kayfiyya), as the Book of our Lord spoke of it when He said: {Faces on that day are radiant, looking at their Lord} (Surah al-Qiyama, verses 22-23). And its interpretation (tafsir) is according to what Allah the Exalted intended and knew. And everything that has come in that regard from the authentic hadith from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and from his Companions, may Allah's good pleasure be upon them all, it is as he said, and its meaning and interpretation are according to what He intended. We do not enter into that by making ta'wil with our opinions nor by [؟] with our desires. The foot of Islam is not established except on the back of submission (taslim) and surrender (istislam). Whoever seeks knowledge of what is concealed from him, it is forbidden to him; despair [؟] does not benefit with submission [؟]. His aspiration veils him from pure tawhid, clear ma'rifa, and true iman, so he wavers between kufr and iman, between denial and affirmation, between acknowledgment and rejection, — obsessed, bewildered, straying, doubtful — neither a believing confirmer nor a denying rejecter. The belief in the vision for the people of the abode of peace is not valid for one who considers it [؟] with speculation or makes ta'wil of it with understanding [؟], since the ta'wil of the vision and the ta'wil of every meaning attributed to Lordship (rububiyya) is the abandonment of ta'wil and the adherence to submission. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that ta'wil (rational interpretation) is required to make sense of ambiguous texts about Allah's attributes.
Correction: The passage states that the correct ta'wil is to abandon ta'wil and adhere to taslim (submission).

Checkpoint

B) To abandon ta'wil and adhere to submission.
C) To seek consensus among scholars.
D) To understand them through personal reflection.

Key Takeaway
The proper approach to divine attributes is taslim—submission without speculative interpretation.

Divine Will and Decree
Imam Tahawi affirms divine will, decree, and justice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that everything occurs by Allah's will, knowledge, decree, and predestination, and that His will is supreme and He is never unjust.

Core Idea
Allah's will dominates all, and He is never unjust.

Imam Tahawi begins by affirming the absolute sovereignty of Allah over all events. Everything happens by His will, knowledge, decree, and predestination. His will overpowers all other wills, and His decree overcomes all human schemes. This passage establishes the foundation of divine predestination and justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the key affirmations about divine will and decree.
2
Identify the five elements
Notice that everything runs by Allah's will, knowledge, decree, and predestination. Then see the consequences: His will overpowers, decree overpowers, He does as He wills, He is never unjust.
3
Reflect on 'He is not questioned'
Consider the implication of the Quranic principle: Allah is not accountable to anyone, but we are accountable to Him.
This emphasizes His absolute sovereignty.

Source Text

وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ يَجْرِي بِمَشِيئَةِ اللهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ وَعِلْمِهِ وَقَضَائِهِ وَقَدَرِهِ، غَلَبَتْ مَشِيئَتُهُ المَشِيئَاتِ كُلَّهَا وَغَلَبَ قَضَاؤُهُ الحِيَلَ كُلَّهَا، يَفْعَلُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَهُوَ غَيْرُ ظَالِمٍ أَبَدًا، تَقَدَّسَ عَنْ كُلِّ سُوءٍ وَتَنَزَّهَ عَنْ كُلِّ عَيْبٍ وَشَيْنٍ، لَا يُسْأَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ وَهُمْ يُسْأَلُونَ. وَفِي دُعَاءِ الأَحْيَاءِ لِلْأَمْوَاتِ وَصَدَقَتِهِمْ مَنْفَعَةٌ لِلْأَمْوَاتِ، وَاللهُ تَعَالَى يَسْتَجِيبُ الدَّعَوَاتِ وَيَقْضِي الحَاجَاتِ، وَيَمْلِكُ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ وَلَا يَمْلِكُهُ شَيْءٌ، وَلَا يُسْتَغْنَى عَنِ اللهِ طَرْفَةَ عَيْنٍ، وَمَنِ اسْتَغْنَى عَنِ اللهِ طَرْفَةَ عَيْنٍ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ وَكَانَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الخَسْرَانِ، وَإِنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى يَغْضَبُ وَيَرْضَى لَا كَأَحَدٍ مِنَ الوَرَى.
And everything runs by the will of Allah Azza wa Jalla, His knowledge, His decree, and His predestination. His will overpowers all wills, and His decree overpowers all stratagems. He does what He wills, and He is never unjust. He is sanctified from every evil and exalted from every defect and blemish. He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned. And in the supplication of the living for the dead and their charity, there is benefit for the dead. And Allah Ta'ala answers supplications and fulfills needs. He owns everything, and nothing owns Him. And no one is independent of Allah even for a blink of an eye. Commentary
This passage covers several key divine attributes and practices. It begins by affirming that everything occurs by Allah's will, knowledge, decree, and predestination. His will dominates all other wills, and His decree overwhelms all human schemes. He does whatever He wills, but He is never unjust; He is free from all evil and imperfection. The verse 'He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned' (Quran 21:23) is cited to emphasize His absolute sovereignty. Next, the passage affirms that supplications and charity offered by the living for the deceased benefit them. Allah answers prayers and fulfills needs, as He owns everything and nothing owns Him. No one is independent of Allah even for a moment; to claim such independence is disbelief. Finally, it affirms that Allah becomes angry and is pleased, but these attributes are not like those of created beings—they are befitting His majesty.

Imam Tahawi concludes this segment by affirming two divine attributes: anger and pleasure. He emphasizes that these attributes are not similar to human emotions. This is a key point in preserving divine transcendence while affirming the attributes mentioned in the Quran and Sunnah.

The Supremacy of Allah's Will and Decree
Affirmation of comprehensive divine decree and its supremacy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that everything happens by Allah's will, knowledge, decree, and predestination, and that no creature's will or plan can override His.

Core Idea
Allah's will overcomes all wills; His decree overcomes all schemes.

This passage lays the foundation for the Islamic doctrine of divine decree (qadar). It begins by affirming that every event, without exception, occurs by Allah's will, knowledge, decree, and predestination. Then it emphasizes the absolute supremacy of His will over all other wills and His decree over all human schemes, reminding us that nothing can thwart what Allah has ordained.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the full Arabic passage once without focusing on analysis. Let the rhythm and emphasis of the original come through. Then read the translation.
Notice the repetition of 'كل' (all) to stress comprehensiveness.
2
Identify the four aspects of divine control
The passage lists four things: will, knowledge, decree, and predestination. Find each term and note how they are linked to 'كل شيء' (everything).
These four are distinct but interconnected aspects of Allah's control over creation.
3
Focus on the two 'overcomes' statements
The passage says His will overcomes all wills, and His decree overcomes all schemes. Reflect on what this means for human free will and planning.
This does not negate human responsibility but establishes ultimate divine sovereignty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ يَجْرِي بِمَشِيئَةِ اللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ وَعِلْمِهِ وَقَضَائِهِ وَقَدْرِهِ، غَلَبَتْ مَشِيئَتُهُ المَشِيئَاتِ كُلَّهَا وَغَلَبَ قَضَاؤُهُ الحِيَلَ كُلَّهَا، يَفْعَلُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَهُوَ غَيْرُ ظَالِمٍ أَبَدًا، تَقَدَّسَ عَنْ كُلِّ سُوءٍ وَتَنَزَّهَ عَنْ كُلِّ عَيْبٍ وَشَيْنٍ لَا يُسْأَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ وَهُمْ يُسْأَلُونَ ﴾ [سورة الأنبياء آية: ٢٣].
And everything occurs by the will (mashi'ah) of Allah, His knowledge, His decree (qada'), and His predestination (qadr). His will overcomes all wills, and His decree overcomes all schemes. He does what He wills, and He is never unjust. Exalted is He above every evil, and free is He from every flaw and blemish. He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned (Quran 21:23).
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage affirms the comprehensive divine decree. Everything occurs by Allah's will, knowledge, decree (qada'), and predestination (qadr). His will dominates all other wills, showing that no creature's will can override His. Similarly, His decree overcomes all schemes (hiyal), meaning nothing can thwart what He has ordained. He does as He wills, but He is never unjust (zalim). Then comes a declaration of God's transcendence: He is exalted above all evil and free from every flaw and blemish. The verse from Quran 21:23 is cited: 'He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned.' This establishes God's absolute sovereignty: He answers to no one, but all creation is accountable to Him.

Key Terms
مشيئة
قضاء
قدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that human free will completely negates divine decree, making Allah's control limited.
Correction: This passage shows that while humans have will and schemes, Allah's will and decree are supreme and overcome all—they do not negate human responsibility but establish ultimate divine sovereignty.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what does Allah's will overcome?
A) All obstacles
B) All wills
C) All knowledge
D) All deeds

Key Takeaway
Everything, without exception, occurs by Allah's will, knowledge, decree, and predestination, and His will and decree are absolutely supreme.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that everything occurs by Allah's will and decree. Think of a recent disappointment or setback in your life. Can you truly say, from your heart, that it was from Allah? If not, what is stopping you from surrendering to His decree?
?
If Allah's will overcomes all wills, then your most carefully laid plans are subject to His permission. When you plan tomorrow, do you actually live with that reality? What would change if you did?
?
Your schemes cannot escape Allah's decree. Is there a situation where you are trying to 'outsmart' Allah's plan through your own efforts? What would it look like to submit to His decree instead of resisting it?

Allah's Justice and Sovereignty
Affirmation of divine justice, transcendence, and sovereignty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's absolute will does not contradict His justice, and that He alone is sovereign over creation.

Core Idea
Allah does as He wills, is never unjust, and answers to no one.

After establishing the supremacy of divine decree, the passage turns to Allah's own nature. It affirms that He does whatever He wills yet is never unjust. It declares His transcendence above all evil and imperfection, and concludes with a powerful Quranic verse that establishes His absolute sovereignty: He is not questioned about what He does, but all others are. This lesson explores how divine will and justice coexist.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read the Arabic from 'يَفْعَلُ مَا يَشَاءُ' to the end. Notice the shift from describing what Allah does to describing His attributes.
The verse at the end is from Surah Al-Anbiya 21:23.
2
Identify the key affirmations
The passage makes three affirmations: 1) He does what He wills, 2) He is never unjust, 3) He is transcendent above evil and flaws. Find each in the text.
These affirmations protect against misunderstanding God's actions.
3
Analyze the Quranic verse
The verse says: 'He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned.' Reflect on what this teaches about God's sovereignty and human accountability.
This is a key verse in discussions of divine justice (adl).

وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ يَجْرِي بِمَشِيئَةِ اللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ وَعِلْمِهِ وَقَضَائِهِ وَقَدْرِهِ، غَلَبَتْ مَشِيئَتُهُ المَشِيئَاتِ كُلَّهَا وَغَلَبَ قَضَاؤُهُ الحِيَلَ كُلَّهَا، يَفْعَلُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَهُوَ غَيْرُ ظَالِمٍ أَبَدًا، تَقَدَّسَ عَنْ كُلِّ سُوءٍ وَتَنَزَّهَ عَنْ كُلِّ عَيْبٍ وَشَيْنٍ لَا يُسْأَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ وَهُمْ يُسْأَلُونَ ﴾ [سورة الأنبياء آية: ٢٣].
And everything occurs by the will (mashi'ah) of Allah, His knowledge, His decree (qada'), and His predestination (qadr). His will overcomes all wills, and His decree overcomes all schemes. He does what He wills, and He is never unjust. Exalted is He above every evil, and free is He from every flaw and blemish. He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned (Quran 21:23).
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage affirms the comprehensive divine decree. Everything occurs by Allah's will, knowledge, decree (qada'), and predestination (qadr). His will dominates all other wills, showing that no creature's will can override His. Similarly, His decree overcomes all schemes (hiyal), meaning nothing can thwart what He has ordained. He does as He wills, but He is never unjust (zalim). Then comes a declaration of God's transcendence: He is exalted above all evil and free from every flaw and blemish. The verse from Quran 21:23 is cited: 'He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned.' This establishes God's absolute sovereignty: He answers to no one, but all creation is accountable to Him.

Key Terms
ظالم
سوء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because Allah does what He wills, He could be unjust or arbitrary.
Correction: This passage directly refutes that by stating that He is never unjust, and emphasizes His transcendence above all evil. His sovereignty is always exercised with perfect justice and wisdom.

Checkpoint
What does the Quranic verse (21:23) say about being questioned?
A) Allah is questioned by angels
B) Allah is not questioned, but others are
C) Both Allah and humans are questioned
D) No one is questioned

Key Takeaway
Allah does as He wills but is never unjust; He is transcendent above all evil, and He alone is sovereign over all creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation that feels deeply unfair, do you truly trust that Allah is never unjust (غير ظالم أبدًا) in that moment? What specific trial makes you waver, and how does this passage demand you to repent of questioning His justice?
?
Have you ever secretly harbored resentment toward Allah for something He decreed? Read the verse 'He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned' (Quran 21:23). How does this truth expose the arrogance of your heart, and what change in attitude must you make today?
?
If you truly believed that Allah is free from every flaw and blemish, would you still complain about His decisions? Pause and think: what does your complaining reveal about your view of Allah's perfection? Write down one complaint you must now surrender.
